1802 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


State v. Velasquez


CASE NO. 3D02-2756


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, THIRD DISTRICT


879 So. 2d 1259; 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 11736; 29 Fla. L. Weekly D 1824



August 11, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication August 27, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court for Miami-Dade County, Dennis Murphy, Judge. LOWER TRIBUNAL NO. 02-13294.
State v. Velasquez, 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 9177 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 3d Dist., June 30, 2004)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed an order from the Circuit Court for Miami-Dade County (Florida), which reduced a charge against defendant for trafficking in cannabis in violation of Fla. Stat. ch. 893.135(1)(a) (2002) to a charge of possession of cannabis. Defendant filed a motion for rehearing.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested and charged with trafficking in cannabis in violation of Fla. Stat. ch. 893.135(1)(a) (2002) after officers recovered 55 cannabis plants, weighing 30 pounds total. Defendant moved to dismiss, arguing that 300 plants were needed to sustain a trafficking charge. The trial court granted defendant's motion and allowed him to plead guilty to a possession count. The State appealed. Defendant filed a motion for rehearing of the court's reversal of that order. He challenged for the first time whether the court had jurisdiction to review an order reducing a criminal charge. The court noted that on prior cases, it had ruled that it did have jurisdiction. The court adhered to its prior determination that the statutory definition of cannabis under Fla. Stat. ch. 893.02(3) (2001) did not distinguish between processed and unprocessed cannabis. Therefore, 25 pounds of cannabis, which was the statutory minimum for a trafficking offense, was 25 pounds of cannabis either in processed or unprocessed form. The court held that since defendant had 30 pounds of cannabis, albeit in unprocessed form, the trial court erred in reducing the trafficking charge to a possession charge.


OUTCOME: The court granted defendant's motion for rehearing, withdrew its previous order, and entered a new opinion which, nevertheless, reversed the order reducing the charges against defendant.

 

1803 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Wilson v. County of Orange


Case No. 5D03-4065


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


881 So. 2d 625; 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 11655; 29 Fla. L. Weekly D 1800



August 6, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication October 6, 2004.
Later proceeding at Wilson v. County of Orange, 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 15018 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 5th Dist., Sept. 17, 2004)
Review denied by Orange County v. Wilson, 895 So. 2d 406, 2005 Fla. LEXIS 299 (Fla., Feb. 4, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Orange County, Janet C. Thorpe, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED and REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owners sought review of the dismissal of their complaint with prejudice by the Circuit Court for Orange County (Florida). The property owners argued that the trial court erred in dismissing the 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 claim as well as the remaining counts for declaratory relief. The property owners had challenged the facial constitutionality of certain statutes and ordinances dealing with code violation procedures.


OVERVIEW: The property owners began evicting a tenant for unpaid rent from their trailer park. A county code inspector, whom they had seen coming and going from the same tenant's trailer, told the property owners that if they moved forward with the eviction, he would "cause them many problems." Immediately thereafter, the property owners were cited for code violations. A code inspector filed affidavits of noncompliance. Relying solely on that affidavit of noncompliance and without conducting any further hearing, the code enforcement board imposed fines on the property owners. The appellate court concluded that the property owners' allegations sufficiently alleged a cause of action under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. The allegations were sufficient to invoke the trial court's jurisdiction to determine the constitutionality of the challenged statutes and ordinances. The property owners' facial constitutional challenges could not be barred by failure to exhaust administrative remedies. The evidence of a code violation and failure to cure the violation in the first action was not essential to the second action. Thus, the actions were not the same and res judicata did not apply.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed and the matter was remanded for further proceedings.

Almenares v. State


Case No. 5D04-730


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 10994; 29 Fla. L. Weekly D 1698



July 23, 2004, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:

 [*1] NOT FINAL UNTIL TIME EXPIRES TO FILE REHEARING MOTION AND, IF FILED, DISPOSED OF.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing granted by, Opinion withdrawn by, Substituted opinion at, Remanded by Almenares v. State, 882 So. 2d 493, 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 13750 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 5th Dist., Sept. 17, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: 3.800 Appeal from the Circuit Court for Osceola County, Thomas W. Turner, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED and REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the decision of the Circuit Court for Osceola County (Florida), which summarily denied his Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.800(a) motion.


OVERVIEW: In his motion, defendant challenged the three-year mandatory minimum sentence which was imposed on his conspiracy to traffic in cocaine conviction pursuant to the sentencing enhancements set forth in 1999 Fla. Laws ch. 188, arguing that the sentence was illegal because 1999 Fla. Laws ch. 188 had been held unconstitutional. The appellate court concluded that, in denying defendant's Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.800 motion, the trial court relied upon a decision from which the appellate court had since receded. Thus, defendant's sentence was illegal and he was entitled to have it corrected. The State argued that Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.800 relief was not warranted because defendant could not demonstrate any prejudice resulting to him from the imposition of a three-year mandatory minimum sentence where he had to serve 85 percent of his 48 month sentence pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 944.275(4)(b)3 (2001). However, even though the mandatory minimum term of imprisonment would have no impact on the length of defendant's incarceration, the trial court was nevertheless required to strike the mandatory minimum term from defendant's sentencing documents.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the trial court's denial of defendant's motion and remanded the matter to the trial court with directions to strike the mandatory minimum term from his sentence. The appellate court certified a conflict with another case.

 

1806 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Delgado v. State


Case No. 2D03-3044


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


884 So. 2d 142; 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 10573; 29 Fla. L. Weekly D 1650



July 16, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review dismissed by Delgado v. State, 892 So. 2d 1011, 2004 Fla. LEXIS 2437 (Fla., Dec. 21, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Hillsborough County; Rex Martin Barbas, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with directions; conflict certified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court for Hillsborough County (Florida), which convicted him of trafficking in cocaine and imposed the mandatory minimum sentence, pursuant to 1999 Fla. Laws ch. 188.


OVERVIEW: Chapter 188 provided for mandatory minimum sentences for certain drug offenses. For a certain period of time, ch. 188 was an unconstitutional violation of the single-subject rule of the Florida Constitution. In 2002, the Florida Legislature reenacted the substantive provisions of ch. 188 and cured the single-subject violation. The Legislature also purported to make the new law retroactive to the date of the 1999 statute. However, the court found the retroactive reach of 2002 Fla. Laws ch. 212 in violation of the Ex Post Facto Clauses of the U.S. and Florida Constitutions. Thus, 1999 Fla. Laws ch. 188 was void, and 2002 Fla. Laws ch. 212 applied prospective only from the date of its enactment. The State conceded that the date of defendant's offense fell within the window for asserting challenges to the minimum mandatory sentence and agreed that defendant's sentence was illegal. The court ruled that those persons committing offenses between July 1, 1999, and April 29, 2002, should be sentenced under the 1997 Florida Statutes. Accordingly, the court ordered that defendant should be resentenced under Fla. Stat. ch. 893.135(1)(b)(1)(a).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction. The court reversed defendant's sentence and remanded the cause for resentencing.

 

1807 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Martin v. State


CASE NOS. 4D01-631 & 4D02-4291


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


876 So. 2d 1256; 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 9928; 29 Fla. L. Weekly D 1604



July 7, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 23, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: Consolidated appeals from the Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County; Stephen A. Rapp, Judge; L.T. Case No. 97-5327 CFA02.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED and REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pleaded guilty to five counts of the attempted murder of a law enforcement officer with a firearm and to discharging a machine gun. After defendant's sentence was corrected twice, an agreed order was entered by the Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County (Florida), which imposed a sentence of five concurrent 39-year sentences and an eight-year mandatory minimum. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court incorrectly scored all five attempted murder convictions as primary offenses. The appellate court held that any scoresheet error was not harmless, as the most recent sentencing order imposed a guidelines sentence. Defendant was a Heggs defendant and was sentenced under the 1994 Florida Sentencing Guidelines. Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.702 applied, as it was specific to the 1994 Guidelines. Under Rule 3.703(d)(3), only one offense could be scored as the primary offense. Even if the "one offense" language was construed to include multiple counts, the language was at least ambiguous and under the rule of lenity, it was construed most favorably to the accused. The grid and the Commission Note relied on in cases decided under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.701 to find that multiple counts should be scored as primary offenses were inapplicable to Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.702 cases. Further, the form associated with Rule 3.702 did not show a calculation method for additional counts of a primary offense and had only one blank for the primary offense. Only one of defendant's attempted murder counts should have been scored as a primary offense.


OUTCOME: The sentencing order was reversed on the multiple conviction ground and the case was remanded. The order was affirmed on all other issues.

 

1808 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Bailey v. State


CASE NO. 4D04-1085


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


877 So. 2d 836; 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 9940; 29 Fla. L. Weekly D 1595



July 7, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 23, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal of order denying rule 3.800(a) motion from the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County; Stanton S. Kaplan, Judge; L.T. Case No. 95-5659 CF10.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his conviction from the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County (Florida) denying his motion to correct illegal sentence, filed pursuant to Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.800(a). His plea colloquy established that he understood that he could be habitualized and he was sentenced on each count as a habitual violent felony offender with a mandatory minimum.


OVERVIEW: In three counts, defendant was charged with attempted first degree murder with a firearm, a life felony, and attempted robbery with a firearm. The State agreed to omit the firearm so that he could receive an enhanced sentence for that count as a habitual felony offender. He entered no contest pleas and the colloquy established that he knew that he could be habitualized. He was sentenced on each of the two counts to 25 years' imprisonment as a habitual violent felony offender with a 15-year mandatory minimum. A firearm mandatory minimum was imposed only with respect to the second count. On appeal, the court rejected his contention that his first count was reduced from a life felony because he possessed a handgun instead of a firearm, holding that the two were synonymous as a matter of law. As for his sentence, the court held that he had pleaded to a first degree felony, and his habitualized sentence was not improper. As for his 15-year mandatory minimum for count two, because attempted robbery with a firearm was a second degree felony, he was subject only to a mandatory minimum 10-year sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.

1810 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


State v. Rose


Case Nos. 2D03-3943, 2D03-4480, 2D03-4510, CONSOLIDATED


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


876 So. 2d 1240; 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 9172; 29 Fla. L. Weekly D 1548



June 30, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 23, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Polk County; Susan W. Roberts, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Polk County (Florida) dismissed informations filed against defendants charging them with violating Fla. Stat. ch. 812.155(3) (2001), for failing to return leased property valued at $ 300 or more to the lessor with the intent to defraud. The State appealed the judgment.


OVERVIEW: The trial court found that Fla. Stat. ch. 812.155(3) (2001) unconstitutional because it created a special law, which was prohibited by Fla. Const. art. III, § 11(a). A special law was one relating to, or designed to operate upon, particular persons or things, or one that purported to operate upon classified persons or things when classification was not permissible or the classification adopted was illegal. A general law operated universally throughout the state, or uniformly upon subjects as they might exist throughout the state. The appellate court held that the statute was not a prohibited special law, as it did not operate only upon particular persons or things, nor did it operate only in a specially indicated part of the state. Rather, Fla. Stat. ch. 812.155(3) (2001) operated on all those persons who failed to return leased property under the circumstances specified in the statute. The appellate court held that Fla. Stat. ch. 812.155(3) (2001) was not a constitutionally prohibited special law.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and remanded.

 

1811 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


State v. Velasquez


CASE NO. 3D02-2756


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, THIRD DISTRICT


2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 9177; 29 Fla. L. Weekly D 1539



June 30, 2004, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:

 [*1] THIS OPINION WAS WITHDRAWN BY THE COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Opinion withdrawn by, Substituted opinion at, On rehearing at State v. Velasquez, 879 So. 2d 1259, 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 11736 (Fla. 3d DCA, Aug. 11, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court for Miami-Dade County, Dennis Murphy, Judge. LOWER TRIBUNAL NO. 02-13294.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Miami-Dade County (Florida) reduced a charge of trafficking in cannabis to a charge of possession of cannabis. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: The State challenged the judgment entered. In response, defendant argued that the phrase "in excess of 25 pounds of cannabis" referred only to processed cannabis and that unprocessed cannabis plants, though weighing more than 25 pounds, did not meet the statute's requirements for trafficking unless they reach 300 in number. The appeals court disagreed. The statutory definition of cannabis did not distinguish between processed and unprocessed cannabis. Therefore, 25 pounds of cannabis was 25 pounds of cannabis, whether it was in processed or unprocessed form. Since defendant had 30 pounds of cannabis, albeit in unprocessed form, the trial court erred in reducing the trafficking charge to a possession charge. Defendant's alternative argument that Fla. Stat. ch. 893.135(1)(a) was unconstitutional failed, as 2002 Fla. Laws 212, and not 1999 Fla. Laws 188 governed.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded.

 

1812 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Martin Mem'l Med. Ctr., Inc. v. Tenet Healthsystem Hosps., Inc.


CASE NO. 1D03-4567


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


875 So. 2d 797; 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 8984; 29 Fla. L. Weekly D 1533



June 29, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 15, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from the circuit court for Leon County. P. Kevin Davey, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant hospitals appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court for Leon County (Florida), which declared 2003 Fla. Laws ch. 289 unconstitutional as a special or local law which had not been adopted in compliance with Fla. Const. art. III, § 10, and permanently enjoined the Florida Agency for Health Care Administration (AHCA) from issuing any exemptions pursuant to that law.


OVERVIEW: 2003 Fla. Laws ch. 289 authorized the AHCA to issue hospitals in Palm Beach, Polk, Martin, St. Lucie and Indian River Counties exemptions from certificate of need review for the establishment of open-heart-surgery programs when the applications for exemption complied with certain criteria. On appeal, appellees, hospitals and other healthcare-related entities, argued that, because the Attorney General of Florida had elected not to participate in the appeal in any capacity, Fla. Stat. ch. 86.091 (2003) required dismissal of the appeal. The appellate court concluded that appellants were entitled to prosecute the appeal. The Attorney General participated in the litigation at the trial level, as counsel for the AHCA, and he was aware of the appeal. Thus, the requirements of Fla. Stat. ch. 86.091 had been met, and the presence of the Attorney General was not required in the appeal. In addition, the trial court correctly held 2003 Fla. Laws ch. 289 unconstitutional as a special or local law which had not been adopted in compliance with Fla. Const. art. III, § 10. The law created a closed class limited to five counties.


OUTCOME: Appellees' motion to dismiss the appeal was denied. The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

1813 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Waits v. State


CASE NO. 5D04-617


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


877 So. 2d 784; 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 8933; 29 Fla. L. Weekly D 1527



June 25, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 14, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: 3.800 Appeal from the Circuit Court for Osceola County, Margaret T. Waller, Judge.
State v. Waits, 848 So. 2d 1030, 2003 Fla. LEXIS 174 (Fla., 2003)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed without prejudice.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the decision of the Circuit Court for Osceola County (Florida), which summarily denied his motion to correct sentence filed pursuant to Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.800(a).


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant argued that his classification as a prison releasee reoffender (PRR) was improper because 1999 Fla. Laws ch. 188, amending the PRR statute, effective July 1, 1999, was found to be unconstitutional due to its violation of the single subject requirement of the Florida Constitution. Defendant alleged that he committed his offense during the period between the unconstitutional enactment of the amended statute and the legislature's reenactment of the changes curing the constitutional infirmity. The appellate court could not determine from the limited record before it whether defendant was adversely affected by the unconstitutional amendments to the PRR statute. 1999 Fla. Laws ch. 188 did not create the PRR statute. It simply made some changes to a preexisting PRR statute. If defendant qualified as a prison releasee reoffender under the prior statute, he was not adversely affected by the unconstitutional revision and would not be entitled to relief. The Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.800(a) motion filed by defendant did not demonstrate that his sentence was illegal on its face.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's denial of defendant's motion but without prejudice to his filing an amended motion demonstrating that he was adversely affected by the relevant law.

Scanes v. State


CASE NO. 4D04-1324


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


876 So. 2d 1238; 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 8738; 29 Fla. L. Weekly D 1496



June 23, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
Rehearing denied by Scanes v. State, 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 12074 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., Aug. 4, 2004)
Review denied by Scanes v. State, 892 So. 2d 1014, 2004 Fla. LEXIS 2431 (Fla., Dec. 21, 2004)
Later proceeding at Scanes v. State, 895 So. 2d 428, 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 1788 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., Feb. 9, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal of order denying rule 3.800(a) motion from the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County; Marc H. Gold, Judge; L.T. Case No. 94-000206CF10A.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following a jury trial, defendant was declared a habitual felony offender and sentenced concurrently to 30 years in prison on two second-degree felonies. Defendant appealed the order of the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County (Florida), which summarily denied his motion to correct an illegal sentence filed pursuant to Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.800(a).


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant argued that his 30-year sentences exceeded the appropriate statutory maximum for second-degree felonies because the trial court did not orally sentence him "as" a habitual felony offender. Specifically, the trial court held him to be a habitual felony offender and concurrently sentenced him to the enhanced sentence, but did not state that the 30-year sentences were imposed on defendant "as" a habitual felony offender. The appellate court concluded that it was clear from the plea colloquy, the written habitual felony offender finding, and the written sentence, that the trial court intended to, and did, contemporaneously sentence defendant as a habitual felony offender.


OUTCOME: The order of the trial court was affirmed.

Smith v. State


CASE NO. 3D04-46


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, THIRD DISTRICT


876 So. 2d 682; 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 10183; 29 Fla. L. Weekly D 1484



June 23, 2004, Opinion filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 9, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal under Florida Rule of Appellate Procedure 9.141(b) (2) from the Circuit Court for Miami-Dade County, Henry Leyte-Vidal, Judge. LOWER TRIBUNAL NO. 83-713.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court, Miami-Dade County (Florida), which denied his motion to correct illegal sentence. Defendant was convicted on two counts of robbery with a pistol, burglary without a firearm, and two counts of kidnapping with a pistol, and was sentenced to concurrent 10-year terms for robbery and burglary convictions, and to life for the kidnapping convictions, to be served consecutive to the first robbery count.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the guidelines under which he was sentenced for robbery and burglary, under Fla. Stat. § 921.001 (1983), were later declared unconstitutional until subsequently enacted by the legislature. The State properly conceded that, for that reason, defendant should be re-sentenced on those counts. On appeal, the court held that the trial court improperly denied defendant's motion, under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.800, on the robbery and burglary counts and remanded for resentencing either to non-guideline, parole-eligible sentences, or, if defendant elected, to sentences under the version of the sentencing statutes in effect at the time that defendant made an effective election. Defendant had the right to be present at re-sentencing and to be represented by counsel.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court in part as to the sentences on two counts of robbery and one count of burglary and remanded the cause for re-sentencing on those convictions. The court affirmed the sentence on the kidnapping convictions.

Newell v. State


Case No. 2D03-2111


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


875 So. 2d 747; 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 8354; 29 Fla. L. Weekly D 1429



June 16, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 7, 2004.
Review denied by Newell v. State, 917 So. 2d 194, 2005 Fla. LEXIS 2470 (Fla., Nov. 18, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Pasco County; Wayne L. Cobb, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Pasco County (Florida) convicted defendant of failing to comply with the sexual offender registration requirements contained in Fla. Stat. ch. 943.0435 (2000). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged his conviction and sentence, contending that Fla. Stat. ch. 943.0435 violated procedural and substantive due process requirements. The appeals court disagreed. Procedural due process challenges had previously been rejected by the instant court and other district courts of appeal. Concerning substantive due process, defendant argued that ch. 943.0435 improperly lacked any requirement of guilty knowledge, scienter, or mens rea. However, the Florida Supreme Court rejected this argument, and held that ch. 943.0435 had to be construed as including a knowledge requirement. Finally, defendant's remaining arguments lacked merit.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Rodgers v. State (In re Rogers)


Case No. 2D01-1106


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


875 So. 2d 737; 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 8319; 29 Fla. L. Weekly D 1419



June 11, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 2, 2004.
Review denied by Rodgers v. State, 906 So. 2d 1059, 2005 Fla. LEXIS 1416 (Fla., 2005)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Rodgers v. Fla., 126 S. Ct. 570, 163 L. Ed. 2d 478, 2005 U.S. LEXIS 8012 (U.S., Oct. 31, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Polk County; Cecelia M. Moore and J. Michael Hunter, Judges.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed; question certified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the decision of the Circuit Court for Polk County (Florida), which entered an order finding him to be a sexually violent predator and committed him to a secure facility pursuant to the Jimmy Ryce Act, Fla. Stat. ch. 394, pt. V (2000).


OVERVIEW: Appellant raised numerous issues on appeal. Affirming the circuit court's decision, the court held, inter alia, that (1) the trial court did not err in allowing the testimony of a psychologist who employed three actuarial instruments in determining appellant's likelihood of recidivism; (2) appellant failed to state an equal protection claim based on his contention that he was forced to testify against himself because he did not demonstrate that he was similarly situated to defendants in other types of civil proceedings; (3) the trial court did not abuse its discretion in allowing the admission of hearsay evidence, and appellant's constitutional challenge to Fla. Stat. ch. 394.9155(5) (1999) had no merit; and (4) appellant failed to show that the Department of Family and Children Service's failure to promulgate rules under the Act, as required by Fla. Stat. ch. 394.930 (2000), violated equal protection principles. The court also certified the following question to the state supreme court: May an individual be committed under the Act in the absence of a jury instruction that the State must prove that the individual has serious difficulty in controlling his or her dangerous behavior?


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's decision, but it certified a question of great public importance to the state supreme court.

Dep't of Revenue v. Swago T-Shirts, Inc.


CASE NO. 4D02-2852


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


877 So. 2d 761; 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 8199; 29 Fla. L. Weekly D 1402



June 9, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication August 11, 2004.
Rehearing denied by Dept of Revenue v. Swago T-Shirts, 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 12572 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., Aug. 11, 2004)
Review denied by State Dep't of Revenue v. Swago T-Shirts, Inc., 889 So. 2d 71, 2004 Fla. LEXIS 2131 (Fla., 2004)
Subsequent appeal at Swago T-Shirts, Inc. v. Fla. Dep't of Revenue, 929 So. 2d 597, 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 6619 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., May 3, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County; Thomas M. Lynch, IV, Judge; L.T. Case No. 98-20501 (11).



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Florida Department of Revenue challenged a judgment from the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit in Broward County (Florida), which granted a motion for summary judgment by appellee company and which abated sales and use taxes assessed against the company.


OVERVIEW: The company challenged a tax assessed against it based on a lack of a tax exemption for failing to be a registered dealer. At the same time, it filed a motion for the court to approve an alternative security arrangement under Fla. Stat. ch. 72.011 (1995) wherein the company would pay the amount of the assessment it did not dispute. That arrangement was approved, the company filed a motion for summary judgment in its favor, which was granted, and the Department appealed. The Department claimed the trial court did not have subject matter jurisdiction because the company failed to satisfy the statutory jurisdiction requirements of paying the entire taxes due or else obtaining the Department's approval for the alternative security arrangement. The court found that the statute allowed the trial court to approve the alternative security arrangement regardless of approval by the Department. Therefore, the jurisdictional requirements were satisfied. Moreover, since the evidence showed that the company was a registered dealer, was designated as such on the Department's own records, and no proof that the registration was cancelled existed, the summary judgment decision was proper.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment in the company's favor.

I.B. v. Dep't of Children & Families


CASE NO. 5D03-2480


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


876 So. 2d 581; 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 7930; 29 Fla. L. Weekly D 1356



June 4, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication June 23, 2004.
Later proceeding at Dep't of Children & Family Servs. v. I.B., 891 So. 2d 1168, 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 803 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., Jan. 31, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Volusia County, Shawn L. Briese, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant foster parents sought review of the order from the Circuit Court for Volusia County (Florida), which dismissed their petition to adopt a child, removed the child from their home, and placed him with the child's relatives, who were approved by appellee Department of Children and Families to adopt the child, in Tennessee.


OVERVIEW: A few days after his birth, the child was taken into the Department's custody. Both the child and his mother had tested positive for cocaine. A few months later, the Department placed the child with the foster parents. At the same time, the Department contacted the mother's cousin, who lived in Tennessee. She and her husband were interested in adopting the child. Three months later the guardian ad litem reported that the child was being well-cared for and loved by his foster parents, who were planning to adopt him. The guardian also reported that she had met with the cousin and her husband and that they also seemed to be loving and caring people. The Department selected the relatives as the adoptive parents. The foster parents appealed, and the trial court ruled that they did not have standing to appeal and that it did not have authority to interfere with the Department's selection of the adoptive parents. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded, finding that the foster parents had standing to appeal under Fla. R. Civ. P. 1.230 and that the trial court should have conducted a hearing to consider whether the change in placement was in the child's best interests.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order and remanded to the trial court to hold a hearing to determine whether the change in placement was in the child's best interests. The child was to remain in its current placement pending any decision by the trial court.

 

1820 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


State v. Andrews


CASE NO. 4D02-4451


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


875 So. 2d 686; 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 7736; 29 Fla. L. Weekly D 1328



June 2, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication June 18, 2004.
Review denied by Andrews v. State, 891 So. 2d 549, 2004 Fla. LEXIS 2369 (Fla., Dec. 9, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal and cross-appeal from the Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County; Hubert R. Lindsey, Judge; L.T. Case No. 00-765CFA02.
State v. Andrews, 820 So. 2d 1016, 2002 Fla. App. LEXIS 9440 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., 2002)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed an order from the Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit in Palm Beach County (Florida), which granted a downward departure from the sentence imposed on defendant for the crime of aggravated assault on a law enforcement officer. Defendant cross-appealed his conviction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was originally convicted for attempted second degree murder of a law enforcement officer. A new trial was granted. Defendant was then convicted for aggravated assault on an officer. The State requested at least the mandatory minimum sentence under Fla. Stat. ch. 784.07(2)(c) (1999), but the trial court downwardly departed by sentencing defendant to time served. Both parties appealed. The court found the departure was authorized at the time by case law holding that ch. 784.07(2)(c) was unconstitutional. But, subsequent case law upheld the statute and defendant had to be resentenced to the mandatory minimum. Defendant argued the State had to file an amended information prior to the new trial. The court held that an amended information was not required since defendant was tried on a lesser included offense and the last information alleged all the elements of aggravated assault. The court also rejected defendant's argument that marijuana found in his car should have been excluded under the Williams rule as overly prejudicial. The evidence was a conceivable motive for defendant's attempt to evade officers and a limiting instruction was delivered.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for aggravated assault on a law enforcement officer. The court reversed defendant's sentence and remanded for resentencing and the imposition of the mandatory minimum sentence required by statute, with appropriate credits for time served.

1822 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


State v. Cyphers


Case No. 2D03-1272


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


873 So. 2d 471; 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 6574; 29 Fla. L. Weekly D 1136



May 12, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication June 3, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Sarasota County; Harry M. Rapkin, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed two orders by the Circuit Court for Sarasota County (Florida) which granted defendants' motions to dismiss on the grounds that the statutory scheme they were charged under was unconstitutionally vague. Defendants were charged with keeping a gambling house, contrary to Fla. Stat. ch. 849.01 (2003), and possession of coin-operated devices (slot machines), contrary to Fla. Stat. ch. 849.15 (2003).


OVERVIEW: Defendants operated an arcade amusement center with at least 50 amusement games, which they believed to be permissible under the Fla. Stat. ch. 849.161 (2003) arcade amusement center exception to Fla. Stat. ch. 849. The player inserted cash into the machine and depressed a button, whereby a series of rotating icons began to spin. The player then depressed the button to stop the spinning icons, attempting to line up the icons in certain combinations. A certain number of credits could be exchanged for gift certificates redeemable at various businesses. Some businesses redeemed the gift certificates for merchandise and cash. While skill affected the outcome, there was also an element of chance. The appellate court held defendants' conduct was clearly not protected under Fla. Stat. ch. 849.161(1)(a)(1). Thus, defendants could not sustain a void for vagueness claim, and the court did not reach defendants' argument that Fla. Stat. ch. 849.161(1)(a)(1) was vague when read in conjunction with Fla. Stat. ch. 849.15. Defendants' machines were not coin operated, as required by Fla. Stat. ch. 849.161(1)(a)(1) since they did not accept quarters and were operated by cash bills.


OUTCOME: The orders of the trial court were reversed and the matter was remanded for further proceedings.

Oregrund Ltd. P'ship v. Sheive


CASE NO. 5D03-2408


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


873 So. 2d 451; 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 6429; 29 Fla. L. Weekly D 1111



May 7, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected June 1, 2004. Released for Publication June 16, 2004.
Rehearing denied by Oregrund Ltd. v. Sheive, 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 8717 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 5th Dist., May 28, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Osceola County, Jeffords D. Miller, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED and REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, property owners, filed suit against defendants, investors, on multiple grounds, all of which, save one, were based on violation of Florida's usury statutes. The Circuit Court for Osceola County (Florida) dismissed all of the counts set forth in the third amended complaint, with prejudice. The property owners appealed the judgment.


OVERVIEW: The property owners wanted to borrow approximately $ 600,000 to be used in a business venture. The investors executed an agreement which created a land trust, in which they invested money in return for proportional interests. The terms of an option to repurchase stated that if the owners exercised their right to repurchase in the first year following the sale, the repurchase price was to be $ 1.2 million, and if they exercised the option in the second year following the sale, the price would be $ 1.8 million. If the property was not repurchased in two years, the land trust had the right to sell its one-half interest. The owners experienced financial difficulties, and later deeded their remaining one-half interest in the property to the trust. The owners were unable to exercise the repurchase option. The appellate court held that the allegations were sufficient to plead a cause of action in usury. The court held that the transaction constituted a loan, and that the return expected by the investors, either double or triple their investment, equated to an interest rate which exceeded the permissible amount in Fla. Stat. ch. 687.071(3).


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and remanded.

Wallen v. State


CASE NO. 5D04-326


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


877 So. 2d 737; 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 6047; 29 Fla. L. Weekly D 1059



April 30, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
Rehearing denied by Wallen v. State, 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 10168 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 5th Dist., June 9, 2004)
Remanded by Wallen v. State, 909 So. 2d 520, 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 13398 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 5th Dist., Aug. 26, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: 3.800. Appeal from the Circuit Court for St. Johns County, Robert K. Mathis, Judge.



DISPOSITION: SENTENCE VACATED IN PART; REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for St. Johns County (Florida) summarily denied defendant's motion for post-conviction relief, filed pursuant to Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.800(a), in which he alleged that a 15-year sentence imposed against him upon a conviction for aggravated assault with a deadly weapon was illegal. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged the judgment entered against him. It was not clear from the record whether he was sentenced as an habitual felony offender or a violent felony offender for the aggravated assault with a deadly weapon conviction, but the maximum sentence for a habitual felony offender was 10 years, with a five-year minimum mandatory sentence if he was found to be a violent felony offender. While defendant agreed to the longer 15-year sentence, such did not bar him from attacking the same as an illegal sentence. Because the aggravated assault with a deadly weapon count was only one of several counts that resulted in consecutive and concurrent sentences totaling 75 years, the appeals court only vacated the sentence for the aggravated assault with a deadly weapon count, rejecting defendant's claim that his sentence for aggravated battery was also illegal. But, on remand, the State was allowed the option of agreeing to a legal sentence on the aggravated assault with a deadly weapon count, or withdrawing from the plea agreement and proceeding to trial on all counts.


OUTCOME: The sentence was vacated in part, and the matter was remanded.

K.A. v. Dep't of Children & Family Servs. (In the Interest of K.A.)


Case No. 2D03-866, Case No. 2D03-876


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


880 So. 2d 705; 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 5828; 29 Fla. L. Weekly D 1041



April 28, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication May 25, 2004.  [**1]
Review denied by Fla. Dep't of Children & Families v. K.A., 884 So. 2d 22, 2004 Fla. LEXIS 1491 (Fla., Sept. 8, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Polk County; Robert L. Doyel, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant parents appealed from a judgment entered by the Circuit Court for Polk County (Florida) terminating their parental rights to three children upon the petition of appellee Florida Department of Children and Family Services.


OVERVIEW: The children were removed from their home when the mother brought the infant to the hospital with three broken bones consistent with shaken baby syndrome. The appellate court held that the infant's abuse constituted egregious conduct that threatened the health of the child, and that the parents were the only persons with the opportunity to inflict the injuries. However, there was not substantial evidence that the parents posed a substantial risk of significant harm to the two older children. The two older children had not been abandoned, abused, or neglected. They were well cared for and were closely bonded to their parents. The parents did not suffer from any physical or mental illness that would inhibit their proper care of the older children. Further, there was no indication the older children were aware of the infant's abuse, or that it had any psychological impact upon them. The finding that the termination of the parents' rights to the two older children was the least restrictive means of protecting them was clearly erroneous. Finally, the Department failed to show that termination of the parents' rights to the older children was in their manifest best interest.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed as to its termination of the parental rights to the youngest child. That portion of the judgment that terminated the parents' rights to the two older children was reversed. On remand, if the children were readjudicated dependent, the Department was directed to develop, and the trial court was directed to adopt, a case plan for the parents with a goal of reunification of the parents and their two older children.

Cashatt v. State


CASE NO. 1D02-4638


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


873 So. 2d 430; 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 5656; 29 Fla. L. Weekly D 1026



April 26, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication June 17, 2004.
Rehearing denied by Cashatt v. State, 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 11358 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., June 1, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from the Circuit Court for Duval County. Judge Peter L. Dearing.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled nolo contendere to a violation of Fla. Stat. ch. 847.0135(3) (2001), included in the Computer Pornography and Child Exploitation Prevention Act of 1986. Earlier, the Circuit Court for Duval County (Florida) denied defendant's motions to dismiss. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant arranged, over the Internet, to meet with a detective, who was posing as a 14-year-old boy, for the purpose of participating in illegal sexual activities. On appeal, defendant challenged the facial constitutionality of Fla. Stat. ch. 847.0135(3) (2001) and also contended that the statute was invalid for failure to state a mens rea or scienter requirement. The appellate court ruled that even if ch. 847.0135(3) was considered a content-based restriction on constitutionally protected speech, it passed the "strict scrutiny" test because it promoted a compelling state interest in protecting children from persons who solicited or lured them to commit illegal acts and was narrowly tailored to promote that interest, specifically limiting its prohibitions to communication intended to solicit or lure a child to commit illegal acts. The terms of the statute were sufficiently precise. The State's traverse adequately demonstrated a material dispute of the ultimate facts and that the Internet communications alone constituted a prima facie case of guilt under Fla. Stat. ch. 847.0135(3) (2001). Defendant's Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.190(c)(4) motion to dismiss was properly denied.


OUTCOME: The conviction and sentence were affirmed.

State v. Steele


Case No. 2D04-1049


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


872 So. 2d 364; 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 5581; 29 Fla. L. Weekly D 1016



April 23, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 17, 2004.
Later proceeding at State v. Steele, 884 So. 2d 24, 2004 Fla. LEXIS 1978 (Fla., 2004)
Quashed by, Remanded by, Certified question answered by State v. Steele, 921 So. 2d 538, 2005 Fla. LEXIS 2043 (Fla., Oct. 12, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Petition for Writ of Certiorari to the Circuit Court for Pasco County; Lynn Tepper, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State of Florida sought certiorari review of a pretrial order by the Circuit Court for Pasco County (Florida), which required the State to provide defendant with notice of the aggravating factors it intended to prove in his capital murder trial and which required that the jury would be required to complete a specific interrogatory verdict form regarding the aggravating factors it found.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with first-degree murder. Defendant filed a pretrial motion to bar imposition of the death penalty. That motion was denied, but the State was ordered to provide the defense with adequate notice of the aggravating factors it intended to submit in support of the death penalty. The trial court also announced it would submit a special verdict form for the jury to fill out regarding the aggravating factors. The State appealed. The court found that requiring the State to provide advance notice of the aggravators was a departure from the essential requirements of law because the aggravating factors were limited to those listed in Fla. Stat. ch. 921.141(5) (1987). However, the State was not entitled to relief from the trial court's order regarding the verdict form. Florida law did not specifically prohibit a trial judge from using a special verdict form such as the one ordered, so the order did not depart from the essential requirements of law. The court certified the questions presented to the supreme court if that court wished to review the issue.


OUTCOME: The court denied certiorari as to the portion of the order requiring the special verdict form, but the court granted certiorari as to the portion of the order requiring notice of aggravators. The court quashed that portion of the trial court's order and remanded. The court also certified questions to the state supreme court for its review if it chose.

Bush v. Schiavo


Case No. 2D03-5123


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


871 So. 2d 1012; 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 6573; 29 Fla. L. Weekly D 1020



April 23, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected May 12, 2004.
Subsequent appeal at Bush v. Schiavo, 885 So. 2d 321, 2004 Fla. LEXIS 1539 (Fla., 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from nonfinal order of the Circuit Court for Pinellas County; W. Douglas Baird, Judge.
Schindler v. Schiavo, 866 So. 2d 140, 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 1576 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2d Dist., 2004)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Governor sought review from an order by the Circuit Court for Pinellas County (Florida) that denied his motion to dismiss appellee guardian's underlying cause of action for lack of jurisdiction and improper venue.


OVERVIEW: After the guardian obtained the trial court's authorization to remove the nutrition and hydration tubes sustaining his wife, the Governor entered a stay and directed that the nutrition and hydration tubes be reinserted pursuant to 2003 Fla. Laws ch. 418. The guardian filed an action, inter alia, for a temporary injunction to prohibit the Governor from enforcing the statute. At no time during a hearing on the Governor's objection to the injunction did the Governor's counsel object to the trial court's jurisdiction or the guardian's failure to effect personal service. The appellate court held that by participating in the hearing and receiving material benefits thereof, the Governor submitted to the trial court's jurisdiction. Because the matter concerned the wife, who was in Pinellas County, the sword-wielder doctrine applied and Pinellas County was the proper venue for the litigation.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.

Ortiz v. State


CASE NO. 4D02-4424


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


869 So. 2d 1278; 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 5460; 29 Fla. L. Weekly D 1000



April 21, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 7, 2004.
Review denied by Ortiz v. State, 941 So. 2d 368, 2006 Fla. LEXIS 2402 (Fla., 2006)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Perez Ortiz v. Florida, 549 U.S. 1129, 127 S. Ct. 965, 166 L. Ed. 2d 733, 2007 U.S. LEXIS 298 (2007)
Post-conviction proceeding at, Remanded by Ortiz v. State, 4 So. 3d 794, 2009 Fla. App. LEXIS 2480 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., 2009)
Post-conviction relief denied at Ortiz v. State, 96 So. 3d 908, 2012 Fla. App. LEXIS 5119 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., 2012)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Ortiz v. Crews, 2014 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 185776 (S.D. Fla., June 12, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County; Richard I. Wennet, Judge; L.T. Case No. 01-7486 CFA02.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury in the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County (Florida), convicted defendant of three counts of attempted sexual battery. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: During defendant's trial for sexual battery of his stepdaughter in the home, two other children testified that defendant had molested them when they spent the night at his home. Defendant objected, claiming that Fla. Stat. ch. 90.404(2)(b) (2001) was unconstitutional for violating both due process and constitutional ex post facto prohibitions and for permitting the introduction of irrelevant evidence. The trial court denied the motion and admitted the testimony. Defendant argued that the trial court erred in admitting evidence pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 90.404(2)(b) (2001). The appellate court ruled that Fla. Stat. ch. 90.404(2)(b) (2001) was constitutional in cases where identity of the perpetrator was not in issue. Further, Fla. Stat. ch. 90.404(2)(b) (2001) did not violate the ex post facto clause because it was a procedural change. The trial court carefully and repeatedly instructed the jury as to how to use this evidence. It did not become a feature of the trial. The trial court did not err in admitting this evidence.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Zimmerman v. Fla. Windstorm Underwriting Ass'n


CASE NO. 1D02-2896


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


873 So. 2d 411; 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 5421; 29 Fla. L. Weekly D 971



April 20, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication June 18, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An appeal from the Circuit Court for Leon County. Judge Nikki Ann Clark.
Dep't of Ins. v. Fla. Windstorm Underwriting Ass'n, 802 So. 2d 1153, 2001 Fla. App. LEXIS 16262 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., 2001)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and vacated in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant homeowners appealed from a summary judgment entered by the Circuit Court for Leon County (Florida) ruling that appellee Florida Windstorm Underwriting Association's (FWUA) rate increase did not have to be refunded, denying injunctive relief, and declaring that FWUA's rate increase was approved by appellee Florida Department of Insurance as a result of an arbitration, which had been affirmed in the Department's appeal.


OVERVIEW: The homeowners were aligned with the Department in asserting that arbitration was an improper means of deciding whether a rate hike in the FWUA's premiums should be allowed. The appellate court held that the Department had never given its approval of the rate hike, and that the FWUA's resort to arbitration as a means of raising rates was a material error made by the insurer under Fla. Stat. ch. 627.062(2)(g) (2003). The FWUA's rate increases had to be approved by the Department under the FWUA's Plan of Operation. The FWUA's resort to ch. 627.062(6) after the Department disapproved the request for rate increases was not authorized as the Plan of Operation required Department approval, not an arbitration award. The statutory amendment permitting rate arbitration was permissive, not mandatory, and did not alter the FWUA's Plan of Operation. Neither the FWUA's Plan of Operation nor the Department's rule had been amended to allow the FWUA to elect rate arbitration. As the Department had not acted, the trial court could not order the monetary relief sought by the homeowners. The homeowners were directed to seek any credits or refunds from the Department.


OUTCOME: The trial court's refusal to order refunds and the denial of injunctive relief was affirmed. The judgment and declaration were reversed insofar as it declared that construed the statute and the administrative code.

Sontay v. Avis Rent-A-Car Sys.


CASE NO. 4D03-238


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


872 So. 2d 316; 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 5034; 29 Fla. L. Weekly D 942



April 14, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 28, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County; Elizabeth T. Maass, Judge; L.T. Case No. CL 01-3930 AI.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant injured party appealed from a final judgment incorporating his settlement with appellee rental car lessor, entered by the Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County (Florida), in the injured party's suit against the lessor for vicarious liability, negligent entrustment, and a derivative claim on behalf of the injured party's minor children, after the negligent entrustment count was dismissed.


OVERVIEW: The injured party argued that Fla. Stat. ch. 324.021(9) was unconstitutional as violative of his right of access to the courts. The appellate court noted that the state's highest court had approved of ch. 324.021(9)(b)1, which eliminated the vicarious liability of long-term lessors provided the lessee maintained certain levels of insurance coverage. Limiting the liability of one vicariously liable did not equate to denial of access to court as ch. 324.021(9)(b) did not limit the injured party's right to recover damages from the actual driver. Nor did it place a cap upon those damages. The statute also did not limit the injured party's right to a jury trial. Finally, the statute was rationally related to the legitimate legislative goal of shifting some of the responsibility for damages due to the operation of the motor vehicle from the owner of a motor vehicle to the driver of the vehicle, who was the actual tortfeasor, in short term leases. The statute did not discriminate against plaintiffs suffering the worst injuries as the damages cap applied to all plaintiffs and did not contain any arbitrary or oppressive classifications.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1837 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Ward v. Ward


CASE NO. 3D03-956


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, THIRD DISTRICT


874 So. 2d 634; 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 5201; 29 Fla. L. Weekly D 919



April 14, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication June 9, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from the Circuit Court for Miami-Dade County, Philip Cook, Judge. LOWER TRIBUNAL NO.: 99-13140.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee wife filed an action against appellant husband, seeking dissolution of the parties' marriage and primary parental responsibility for the parties' child. The husband joined appellee wife's parents as parties to the action, and filed a motion to vacate a prior order which gave custody of his daughter to his wife's parents. The Circuit Court for Miami-Dade County (Florida) denied the husband's motion, and the husband appealed.


OVERVIEW: A husband and wife let their daughter live with the wife's parents and subsequently executed an agreement which gave the parents custody of their daughter. Several months later, the parents sought a court order awarding them custody of the child, and a court gave them custody. Six months later, the wife filed an action seeking dissolution of her marriage. The husband joined the wife's parents as parties in the wife's action, and he sought an order vacating the order which gave his wife's parents custody of his child. However, the trial court denied his motion to vacate the order. The appellate court held that (1) the husband was entitled to have the order awarding custody of his daughter to his wife's parents modified if he showed that he was fit to have custody and that a change in custody would not be detrimental to the child; and (2) because there was no evidence that the husband waived his parental rights or that his parental rights were terminated, and the parties agreed that he was fit to have custody, the trial court should have heard evidence on the issue of whether a change in custody would have been detrimental to the child before it denied the husband's motion.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the trial court's judgment denying the husband's motion to vacate the order awarding custody of his child to the wife's parents, and remanded the case with instructions that the trial court permit all parties to introduce evidence on the issue of whether a change in custody would be likely to produce mental, physical, or emotional harm of a lasting nature to the child.

Smith v. State


CASE NO.: 1D02-4229 and 1D02-5001


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


871 So. 2d 296; 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 4572; 29 Fla. L. Weekly D 853



April 7, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 21, 2004.
Rehearing denied by Smith v. State, 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 7606 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., May 5, 2004)
Review denied by Smith v. State, 942 So. 2d 413, 2006 Fla. LEXIS 2482 (Fla., Oct. 17, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from the Circuit Court for Okaloosa County. Thomas T. Remington, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED in part, REVERSED in part, and REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Okaloosa County, Florida, entered judgments in two criminal cases against defendant. Defendant's appeals of the judgments were consolidated for appeal. In the second case, defendant's appellate counsel (1) moved, under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.800(b)(2), to correct the trial court's sentencing errors, and (2) argued that the trial court erred in declaring defendant to be a sex offender.


OVERVIEW: In the second case, counsel alleged that under Rule 3.800(b)(2), defendant's new split sentences for attempted lewd acts were excessive and that sex offender probation could not be imposed for grand theft. The trial court agreed and orally pronounced a corrected sentence. The appeals court found, however, that the trial court failed to enter, and on remand was required to enter, a written judgment and sentence to reflect the corrected oral pronouncement of sentence. The trial court had rejected defendant's argument that Fla. Stat. ch. 943.0435 (1998), which required the registration of "sex offenders," was unconstitutional on the ground that it denied procedural due process. The appeals court had recently rejected that constitutional challenge under both Fla. Stat. chs. 775.21, 943.0435. Fla. Stat. ch. 775.21 was the sexual predator law. Fla. Stat. chs. 775.21, 943.0435 were indistinguishable, with respect to whether a hearing was required before the stigma of sexual offender status was imposed, as they both required an automatic determination if one of the enumerated crimes had been committed, registration for life, and criminal prosecution if a person failed to register.


OUTCOME: The appeals court affirmed the appeal in the first case without discussion. The appeals court reversed only the sentencing judgment in the second case, and remanded the case for the entry of a corrected written sentencing judgment in accordance with its instructions.

 

1839 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Zatyka v. State


Case No. 2D03-3265


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


872 So. 2d 285; 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 4636; 29 Fla. L. Weekly D 858



April 7, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 4, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal pursuant to Fla. R. App. P. 9.141(b)(2) from the Circuit Court for Pinellas County; Linda R. Allan, Judge.
Zatyka v. State, 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 17567 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2d Dist., Nov. 19, 2003)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, who was convicted of trafficking in phenethylamines, appealed the denial of his petition for a writ of habeas corpus by the Circuit Court for Pinellas County (Florida). Since defendant claimed that the imposed mandatory minimum was an illegal sentence pursuant to Taylor, his petition was treated as a motion to correct an illegal sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant asserted his sentence was illegal under Taylor. The appellate court held that even though defendant committed his offense within the Taylor window period. the Taylor case was inapplicable to defendant's claim for relief. In Taylor, the statutory changes contained in 1999 Fla. Laws ch. 188 were determined to be unconstitutional because the enactment of 1999 Fla. Laws ch. 188 violated the single subject rule contained in Florida's constitution. However, the offense of trafficking in phenethylamines and its mandatory minimum sentences were initially enacted into law by 2000 Fla. Laws ch. 320, which came afterwards. Therefore, the holding of Taylor did not apply. Because the mandatory minimum sentence imposed on defendant was a legal sentence, the trial court properly denied defendant's petition for a writ of habeas corpus.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Anglin v. State


Case No. 5D03-329


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


869 So. 2d 674; 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 4296; 29 Fla. L. Weekly D 830



April 2, 2004, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:

 [**1] THIS OPINION WAS WITHDRAWN BY THE COURT


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication May 5, 2004.
Reversed by, Remanded by State v. Jones, 908 So. 2d 1054, 2005 Fla. LEXIS 731 (Fla., Apr. 21, 2005)
On remand at, Opinion withdrawn by Anglin v. State, 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 9049 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 5th Dist., June 3, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Orange County, Richard F. Conrad, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED FOR CORRECTION OF SENTENCE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment by the Circuit Court for Orange County (Florida) that, inter alia, sentenced him to minimum mandatory terms for aggravated assault on a law enforcement officer; defendant claimed that he was forced to proceed pro se and that the mandatory sentences were unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pleaded guilty to robbery with a firearm, aggravated assault on a law enforcement officer, and aggravated fleeing or attempting to elude a law enforcement officer at high speed or with wanton disregard. The appellate court held that while defendant's counsel was permitted to withdraw at the sentencing hearing, defendant was not required to proceed pro se. Rather, the trial court appointed the same attorney to act as standby counsel and the attorney functioned as defendant's attorney in all material respects at sentencing. Given the length of defendant's sentences, the minimum mandatory provisions had no impact on the term of his incarceration. However, because the minimum mandatory sentences imposed under Fla. Stat. ch. 784.07(2)(c) (2001) violated the single subject rule and the constitutional ex post facto clauses, the trial court was to delete them.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed; however, the sentence was remanded for correction.

Ennis v. Regier


Case Nos. 2D03-877, 2D03-887, CONSOLIDATED


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


869 So. 2d 701; 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 4336; 29 Fla. L. Weekly D 844



April 2, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 21, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeals from the Circuit Court for DeSoto County; James S. Parker, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the denial of his two petitions for habeas corpus by the Circuit Court for DeSoto County (Florida), as the trial court did not consider them on the merits. In the first petition, he contended his continued detention was illegal and that the State failed to comply with time standards set forth in Fla. Stat. ch. 394.9135 (2000). The second petition asserted his continued detention was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was due to be released. However, the State sought to have him civilly committed as a sexually violent predator. Thus, he was transferred to the custody of the Department of Children and Family Services to be detained in accordance with the provisions of the Jimmy Ryce Act, Fla. Stat. ch. 394.910 to 394.930 (2000). The appellate court held his constitutional argument had already been rejected by the United States Supreme Court and the Florida Supreme Court. His contention that the expert's reports were not legally sufficient to support his detention was not a proper basis for habeas relief. However, his contention that the State did not comply with the time requirements of Fla. Stat. ch. 394.9135 did raise an issue that was properly the subject of a habeas petition. Therefore, the trial court should have considered that portion of his petition on the merits. However, he was not entitled to complete relief. Certain provisions did not apply to him. His assertion that he was not brought to trial within 30 days as required by Fla. Stat. ch. 394.916(1) could have entitled him to immediate release.


OUTCOME: The dismissal of the second petition was affirmed. The dismissal of the first petition was affirmed in part and reversed in part. The matter was remanded for the trial court to consider the issue of whether appellant was brought to trial within 30 days and whether the State properly sought a continuance.

Gilreath v. Westgate Daytona, Ltd.


Case No. 5D02-3699


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


871 So. 2d 961; 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 4335; 29 Fla. L. Weekly D 819



April 2, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
Rehearing denied by Gilreath v. Westgate Daytona, Ltd., 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 7795 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 5th Dist., May 4, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Volusia County, Edwin P. B. Sanders, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED in part; REVERSED in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county appraiser sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court for Volusia County (Florida) which quashed the appraiser's ad valorem tax assessments of certain condominium units owned by appellee developer over a two-year period. The judgment declared that the condominium units were improperly assessed as timeshare property.


OVERVIEW: A declaration of condominium governed a condominium complex and allowed for future creation of timeshare estates. The developer purchased 24 condominium units and began to market 16 units as timeshares. The trial court ordered the auditor to reassess all of the units as condominiums. The appellate court concluded that the assessment of the units as timeshares was proper after approval of the public offering statement (POS). Because the POS was not approved until November of the first year of assessments, and in light of the requirement that the assessment had to be made as of January 1 pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 192.042(1) (2002), the units were improperly assessed as timeshares for the first year, but not for the following year. The use of the condominiums as timeshares under Fla. Stat. ch. 193.011(2) (2002) was totally dependent on conversion of the units to timeshares. Moreover, the use of timeshares was not immediate and was speculative because it depended on obtaining approval of the POS. Thus, assessing the condominiums as timeshares as their highest and best use prior to approval of the POS was improper.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed as to the assessments prior to January 1. It was reversed as to its order quashing the assessments after January 1.

R.A.M. of S. Fla., Inc. v. WCI Cmtys., Inc.


Case No. 2D03-284


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


869 So. 2d 1210; 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 3868; 29 Fla. L. Weekly D 761



March 26, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by R.A.M. of S. Fla., Inc. v. WCI Cmtys., Inc., 895 So. 2d 406, 2005 Fla. LEXIS 293 (Fla., Feb. 8, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Lee County; J. Frank Porter, Acting Circuit Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant subcontractor challenged a decision of the Circuit Court for Lee County (Florida), which granted appellee property owner's motion to stay arbitration, ruled that the subcontractor's contract action and lien claim against appellee property owner, asserted as a cross-claim in litigation initiated by a third party, was based on an unenforceable contract under Fla. Stat. ch. 489.128 (2000), and discharged the subcontractor's lien.


OVERVIEW: During construction, a dispute arose regarding the work being performed by the subcontractor, and the owner refused to pay certain sums due under the contract. Although the owner invoked an arbitration clause in the contract, it subsequently learned that the subcontractor did not become licensed until two years after the construction began and more than a year and a half after it was terminated. Affirming, the court held that the subcontractor was not entitled to cure its unlicensed status pursuant to the prior version of Fla. Stat. ch. 489.128 (1999) where the cure provision of the statute was repealed by ch. 489.128 (2000). The trial court's application of ch. 489.128 (2000), rendering the contract unenforceable, was not a retroactive application because the subcontractor was on "fair notice" that the statutory provision for curing its unlicensed status was a matter of legislative grace that could be withdrawn by subsequent legislative action, the right the subcontractor had under ch. 489.128 (1999) was not a vested right, and once ch. 498.128 (2000) became effective, the opportunity previously afforded to the subcontractor to cure its unlicensed status was properly cut off.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order barring the subcontractor's claims against the owner.

Jones v. State


CASE NO.: 5D01-2775


DISTRICT COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


872 So. 2d 938; 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 3885; 29 Fla. L. Weekly D 747



March 26, 2004, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:

 [**1] THIS OPINION WAS WITHDRAWN BY THE COURT


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Jones v. State, 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 5527 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 5th Dist., Mar. 26, 2004).
Reversed by, Remanded by State v. Jones, 908 So. 2d 1054, 2005 Fla. LEXIS 731 (Fla., Apr. 21, 2005).
Opinion withdrawn by Jones v. State, 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 10757 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 5th Dist., June 16, 2005).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Orange County, Frederick J. Lauten, Judge.
Jones v. State, 2002 Fla. App. LEXIS 16136 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 5th Dist., Nov. 1, 2002).



DISPOSITION: REVERSED and REMANDED FOR RESENTENCING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty under a plea bargain to two counts of aggravated assault on a law enforcement officer in violation of Fla. Stat. ch. 784.07(2)(c). The Circuit Court for Orange County, Florida, imposed mandatory minimum sentences. Defendant appealed, alleging that retroactive application of a statutory amendment imposing mandatory minimum sentences violated the U.S. and Florida Constitution's Ex Post Facto Clauses.


OVERVIEW: The offenses at issue were committed before the effective date of 2002 Fla. Laws ch. 209, which purported to amend Fla. Stat. ch. 784.07(2)(c) (1997) to require imposition of a mandatory minimum prison term. 2002 Fla. Laws ch. 209 was passed in response to state appellate courts having found 1999 Fla. Laws ch. 188, which also provided for such sentences, to be unconstitutional for violating the single subject rule imposed by Fla. Const. art. III, § 6. The instant court had held in Hersey v. State, 831 So. 2d 679 (Fla. 5th DCA 2002), that 2002 Fla. Laws ch. 209 could be applied retroactively, but it receded from that decision. Chapter 209 was never a part of Florida law because its unconstitutional enactment rendered it void ab initio. Moreover, 1999 Fla. Laws ch. 188 effected a substantive change in the law to defendant's detriment. That defendant had entered into a plea agreement was immaterial; imposition of a mandatory minimum sentence that was not authorized by statute was an illegal sentence, and a defendant could not be bound by an agreement to accept an illegal sentence.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded for resentencing.

Bush v. Holmes


CASE NOS.: 1D02-3160, 1D02-3163 and 1D 02-3199


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


867 So. 2d 1270; 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 3598; 29 Fla. L. Weekly D 720



March 23, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 8, 2004.
Subsequent appeal at, Question certified by Bush v. Holmes, 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 12479 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., Aug. 16, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from an order of the Circuit Court for Leon County. Honorable P. Kevin Davey, Judge.
Bush v. Holmes, 767 So. 2d 668, 2000 Fla. App. LEXIS 12658 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., 2000)



DISPOSITION: Appellants' motion to review the trial court's orders conditioning the automatic stay with the posting of a bond granted; automatic stay will remain in effect pending review without appellants posting a bond.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The judgment of the Circuit Court for Leon County held that the Opportunity Scholarship Program, Fla. Stat. ch. 229.0537 (1999), was unconstitutional under Fla. Const. art. I, § 3. The trial court required appellants, state officials and others, to post a bond or letter of credit to secure reimbursement of funds lost to the school districts while the case was appealed. Appellants sought removal of the bond.


OVERVIEW: Under Fla. R. App. P. 9.310(b)(2), the state, any public officer in an official capacity, board, commission, or other public body was allowed an automatic stay pending review without the necessity of posting a bond. The Florida Supreme Court had interpreted the rule as allowing trial and appellate courts the discretion to require governmental entities to post supersedeas bonds in suits where the judgment concerned operational-level functions but found that no authority existed to lawfully require such bonds in planning-level governmental functions. The appellate court concluded that the Florida Legislature's enactment of the Opportunity Scholarship Program was clearly a planning-level governmental function that did not require a bond for review of the trial court's declaration that it was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The appellate court granted appellants' motion to review the trial court's orders conditioning the automatic stay with the posting of a bond and held that the automatic stay would remain in effect pending review without appellants posting a bond or letter of credit as required by the trial court.
