Fla. Pub. Emples. Council 79 v. Pub. Emples. Rels. Comm'n


CASE NO. 1D03-1190


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


871 So. 2d 270; 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 3533; 175 L.R.R.M. 2502; 29 Fla. L. Weekly D 694



March 22, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 20, 2004
Review denied by Fla. Pub. Emples. Council 79 v. Public Emples. Rels. Comm'n, 884 So. 2d 22, 2004 Fla. LEXIS 1528 (Fla., Sept. 8, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from an order of the Public Employees Relations Commission.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee Florida Public Employees Relations Commission (PERC) dismissed appellant union's petitions to amend certification on the basis that the union's exception that Fla. Stat. ch. 447.203(2) (2002) was not controlling was meritless and determined that the statute clearly and unambiguously set forth that the Boards of Trustees were deemed the public employers.


OVERVIEW: The Florida Legislature passed a law abolishing the Florida Board of Regents, effective July 1, 2001, and established new criteria for local Boards of Trustees at each state university. The law provided that the individual boards would be the public employer with respect to all public employees of the respective state university. Thereafter, the voters of Florida approved a constitutional amendment on the issue. On appeal, the union argued that the PERC erred by designating the university Boards of Trustees as the public employers of their respective universities. The appellate court noted that, regardless of the PERC's reliance on Fla. Stat. ch. 447.203(2) (2002) in denying the union's petitions, it reached the correct result because the Board of Governors' action of designating the Boards of Trustees as the public employers of their respective universities constituted a legitimate exercise of constitutional authority. The appellate court held that, as the Board of Governors, pursuant to the powers bestowed upon it by the voters of Florida, designated the Boards of Trustees as the public employers of their respective universities, the PERC's order would not be disturbed.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Williams v. State


Case No. 2D03-4305


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


870 So. 2d 213; 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 3517; 29 Fla. L. Weekly D 688



March 19, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reversed by, Remanded by State v. Henderson, 894 So. 2d 966, 2005 Fla. LEXIS 266 (Fla., Feb. 17, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Polk County; Wm. Bruce Smith, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded, with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the order of the Circuit Court for Polk County (Florida) denying his motion to correct illegal sentence filed pursuant to Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.800(a).


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed the three-year mandatory minimum term of imprisonment imposed pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 893.135(1)(f)(1)(a) (1999) was illegal based on Taylor, which found that 1999 Fla. Laws 188, providing for the imposition of mandatory minimum prison sentences for certain drug offenses, was unconstitutional. However, the trial court found Taylor did not apply retroactively, because neither the U.S. Supreme Court nor the Florida Supreme Court had adopted the change of law. The appellate court found this reasoning erroneous. The law drew a distinction between a void law and one that was merely voidable. Thus, based on Green and Taylor, 1999 Fla. Laws 188 was illegally enacted and void ab initio. Pursuant to Green, if defendant committed the offense within the Taylor window, the trial court was required to resentence him under the 1997 version of ch. 893.135(1)(f)(1)(a). The legislature provided for the retroactive application of each reenactment to July 1, 1999, the effective date of 1999 Fla. Laws 188. The trial court relied on Callaway, but Calloway and Witt had no application when an appellate court determined a statute was never legally enacted.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and remanded, with instructions. If, as he alleged in his motion, defendant committed the offense of trafficking in methamphetamine within the proper window, the trial court was to resentence him. Conflict was certified with the Fourth and Fifth District cases with which the court previously disagreed.

Mailly v. Jenne


CASE NO. 4D03-2195


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


867 So. 2d 1250; 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 3318; 29 Fla. L. Weekly D 657

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County; Victor Tobin, Judge; L.T. Case No. 01-1606 (02).



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff arrestees appealed a grant of summary judgment in favor of defendant sheriff by the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County (Florida), in their action for false arrest.


OVERVIEW: The State charged the arrestees with engaging in lewdness and remaining in a place for the purposes of prostitution, lewdness, or assignation, in violation of Fla. Stat. ch. 796.07(2)(e), (g) (1999). The arrests arose from conduct that occurred at an adults-only "swingers" club. After the State nolle prossed the charges, the arrestees sued the sheriff for false arrest. The appellate court held that the sheriff's interpretation of what was lewd was at least arguable, and not "cockeyed." At the time the arrests occurred, the sheriff had probable cause to arrest the arrestees for remaining in a place for the purposes of prostitution, lewdness, or assignation. Therefore, the trial court properly granted summary judgment to the sheriff.


OUTCOME: The grant of summary judgment was affirmed.

Scofield v. Sibley


CASE NO. 1D02-3026


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


874 So. 2d 611; 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 2659; 29 Fla. L. Weekly D 563



March 4, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 1, 2004.
Rehearing denied by Scofield v. Sibley, 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 10173 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., June 15, 2004)
Review denied by Scofield v. Sibley, 890 So. 2d 1115, 2004 Fla. LEXIS 2226 (Fla., Nov. 30, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from the Circuit Court of Alachua County. Larry G. Turner, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a father and his daughter, filed a 12-count complaint against defendants, a doctor and a health center, alleging claims for negligence and for intentional torts. The Circuit Court of Alachua County (Florida) dismissed the complaint with prejudice. Plaintiffs appealed.


OVERVIEW: The claims derived from an alleged obligation of defendants to notify the father of the intent to perform an abortion on his daughter in September 1997, when she was 14 years old, and to obtain his authorization for the procedure. The complaint also averred that the former minor had a right to disavow her consent, upon attaining the age of majority, and then to sue for damages occasioned by the procedure. The appellate court held that the claims were completely foreclosed by the Florida Supreme Court's previous ruling that a minor (of any age if such minor could become pregnant) had the constitutional right to an abortion without the parents' knowledge or consent, pursuant to the privacy provision of Fla. Const. art. 1, § 23. A minor's right to privacy superseded parental rights in the context of abortion. In light of the wide authority that the State granted an unwed minor to make life-or-death decisions concerning herself or an existing child without parental consent, there did not seem to be a special compelling interest on the part of the state under Florida law in protecting the minor only where abortion was concerned.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

1852 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Baker County Press, Inc. v. Baker County Med. Servs.


CASE NO. 1D03-803


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


870 So. 2d 189; 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 2673; 32 Media L. Rep. 1939; 29 Fla. L. Weekly D 560



March 4, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 10, 2004.
Review denied by Baker County Press, Inc. v. Baker County Med. Servs., 885 So. 2d 386, 2004 Fla. LEXIS 1660 (Fla., 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from the Circuit Court for Baker County. Honorable Elzie S. Sanders, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a corporation and a publisher, appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court for Baker County (Florida) in favor of appellee medical corporation, which ruled that appellants were not entitled to requested documents and minutes of board meetings because the medical corporation was not subject to the Public Records Act, Fla. Stat. ch. 119, or the Sunshine Law, Fla. Stat. ch. 286.


OVERVIEW: The medical corporation was generally subject to the Public Records Act and the Sunshine Law. However, the medical corporation argued that the statutory exemptions had to be considered. The appellate court concluded that Fla. Stat. ch. 395.3036 (2002) provided exemptions for the medical corporation from the Public Records Act and the Sunshine Law, and was facially constitutional because the constitutional concerns expressed by the Florida Supreme Court in Halifax had been satisfied by the Florida Legislature in its enactment of Fla. Stat. ch. 395.3036, and appellants failed to show that Fla. Stat. ch. 395.3036 was unconstitutional. However, in contrast to the enactment of Fla. Stat. ch. 395.3036, there were no legislative findings regarding the public necessity for the exemption in Fla. Stat. ch. 155.40. Therefore, the appellate court agreed with appellants that Fla. Stat. ch. 155.40 was unconstitutional under Halifax.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

1853 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


A.D. v. K.S. (In the Interest of S.D.)


Case No. 2D03-1976


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


869 So. 2d 39; 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 2571; 29 Fla. L. Weekly D 550



March 3, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication March 24, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Writ of Prohibition to the Circuit Court for Pinellas County; Robert James Morris, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: Petition for writ of certiorari granted and case remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner father petitioned for a writ of prohibition and/or a writ of certiorari to the Circuit Court for Pinellas County (Florida) that granted custody of a child to the father and ordered him to allow the maternal relatives to visit with the child.


OVERVIEW: The father specifically objected to that portion of the order that gave the county sheriff's office discretion to permit the maternal grandmother and the maternal great-grandmother to have unsupervised visitation with the minor child. The appellate court treated the petition for writ of prohibition as a petition for writ of certiorari. The appellate court held that, pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 39.509 (2002), the trial court could not legally order the father to provide visitation to the maternal relatives without a showing of harm, as the child was never adjudicated dependent as to the father.


OUTCOME: The petition for writ of certiorari was granted; those portions of the order that granted visitation with the maternal grandmother and great-grandmother were quashed and remanded for further proceedings.

 

1854 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Wright v. State


Case No. 2D03-1954


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


869 So. 2d 24; 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 2381; 29 Fla. L. Weekly D 521



February 27, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 24, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Hillsborough County; Daniel L. Perry, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment by the Circuit Court for Hillsborough County (Florida) that sentenced him for trafficking in 3,4-methylenedioxymethamphetamine (MDMA) pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 893.135(1)(j)(2)(a) (2000). Defendant claimed that the three-year mandatory minimum sentence was illegal.


OVERVIEW: 1999 Fla. Laws ch. 188, which provided for the imposition of mandatory minimum prison sentences for certain drug offenses, was found to be unconstitutional because it violated the single subject rule of the Florida Constitution. Defendant claimed that because his offense occurred in February 2002, within the window period, his mandatory minimum sentence was illegal. The appellate court held that trafficking in MDMA was not among the drug offenses listed in chapter ch. 188 and did not become a statutory offense until 2000 Fla. Laws ch. 320 took effect on October 1, 2000 and imposed mandatory minimum sentences for the new drug offenses created by that amendment. As a result, defendant's sentence was legal and the trial court did not err in sentencing defendant pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 893.135(1)(j)(2)(a) (2000) to the mandatory minimum prison sentence for trafficking in MDMA.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1855 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Reyna v. State


CASE NO. 3D02-3432


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, THIRD DISTRICT


866 So. 2d 214; 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 2158; 29 Fla. L. Weekly D 468



February 25, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 12, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from the Circuit Court for Miami-Dade County, Jerald Bagley, Judge. LOWER TRIBUNAL NO. 02-8247.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court for Miami-Dade County (Florida), which denied his motion to dismiss an information that charged him as an adult for a burglary that was committed when defendant was 16 years old.


OVERVIEW: Under the authority granted to it by Fla. Stat. ch. 985.227(1)(b), the State elected to prosecute defendant as an adult, even though the burglary he was charged with was committed when defendant was 16 years old. Defendant moved to dismiss the information on the ground that ch. 985.227(1)(b) and Fla. Stat. ch. 985.227(4) were unconstitutional. Defendant argued that those statutes violated the separation of powers doctrine and deprived him of the equal protection of the laws. The trial court denied the motion. Defendant pled no contest in exchange for one year of probation and a withhold of adjudication. He reserved his right to appeal the denial of his motion to dismiss as part of his plea bargain agreement. The court held that although the direct file statute had been amended many times over the years, the case of State v. Cain, 381 So. 2d 1361 (Fla. 1980) remained dispositive and mandated the rejection of defendant's claim.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

1856 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Crow v. State


CASE NO. 1D03-3404


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


866 So. 2d 1257; 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 1804; 29 Fla. L. Weekly D 443



February 19, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 8, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from the Circuit Court of Bay County. Michael C. Overstreet, Judge.
Crow v. State, 503 So. 2d 420, 1987 Fla. App. LEXIS 7034 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., 1987)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant inmate was convicted of first-degree murder, and his conviction was affirmed on appeal. Seventeen years later, he filed a motion for postconviction DNA testing under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.853, alleging that the test results would prove that he was not the source of the semen found in the victim's body. The Circuit Court of Bay County, Florida, denied the motion, and the inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: The inmate admitted stabbing the victim, but denied committing anal intercourse. He claimed that the victim was making forcible sexual advances and that he killed him in self defense. The State used the evidence that the victim had semen in his rectum to support its theory of premeditation and to refute the inmate's self defense claim; however, at trial the semen could not be positively identified as the inmate's. The trial court held that the inmate was not entitled to a DNA test since he admitted fatally stabbing the victim. The supreme court noted that the inmate qualified for a postconviction DNA test under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.853, but not under Fla. Stat. ch. 925.11(2)(a) (2003), which allowed such a test only to resolve a mistaken identity claim. The supreme court rejected the State's claim that Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.853 violated the separation of powers provision of Fla. Const. art. II, § 3. The decision to grant a new trial in a criminal case was unquestionably within the province of the courts, and the legislature's failure to define the circumstances under which a new trial could be granted was an apparent recognition of the fact that the issue was one for the courts.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded. On remand, the trial court could take any action authorized by the applicable rule of criminal procedure to determine whether the inmate's allegations were true and, if so, whether he was entitled to DNA testing.

 

1857 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Karwoski v. State


CASE NO. 4D02-4642


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


867 So. 2d 486; 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 1671; 29 Fla. L. Weekly D 431



February 18, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 2, 2004.
Rehearing denied by Karwoski v. State, 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 4990 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., Apr. 2, 2004)
Review denied by Karwoski v. State, 879 So. 2d 622, 2004 Fla. LEXIS 1019 (Fla., June 29, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County; Kenneth D. Stern, Judge; L.T. Case No. 01-5366 CFA02.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County (Florida), which found him guilty of computer pornography and child exploitation in violation of Fla. Stat. ch. 847.0135(3). Defendant was sentenced to community control and placed on sex offender probation.


OVERVIEW: A police officer went on-line posing as a 15-year-old boy. He was contacted by defendant. Defendant arranged a meeting so the two could have sex. On appeal, defendant argued that Fla. Stat. ch. 847.0135 was unconstitutionally overbroad, vague, and an impermissible content-based regulation in violation of his First and Fourteenth Amendment rights. The appellate court concluded that it was the speech itself that translated into the criminal conduct. Defendant's speech amounted to seduction, solicitation, and enticement of a child to commit a crime that was prohibited. Thus, defendant's overbreadth argument was unpersuasive as well as his position that the statute was an impermissible content-based regulation. Also, the statute was not overbroad for failing to define the term child because the statute specifically pointed to other chapters of the Florida Statutes where the victim was defined by age. Finally, the State proved the elements of the charges beyond a reasonable doubt. The fact that the only potential victim was an undercover officer did not preclude a conviction because the evidence indicated that the officer clearly portrayed himself as a 15-year-old boy.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and sentence were affirmed.

 

1858 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


T.T. v. State


CASE NO. 4D02-4683


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


865 So. 2d 674; 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 1686; 29 Fla. L. Weekly D 435



February 18, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 5, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County; Moses Baker, Jr., Judge; L.T. Case No. 2002CJ004189.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, a juvenile, appealed the decision of the Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County (Florida), which convicted her of knowingly disrupting a school function in violation of Fla. Stat. ch. 877.13 (2003).


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant argued that she was entitled to a judgment of acquittal. The appellate court concluded that there was sufficient evidence that she "knowingly" disrupted the proceedings. She was yelling and screaming at a school function, and was forcibly removed by police officers. An assistant principal testified that defendant's refusal to leave with the police officers disrupted the events. While defendant might have been able to resist a seizure by officers arising from conduct outside of school in the general public, she could not do so at a school function where her resistance itself disrupted the event. There was no suggestion in the testimony of anyone that her conduct in refusing to accompany the police officers was anything but knowing and purposeful on her part.


OUTCOME: The conviction was affirmed.

 

1859 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Bush v. Schiavo


Case No. 2D03-5783


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


866 So. 2d 136; 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 1568; 29 Fla. L. Weekly D 396



February 13, 2004, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Writ of Certiorari to the Circuit Court for Pinellas County; W. Douglas Baird, Judge.
Schindler v. Schiavo (In re Schiavo), 851 So. 2d 182, 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 8342 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2d Dist., 2003)



DISPOSITION: Petition for writ of certiorari granted; protective order quashed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner Governor petitioned for a writ of certiorari to the Circuit Court for Pinellas County (Florida) quashing a protective order entered at the request of respondent guardian that prohibited the Governor from taking the depositions of seven witnesses in a declaratory judgment action filed by the guardian seeking a determination that 2003 Fla. Laws ch. 418 was unconstitutional on its face and as applied to the guardian's ward.


OVERVIEW: The Governor sought to depose the guardian's relatives, medical experts, and the person who resided with the guardian. The guardian argued that any facts attested to by the witnesses were irrelevant and that all of the relevant facts were either adjudicated in the guardianship proceeding or were stipulated to by the parties. The appellate court held that some facts as to the guardian's claims that the statute was an unconstitutional bill of attainder and an invalid special law might not have been considered in the guardianship proceeding such as those pertaining to the enactment of the statute and its effect on the ward. The trial court erred in entering the protective order without resolving the parties' arguments as to the propriety of inquiry into the statute's impact on the ward and other factually based aspects of the constitutional challenge, and as to the propriety of further inquiry into facts adjudicated in the guardianship proceeding. Thus, the protective order lacked good cause. The error was not remediable on appeal as there was no way to determine how the denial of the right to depose alleged material witnesses would have affected the outcome of the action.


OUTCOME: The petition was granted. The protective order was quashed.

 

1860 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Mallory v. State


CASE NO. 4D02-908


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


866 So. 2d 127; 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 1327; 29 Fla. L. Weekly D 382



February 11, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication February 27, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County; Paul L. Backman, Judge; L.T. Case No. 01-582 CF10A.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County (Florida), convicted defendant of possession of a firearm by a convicted felon. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged his conviction, arguing that the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress. His counsel acknowledged that the motion, which was denied before trial, was not renewed during trial, and was therefore waived. But, a recent statutory amendment under Fla. Stat. ch. 90.104(1)(b) (2003) purported to eliminate the need to renew the objection at trial. Even if this statute was procedural, the instant court recommended that it be adopted as a rule. Because most pretrial denials of motions to suppress were based on findings of fact, the vast majority of those rulings, when considered on the merits, were affirmed on appeal. If those cases could be decided on direct appeal, it would eliminate the need for post-conviction proceedings on that issue. The new statute did not preclude a party from asking the court to reconsider the prior ruling at trial, it only eliminated the necessity of having to make a perfunctory renewal of the objection. Concluding that there was competent substantial evidence to support the trial court's finding that the firearm was not obtained as the result of an illegal search and seizure, defendant's conviction was upheld.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

1862 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Animal Rights Found. of Fla., Inc. v. Siegel


CASE NO. 5D03-653


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


867 So. 2d 451; 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 1144; 29 Fla. L. Weekly D 355



February 6, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 2, 2004.
Rehearing denied by Animal Rights Foun. of Fla., Inc. v. Siegel, 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 4742 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 5th Dist., Mar. 17, 2004)
Review denied by Siegel v. Animal Rights Found., 879 So. 2d 624, 2004 Fla. LEXIS 1056 (Fla., June 28, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Non-Final Appeal from the Circuit Court for Orange County, R. James Stroker, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED and REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, an animal rights foundation and an individual, sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court for Orange County (Florida), which entered a non-final order granting a temporary injunction to appellees, a timeshare developer and its president, and restricted appellants' protest activities with respect to appellees.


OVERVIEW: The developer hired an exotic animal performance to draw potential buyers for resort timeshares. The developer and its president sued appellants based on their animal rights protest activities. Appellants picketed and circulated leaflets claiming that the president abused animals. The trial court granted appellees a temporary injunction. On appeal, the court held that the evidence failed to prove that appellees were entitled to receive a temporary injunction. Further, portions of the injunction violated appellants' First Amendment rights. As to the injunction provisions regulating appellants' right to picket, the regulations were content-neutral; however, the restrictions, which limited amplification, number of picketers, and videotaping, burdened more speech than was necessary to protect any valid public interest. The prohibitions against publishing particular statements about appellees were content-based and thereby subject to strict scrutiny as prior restraints. There was no compelling state interest that was met by the injunction terms and they violated appellants' First Amendment rights. The subject speech was not commercial speech, but was purely of a political nature.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court and remanded the case.

 

1863 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


City of Miami v. Wellman


CASE NO. 3D01-3050


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, THIRD DISTRICT


875 So. 2d 635; 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 894; 29 Fla. L. Weekly D 328



February 4, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication June 16, 2004.
Rehearing, en banc, denied by City of Miami v. Wellman, 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 11019 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 3d Dist., June 16, 2004)
Quashed by, Remanded by City of Miami v. Wellman, 944 So. 2d 251, 2006 Fla. LEXIS 2592 (Fla., 2006)
Judgment entered by City of Miami v. Wellman, 2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 744 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 3d Dist., Jan. 23, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court for Miami-Dade County, Celeste Hardee Muir, Judge. LOWER TRIBUNAL NOS. 99-28417 & 99-19523.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Miami-Dade County (Florida) granted appellee class members injunctive relief in their lawsuit against appellant city attacking the validity of the city's vehicle impoundment ordinance, Miami, Fla., Code §§ 42-120 through 42-125 (1997). The city appealed, and some of the class members cross-appealed.


OVERVIEW: Both parties challenged the judgment entered. The city contended that the trial court erred in holding that its vehicle impoundment ordinance unconstitutionally conflicted with the Florida Contraband Forfeiture Act (Act), Fla. Stat. ch. 932.703(6)(a) (2002), in its treatment of innocent vehicle owners, and erred in holding that the notice requirements of the ordinance unconstitutionally conflicted with the Act. The class members argued that the Act pre-empted the ordinance. The appeals court agreed with the class members. While the Act allowed forfeiture in similar circumstances to the ones outlined in the ordinance, it provided rights which were not provided for in the ordinance. Also, the Act directly pre-empted the ordinance because it provided for a comprehensive procedure for forfeiture of property. Finally, the taking of a vehicle under the ordinance was a forfeiture because such taking was temporary. Even if a vehicle owner paid the penalty and got the vehicle back, the owner suffered a permanent loss of the amount paid as a penalty. If the owner did not prevail or pay the penalty, then the vehicle faced a sale, leaving the owner permanently deprived of his property.


OUTCOME: The order granting injunctive relief enjoining the city from enforcing its ordinance was affirmed. That part of the order finding the ordinance was enforceable in part with respect to owners who were drivers or passengers of a vehicle that was seized was reversed.

1865 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


State v. Harden


CASE NO. 3D03-521


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, THIRD DISTRICT


873 So. 2d 352; 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 623; 29 Fla. L. Weekly D 593



January 28, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected March 10, 2004. Released for Publication April 13, 2004.
Affirmed by State v. Harden, 938 So. 2d 480, 2006 Fla. LEXIS 889 (Fla., May 18, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court for Miami-Dade County, David Miller, Judge. LOWER TRIBUNAL NO. 00-38785 (A-J).



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State filed a nine-count information charging defendant and nine other defendants with racketeering, conspiracy to commit racketeering, and Medicaid fraud. The State appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court for Miami-Dade County (Florida) that granted defendants' motion to dismiss the information, and declared Florida's Medicaid Provider Fraud Statute, Fla. Stat. ch. 409.920(2)(e) (2000), unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The State alleged that the defendants violated the "anti-kickback" provision of Florida's Medicaid Provider Fraud Statute, Fla. Stat. ch. 409.920(2)(e) (2000), by paying drivers, who were alleged to be employed by or associated with three corporate entities that were engaged in the business of providing dental services to children, a per head fee or commission for the solicitation and transportation of Medicaid eligible children to dental facilities for treatment. Defendant filed a motion to dismiss the information arguing, among other things, that payment of wages by a Medicaid provider to its employees was expressly protected by federal Medicaid statutes and regulations. The trial court applied implied conflict preemption analysis and found that Fla. Stat. ch. 409.920(2)(e) was unconstitutional. Additionally, the trial court found that the mens rea requirement in Fla. Stat. ch. 409.920(1)(d) was preempted by federal law, and also unconstitutional. The appellate court found that the trial court properly found that there was implied conflict preemption and declared the statute unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Estate of Youngblood v. Halifax Convalescent Ctr., Ltd.


CASE NO. 5D02-1957


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


874 So. 2d 596; 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 465; 29 Fla. L. Weekly D 272



January 23, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Estate of Youngblood v. Halifax Convalescent Ctr., 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 10165 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 5th Dist., June 10, 2004)
Motion granted by Delta Health Group, Inc. v. Estate of Youngblood, 912 So. 2d 1217, 2005 Fla. LEXIS 1974 (Fla., Sept. 13, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Volusia County, J. David Walsh, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED; Conflict CERTIFIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a deceased nursing home patient's daughter, sought review from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Volusia County (Florida), which was entered in favor of appellee nursing home successor in the daughter's action alleging negligent treatment and care of her mother, deprivation of her nursing home rights under Fla. Stat. ch. 400, and punitive damages. The successor cross-appealed the denial of its motion for attorney's fees.


OVERVIEW: The daughter commenced the action against the original facility in her guardian capacity, but after her mother's death, she continued the action as personal representative and joined the successor. The original facility settled with the daughter. The trial court entered summary judgment for the successor on the Fla. Stat. ch. 400 claims, directed a verdict against the daughter for punitive damages, and the jury returned a verdict on the negligence claims for the successor. On appeal by the daughter, the court found that the trial court abused its discretion in allowing the successor to peremptorily challenge the only two African-American venirepersons, as it was clear under the Melbourne factors that at least one person was stricken for pretextual reasons. The court found that denial of attorney's fees to the successor was proper, as was the refusal to include the original facility on the verdict form. Although the mother died prior to the joinder of the successor, the court found that the legislative intent of whether the statutory action survived was best determined by using the 2001 version of Fla. Stat. ch. 400.023. A directed verdict on punitive damages was erroneous.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and ordered that the daughter receive a new trial. The court certified a conflict with a sister court's decision in another case.

 

1867 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Cartwright v. State (In re Cartwright)


Case No. 2D00-4663


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


870 So. 2d 152; 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 421; 29 Fla. L. Weekly D 259



January 21, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Cartwright v. State, 914 So. 2d 952, 2005 Fla. LEXIS 2152 (Fla., Oct. 17, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Manatee County; Thomas M. Gallen, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed; question certified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of an order entered by the Circuit Court for Manatee County (Florida) civilly committing him for treatment as a sexually violent predator under the statute commonly known as the Jimmy Ryce Act, Fla. Stat. ch. 394, part V (2000).


OVERVIEW: Three of appellant's issues were addressed: his commitment violated his contractual rights with the State under his previous plea agreement; the provision of the Ryce Act permitting the admission of hearsay evidence was unconstitutional on various grounds; and the instructions given by the trial court were inadequate. Appellant raised no meritorious issues. Any rights appellant had under his plea agreement pertained only to the criminal sanctions against him. Any such rights were totally irrelevant to the separate civil proceedings against him under the Ryce Act. Admission of hearsay evidence did not violate appellant's right to confrontation as those provisions under the Florida and U.S. Constitutions were expressly limited to "criminal prosecutions," and Fla. Stat. ch. 394.9155(5) (2000) did not impermissibly invade the authority vested by Fla. Const. art. V, § 2(a), in the Florida Supreme Court to adopt rules for the practice and procedure in all courts. Although appellant's challenge to the jury instructions was rejected, a question was certified as to whether a specific jury instruction for the involuntary civil commitment of sexually violent predators was required.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the order committing appellant as a sexually violent predator under the Ryce Act, but certified a question to the Florida Supreme Court regarding jury instructions as one of great public importance.

 

1868 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Rodriguez v. State


CASE NO. 3D01-2332


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, THIRD DISTRICT


906 So. 2d 1082; 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 457; 29 Fla. L. Weekly D 241



January 21, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
Motion granted by Rodriguez v. State, 868 So. 2d 530, 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 19371 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 3d Dist., Feb. 27, 2004)
Affirmed by State v. Rodriguez, 920 So. 2d 624, 2005 Fla. LEXIS 1342 (Fla., June 23, 2005) Released for Publication July 26, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from the Circuit Court for Miami-Dade County, Jose M. Rodriguez, Judge. LOWER TRIBUNAL NO. 01-8689.
Rodriguez v. State, 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 11074 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 3d Dist., July 23, 2003)



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part and affirmed in part. Conflict certified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the Circuit Court for Miami-Dade County (Florida), which convicted him of, and sentenced him for, resisting an officer without violence, fleeing or attempting to elude a law enforcement officer, unlawful display of authorized indicia of law enforcement authority in violation of Fla. Stat. ch. 843.085, and reckless driving. Before the court was a motion for rehearing and clarification.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was observed by police driving recklessly on a motorcycle over 100 miles per hour while he was wearing a shirt with the word "POLICE" written on the front and back. Reversing in part, the court held that defendant's conviction for the unlawful display of authorized indicia of law enforcement authority pursuant to ch. 843.085(1) should be vacated because the statute was impermissibly content-based, overbroad, and proscribed conduct protected by Fla. Const. art. I, §§ 4 and 9 and the First and Fourteenth Amendments to the United States Constitution. However, defendant's remaining convictions were affirmed because (1) although the trial court abused its discretion when it permitted the State to elicit testimony from an officer about the behavior of a common class of criminals, the error was harmless; (2) the allegedly inflammatory statements of the prosecutor in closing arguments were made in response to a defense argument, and, thus, the claimed error was invited; and (3) although defendant's response to an officer as to why he did not stop the motorcycle should have been suppressed because it was the product of direct custodial interrogation, the error was harmless.


OUTCOME: The court granted rehearing and clarification, withdrew its previous opinion, and substituted this opinion, in which it reversed and vacated defendant's conviction and sentence for the unlawful display of authorized indicia of law enforcement authority but affirmed his convictions and sentences on the remaining counts. The court also certified a conflict with another district's decision.

 

1869 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Amerisure Ins. Co. v. State Farm Mut. Auto. Ins. Co.


Case No. 2D02-4757


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


865 So. 2d 590; 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 164; 29 Fla. L. Weekly D 219



January 14, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by Amerisure Ins. Co. v. State Farm Mut. Auto. Ins. Co., 884 So. 2d 21, 2004 Fla. LEXIS 1541 (Fla., 2004)
Later proceeding at Amerisure Ins. Co. v. State Farm Mut. Auto. Ins. Co., 886 So. 2d 226, 2004 Fla. LEXIS 1976 (Fla., 2004)
Approved by Amerisure Ins. Co. v. State Farm Mut. Auto. Ins. Co., 897 So. 2d 1287, 2005 Fla. LEXIS 484 (Fla., Mar. 17, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the County Court for Pinellas County; Henry J. Andringa, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed; conflict certified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant commercial insurer sought review from a grant of summary judgment in favor of appellee personal insurer by the County Court for Pinellas County (Florida) in the personal insurer's action for reimbursement under Fla. Stat. ch. 627.7405 (2001).


OVERVIEW: While driving a vehicle insured by the commercial insurer, the insured and her children were injured when they were struck by another vehicle. The insured received PIP payments from her personal insurer. The commercial insurer refused to reimburse the personal insurer under § 627.7405. On appeal, the commercial insurer claimed that § 627.7405 violated its equal protection rights. The appellate court held that the personal insurer was entitled to summary judgment. Section 627.7405 served the legitimate governmental purpose of reducing overall automobile insurance rates. The commercial insurer did not establish that there was no conceivable factual predicate that would rationally support the personal and commercial insurer classifications. Conflict was certified with a decision by the Court of Appeal of Florida, Third District.


OUTCOME: The grant of summary judgment was affirmed and conflict was certified.

Seitz v. State


CASE NO. 3D03-1628


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, THIRD DISTRICT


867 So. 2d 421; 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 175; 29 Fla. L. Weekly D 210



January 14, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 10, 2004.
Post-conviction relief granted at, Remanded by State v. Seitz, 935 So. 2d 541, 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 9423 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 3d Dist., June 14, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from the Circuit Court of Miami-Dade County, Rosa Rodriguez, Judge. LOWER TRIBUNAL CASE NO. 01-19972.



DISPOSITION: The order revoking Seitz' probation is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled no contest to five misdemeanor counts: battery, stalking, and several violations of a previously entered injunction protecting against repeat violence. Defendant was placed on probation. The State filed an affidavit of violation of probation which alleged that defendant engaged in stalking his victim by harassment. Defendant appealed the order of the Circuit Court of Miami-Dade County (Florida), which revoked his probation.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant argued that because he did not have any direct or indirect contact with the victim, the trial court abused its discretion by finding him guilty of stalking. The appellate court concluded that the stalking statute, Fla. Stat. ch. 784.048 (2001), did not require contact, direct or indirect, as a part of the offense of stalking. Defendant also argued that the trial court's application of the stalking statute to him was a due process violation, as nothing in the statute gave notice that his behavior would be considered a violation of the statute. The appellate court concluded that defendant's constitutional contentions had previously been rejected. Finally, defendant argued that the trial court had no jurisdiction to revoke the three consecutive probation terms that had not yet commenced. However, none of defendant's four consecutive probationary periods had expired prior to the process of revocation having been set in motion. In addition, because the trial court was free to revoke probation at any time for misconduct that demonstrated defendant's unfitness for probation, it was permissible to revoke the consecutive terms which had not yet commenced.


OUTCOME: The order revoking defendant's probation was affirmed.

 

1871 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Agency for Health Care Admin. v. HHCI Ltd. P'ship


CASE NO. 1D02-1588


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


865 So. 2d 593; 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 183; 29 Fla. L. Weekly D 237



January 14, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 1, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from an order of the Department of Administrative Hearings.



DISPOSITION: Vacated and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the Florida Agency for Healthcare Administration, sought review of an order of the Department of Administrative Hearings (Florida), which awarded appellee healthcare limited partnership all of its attorney's fees in the partnership's action that successfully challenged the Agency's non-rule policy. At issue, in part, was Fla. Stat. ch. 120.595(4) (2001).


OVERVIEW: The partnership operated several nursing home facilities. The Agency filed an administrative complaint seeking to revoke the licenses of the nursing homes, relying on a then-new statute, Fla. Stat. ch. 400.121(3) (2001). The partnership took the position that the Agency's action was illegal and devised a multi-pronged strategy to preserve the licenses. An administrative law judge (ALJ) ultimately determined that the Agency's actions violated Fla. Stat. ch. 120.54(1)(a) (2000), which generally provided that any agency statement defined as a rule had to be adopted by the Administrative Procedure Act's rulemaking procedure as soon as feasible. The partnership then sought its attorney's fees, not only for the successful challenge to the non-rule policy, but for all of the activities engaged in by its counsel. The ALJ awarded the partnership all of the fees requested. On appeal, the court held that, in light of the strict construction to be applied to attorney's fee statutes such as Fla. Stat. ch. 120.595(4) (2001), it was unable to uphold the award beyond fees that were incurred in the non-rule challenge.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the decision below and remanded the case. On remand, the ALJ was to determine what fees were recoverable under the court's reading of the statute. The ALJ was to exclude any fees expended to prove the amount, as opposed to the entitlement, of attorney's fees, as well as any fees incurred in proving entitlement to attorney's fees for efforts beyond the challenge. The costs were to bear a relationship to the non-rule challenge.

Ellis v. Burk


Case No. 5D03-371


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


866 So. 2d 1236; 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 75; 29 Fla. L. Weekly D 195



January 9, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 17, 2004.
Rehearing denied by Ellis v. Burk, 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 3785 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 5th Dist., Feb. 27, 2004)
Review denied by Ellis v. Burk, 879 So. 2d 621, 2004 Fla. LEXIS 1692 (Fla., June 16, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Brevard County, Kerry I. Evander, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants sought review of the final judgment of the Circuit Court for Brevard County (Florida), which declared Brevard County, Fla., Home Rule Charter § 5.4 to be inconsistent with Fla. Stat. chs. 129, 200, and therefore violative of Fla. Const. art. VIII, § 1(g).


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the issue was whether the tax cap provision contained in Brevard County, Fla., Home Rule Charter § 5.4 was inconsistent with Florida law governing the annual consideration and adoption of budgets and millage rates by county commissions. The appellate court found that the trial court correctly concluded that the charter provision was unconstitutional as being in conflict with Fla. Stat. chs. 129, 200, which set forth the statutory framework by which counties were to establish budgets and millage rates. Nothing in Fla. Stat. ch. 129 regarding the establishment of a budget, or in Fla. Stat. ch. 200 regarding the establishment of a millage rate, provided for a cap on the budget that could be overridden by a super-majority vote of county commissioners. To impose such a cap was contrary to the scheme established by the legislature. In addition, the charter provision providing for a referendum to override the ad valorem revenue cap in the event additional ad valorem revenues were deemed necessary by the county commission directly violated Fla. Stat. ch. 125.01(1)(r), which provided, inter alia, that no referendum was required for the levy by a county of ad valorem taxes.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

J.F. v. Dep't of Children & Families

January 7, 2004, Opinion Filed

Review granted by Fla. Dep't of Children & Families v. J.F., 876 So. 2d 561, 2004 Fla. LEXIS 1402 (Fla., 2004)
Vacated by, Remanded by Fla. Dep't of Children & Families v. J. F., 887 So. 2d 1200, 2004 Fla. LEXIS 1807 (Fla., Oct. 14, 2004)
Opinion withdrawn by, Substituted opinion at, Remanded by J.F. v. Dep't of Children & Families, 890 So. 2d 434, 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 20079 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., Dec. 29, 2004)

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother sought review from a judgment of the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County (Florida), which granted the petition of appellee social services department and terminated her parental rights over her two children.


OVERVIEW: One child was sheltered and adjudicated dependent, based on allegations that the mother's step-child was physically abused and died while in her care. The mother was convicted of manslaughter and child abuse for the step-child's death. After the mother's incarceration ended, she was offered a case plan. A neuropsychological study indicated that the mother was capable of reestablishing a relationship with her child. The department sought to terminate her rights. The trial court terminated her rights, finding that she did not take responsibility for the step-child's death, had anger-management problems, and did not substantially complete the case plan. On appeal, the court concluded that the department failed to present clear and convincing evidence to support the termination decision. The case plan was complete except for counseling, which was not due to the mother's fault. The other grounds asserted were inadequate to support termination under Fla. Stat. ch. 39.806 (2002).


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the trial court and remanded the matter for continuation of the children's dependency status.

B.C. v. Dep't of Children & Families


Case No. 5D03-1680


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


864 So. 2d 486; 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 16; 29 Fla. L. Weekly D 140



January 2, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 22, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Putnam County, Elizabeth A. Morris, Acting Circuit Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee Florida Department of Children and Families filed a petition for dependency in the Circuit Court for Putnam County (Florida). Appellant father, through counsel, denied the petition for dependency, while the mother consented to the petition. The trial court adjudicated the father's two children to be dependent. The father appealed.


OVERVIEW: At an arraignment hearing, the trial court accepted the mother's consent to and the father's denial to the petition, and withheld adjudication of dependency. A week prior to the disposition hearing, the trial court entered a written order from the earlier arraignment hearing. The written order stated that based on the mother's consent, the court found the children to be dependent within the intent and meaning of Fla. Stat. ch. 39.01(14)(a) (2003). Thus, the written order did not withhold adjudication of dependency, as was agreed at the arraignment hearing. The father argued that the trial court's written order of dependency did not conform to the court's oral pronouncement. He also contended that ch. 39.01(14)(a) was not intended to allow children to be found dependent when the allegations were against only one parent and there existed another fit non-offending parent willing to assume custody. On appeal, the court remanded the matter to the trial court to the extent that the order needed clarification. As a non-offending parent, the father was entitled to placement at disposition unless the placement was shown to endanger the children. Fla. Stat. ch. 39.521 (2003).


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, and the matter was remanded with instructions to conform the written order to the court's oral pronouncement. On remand, the father was free to question the constitutionality of the statute, as applied to him.

Certain Interested Underwriters at Lloyd's London v. City of St. Petersburg


Case Nos. 2D03-1616, 2D03-1916, CONSOLIDATED


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


864 So. 2d 1145; 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 19781; 29 Fla. L. Weekly D 80



December 31, 2003, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Certain Interested Underwriters at Lloyd's London v. City of St. Petersburg, 871 So. 2d 872, 2004 Fla. LEXIS 451 (Fla., Mar. 17, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Pinellas County; John C. Lenderman, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Pinellas County (Florida) held that neither the U.S. Constitution nor the Florida Constitution supported a cause of action filed under the Takings Clause when the police destroyed private property insured by appellant insurer while executing a valid search warrant. The insurer appealed.


OVERVIEW: The insurer challenged the judgment granting appellee city's motion to dismiss the insurer's subrogation action seeking recovery of funds it paid to a property owner, its insured, under the Takings Clause of both the Florida and U.S. Constitution. However, the appeals court agreed that the type of destruction suffered was not historically a compensable taking under either state or federal law. Instead, the appeals court agreed that only when the government's actors caused damage as a result of their negligence or misconduct did the property owner have redress through a tort action or a legislative claims bill. Thus, the appeals court concluded that the only redress that the insurer had was in tort.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Adams v. State


Case No. 2D02-4925


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


869 So. 2d 579; 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 19264; 29 Fla. L. Weekly D 14



December 19, 2003, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication April 6, 2005. Reversed by, Remanded by State v. Henderson, 894 So. 2d 266, 2005 Fla. LEXIS 266 (Fla., Feb. 17, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Hillsborough County; Ronald Ficarrotta, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Convictions affirmed; minimum sentence stricken; conflicts certified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Hillsborough County (Florida) convicted defendant of conspiracy to traffic in heroin and trafficking in heroin, and sentenced him thereon. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was sentenced as a habitual offender to concurrent terms of 30 years' imprisonment, and received a 15-year mandatory minimum sentence for trafficking in heroin under Fla. Stat. ch. 893.135(1)(c)(1)(b) (2001). However, the mandatory minimum sentencing provision, added by 1999 Fla. Laws 188, was declared unconstitutional as a violation of the single subject requirement in the Taylor case. Further, subsequent reenactments of these provisions could not be retroactively applied without violating the Ex Post Facto Clauses in the United States and Florida Constitutions. Because the date of the offenses defendant committed fell within the Taylor window, the mandatory minimum sentence was reversed.


OUTCOME: The convictions were affirmed, the mandatory minimum sentence was stricken, and conflicts were certified.

Jones v. State


CASE NO. 4D02-294


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


861 So. 2d 1261; 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 19218; 29 Fla. L. Weekly D 4



December 17, 2003, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 6, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County; James I. Cohn, Judge; L.T. Case No. 01-4729 CF 10.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from his conviction by the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County (Florida), and from his mandatory life sentence without the possibility of parole for sexual battery on a child under 12 years old.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court erred by designating him a prison releasee reoffender under the Florida Prison Releasee Reoffender Act, specifically Fla. Stat. ch. 775.082(9)(a)(3), because he was convicted of a capital offense rather than a life felony. The appellate court held that the offense could be treated as non-capital for the purpose of applying ch. 775.082(9)(a). It was inconceivable that the legislature did not intend capital sexual battery, as a felony punishable by life, to fall within the scope of the Act. The appellate court also rejected defendant's contention that his sentence violated the federal and state constitutional prohibitions against cruel and unusual punishment. Merely because defendant's sentence was mandatory and severe, it did not follow that it violated the Eighth Amendment. The legislature's imposition of a mandatory life sentence without the possibility of parole for the offense was not out of sync with Florida's historic treatment of sexual battery of a child. Further, the treatment of the crime of capital sexual battery in other jurisdictions was not so out of line as to render the punishment under Florida law unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The conviction and sentence were affirmed.

T. P. v. Dep't of Children & Families (In the Interest of D.B.)


Case No. 5D02-3671


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


860 So. 2d 1084; 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 18798; 28 Fla. L. Weekly D 2868



December 12, 2003, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication December 31, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Putnam County, A. W. Nichols III, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother appealed from an order entered by the Circuit Court for Putnam County (Florida) terminating her parental rights at the request of appellee Florida Department of Children and Families (DCF).


OVERVIEW: The mother argued that she had made substantial changes since her parental rights to her other children were terminated due to child abuse, which resulted in the death of her baby. The appellate court held she failed to show that the conduct that led to termination of parental rights to her other children could not serve as a predictor of her conduct with the instant child. The mother's claim that it was the DCF's fault that she did not pay child support was rejected, as there was no evidence that the DCF interfered with her employment. Going to church and feeling pain from the loss of her children were not examples of substantial changes that would support any conclusion other than the one reached by the trial court. Conflict with the Fourth District Court of Appeal as to the constitutionality of Fla. Stat. ch. 39.806(1)(i) was certified, as were questions as to the standard used to analyze issues under that statute.

Sarasota County v. Curry


Case No. 2D03-2015


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


861 So. 2d 1239; 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 18808; 28 Fla. L. Weekly D 2875



December 12, 2003, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Sarasota County; Andrew D. Owens, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county sought review of an award by the Circuit Court for Sarasota County (Florida) of attorney's fees under Fla. Stat. ch. 73.092(1) (1995) to appellee landowner in an eminent domain action after three potential landowners apportioned a stipulated final judgment, jointly awarded all three potential landowners, among themselves.


OVERVIEW: The county argued that if the offer of judgment was a written offer, the landowner was not entitled to attorney's fees under ch. 73.092(1), as the benefit to the landowner was zero. The appellate court held that the offer of judgment was a written offer. The landowner received $ 7,666 from the stipulated final judgment, but the record did not reflect how much of the offer was intended for the landowner. As the benefits to the landowner were impossible to ascertain, the trial court abused its discretion in awarding the landowner attorney's fees under ch. 73.092(1). Instead, the trial court should have based its attorney's fee award on ch. 73.092(2), which provided factors for consideration in assessing attorney's fees. While a plain language reading of that subsection suggested that it was inapplicable, as the underlying action was not a supplemental proceeding, the appellate court had held that ch. 73.092(2) governed awards of attorney's fees in all eminent domain proceedings in which the condemning authority failed to make a written offer to settle the claim or which otherwise could not be resolved using the benefits analysis in ch. 73.092(1).


OUTCOME: The order was reversed. The case was remanded for reconsideration of the attorney's fees issue. On remand, the landowner was not limited to the amount of fees requested in her motion for attorney's fees.

Gillman v. State

DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment by the Circuit Court for Levy County (Florida) that denied his motion to dismiss an information charging him with driving a motor vehicle while his driver's license was permanently revoked, in violation of Fla. Stat. ch. 322.341. Defendant claimed that the statute was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: After defendant was convicted of violating § 322.341, the state supreme court held that 1998 Fla. Laws ch. 223 violated the single subject rule of Fla. Const. art. III, § 6. Thereafter, the legislature reenacted the provision as part of the biennial adoption of the Florida statutes. However, defendant was convicted before the reenactment became effective. The appellate court held that because defendant could not lawfully be charged under an unconstitutional statute, the order denying his motion to dismiss had to be reversed.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and remanded with instructions.

Bush v. Schiavo


Case No. 2D03-5244


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


861 So. 2d 506; 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 18702; 28 Fla. L. Weekly D 2825



December 10, 2003, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication January 16, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] Petition for Writ of Prohibition to the Circuit Court for Pinellas County; W. Douglas Baird, Judge.
Schindler v. Schiavo (In re Schiavo), 851 So. 2d 182, 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 8342 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2d Dist., 2003)



DISPOSITION: Writ of prohibition denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner Governor of the State of Florida filed a petition for a writ of prohibition to the Circuit Court for Pinellas County (Florida), challenging the trial court's denial of the Governor's motion to disqualify the trial judge from presiding over further proceedings in connection with the challenge to the constitutionality of 2003 Fla. Laws ch. 418 brought by respondent husband, as guardian of his wife.


OVERVIEW: The Governor argued that the trial judge was biased as he characterized ch. 418 as presumptively unconstitutional. The appellate court held that the statement announced the standard by which the trial judge believed the constitutionality of the statute was to be measured. The appellate court had held that the courts were attempting to honor the wife's constitutional right of privacy as it affected her medical decisions, and a legislative act impinging on the right of privacy was presumptively unconstitutional unless proved valid by the State. The trial judge's reference to the infringement upon the wife's rights was part of his legal analysis and was made in support of his decision to lift the automatic stay. The Governor's claim that the trial judge had prejudged the case by concluding that the wife's right of privacy was invaded by the legislation, in view of legal precedent so holding, did not show bias. Finally, the trial judge did not signal his predisposition to rule against the Governor by consulting notes when he ruled. The Governor was able to fully argue his position, and the trial judge took a recess after the arguments were concluded to consider his decision.


OUTCOME: The petition for writ of prohibition was denied with prejudice.

Burger v. Burger


Case No. 2D02-4944


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


862 So. 2d 828; 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 18710; 28 Fla. L. Weekly D 2817



December 10, 2003, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Burger v. Burger, 872 So. 2d 898, 2004 Fla. LEXIS 563 (Fla., Apr. 2, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Polk County; J. Michael Hunter, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother appealed from an order entered by the Circuit Court for Polk County (Florida) transferring primary residential custody of her eight-year-old son to appellee father, and from a temporary order awarding custody to intervenor maternal grandmother.


OVERVIEW: The mother argued that the father failed to meet his burden under the Gibbs test. The appellate court held that the trial court abused its discretion in modifying custody. The circumstances had not substantially changed since the original custody order was entered. The mother and her son were living with the maternal grandmother when the original order was entered. The only proof as to a change in circumstances was evidence of positive changes in the mother's financial stability and in her receipt of treatment for her drug problem. The father failed to prove that his son had witnessed domestic violence to his mother. Second, the best interests of the child were not clearly served by a custody change. The trial court assumed, without evidence to support its assumption, that continuing to reside with the mother would be detrimental to the child. The trial court failed to reference any ascertainable indication that the child was suffering any harm as required by Jacoby and its progeny. The child was performing well in school, enjoyed normal activities, was close to his half-sister, and appeared to be surrounded by love.


OUTCOME: The order modifying custody and the temporary order awarding custody to the maternal grandmother and requiring the mother to have supervised visitation were reversed. The case was remanded to the trial court to enter an order vacating the order granting the father's petition to modify custody and reaffirming the mother's custody as established in the final judgment of dissolution of marriage.

 

1887 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


DeJesus v. State


CASE NO. 4D02-2699


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


862 So. 2d 847; 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 18728; 28 Fla. L. Weekly D 2845



December 10, 2003, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County; Marvin U. Mounts, Judge; L.T. Case No. 01-0009245-CF-A02.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the denial by the Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County (Florida), of his motion to declare Fla. Stat. ch. 943.0435 (2002), the sexual offender statute, unconstitutional, following his entry into a negotiated plea, which included both youthful offender and sex offender probation.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that ch. 943.0435 violated his procedural due process and privacy rights. The appellate court joined other appellate courts' decisions and held that the statute was constitutional. Further, the more restrictive sexual predator statute had withstood a similar constitutional challenge. Defendant did not preserve for appeal his claim that the sexual offender statute could not be applied to him because he was sentenced as a juvenile under the youthful offender statute as defendant did not file a timely motion to withdraw his guilty plea. Further, the youthful offender sentence was an adult sentence. Defendant's argument that because Fla. Stat. ch. 944.607(9) (2002) provided for the offender to register according to Fla. Stat. ch. 943.0435(3) (2002), and that section did not require registration until 48 hours after being released from supervision, defendant should not have to register until he was released from probation, was rejected. Such an interpretation ignored the plain language of the statutes and the clear intent of the legislature. The reference to "release" in ch. 943.0435(3) was for offenders serving prison time, not for those on probation.


OUTCOME: The conviction and sentence were affirmed.

 

1888 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Tate v. State


CASE NO. 4D01-1306


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


864 So. 2d 44; 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 18750; 28 Fla. L. Weekly D 2853



December 10, 2003, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
Rehearing denied by State v. Tate, 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 2309 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., Feb. 12, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County; Joel Lazarus, Judge; L.T. Case No. 99-14401 CF10A.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from his conviction by the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County (Florida), of first-degree murder and the resulting mandatory sentence to life in prison, challenging the denial of his post-trial request for a competency hearing, and challenging the trial court's failure to order, sua sponte, a pre-trial competency evaluation. Defendant also challenged the denial of his motion for a new trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the refusal to order a competency hearing violated his due process rights. The appellate court held that due to defendant's extremely young age and lack of previous exposure to the judicial system, a competency evaluation was constitutionally mandated to determine whether defendant had sufficient present ability to consult with his lawyer with a reasonable degree of rational understanding and whether he had a rational, as well as factual, understanding of the proceedings against him. A competency evaluation was required, particularly due to the complexity of the legal proceedings and the fact that defendant was denied the protection afforded children 14 and older under Fla. Stat. ch. 985.226(2). The plea colloquy was not adequate to evaluate competency given defendant's age, immaturity, his nine or 10-year-old mental age, and the complexity of the proceedings. The trial court's reasoning was insufficient to override the testimony regarding defendant's reduced mental functioning, his possible inability to understand the charges and decisions to be made, the potential penalty, and the professional opinion that a competency evaluation and hearing was necessary.


OUTCOME: The conviction was reversed and the case was remanded. Upon remand, defendant was entitled to a new trial.

 

1889 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Fla. Dep't of Revenue v. Howard


CASE NO. 1D02-3762


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


859 So. 2d 619; 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 18069; 28 Fla. L. Weekly D 2735



November 26, 2003, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication December 12, 2003.
Reversed by, Remanded by Fla. Dep't of Revenue v. Howard, 916 So. 2d 640, 2005 Fla. LEXIS 1358 (Fla., June 30, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from the Circuit Court for Leon County. P. Kevin Davey, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Leon County Circuit Court (Florida) found that only a portion of Fla. Stat. ch. 193.016 was unconstitutional. Both appellant, the Department of Revenue, and appellees, county appraisers and two individual litigants, sought further review.


OVERVIEW: The issue presented was whether Fla. Stat. ch. 193.016 violated the uniform valuation requirement of Fla. Const. art. VII, § 4. The appeals court first held that the statute prescribed a valuation methodology applicable to only a special class of tangible personal property. While the trial court was correct that the first sentence of the statute merely required the property appraiser to consider the prior year tangible personal property assessment reduction made by the value adjustment board, the mandated consideration was an essential component of the valuation methodology for this special class of property. Second, the legislature was authorized to add to or modify to the list of factors found in the statute to be considered by the property appraiser when determining valuations for all types of property. However, except in circumstances specified in Fla. Const. art. VII, § 4, and not present in the instant case, it could not provide additional or different factors which were applicable to only a limited class of property. Because this was the effect of both sentences of the statute, it violated the Florida constitution.


OUTCOME: The judgment that found the second sentence of the statute was unconstitutional was affirmed, but that part of the judgment which held the first sentence was not constitutional was reversed.

 

1890 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Dep't of Revenue v. City of Gainesville


CASE NO. 1D02-1582


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


859 So. 2d 595; 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 18074; 28 Fla. L. Weekly D 2724



November 26, 2003, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication December 12, 2003. As Corrected December 18, 2003. Second Correction December 19, 2003.
Reversed by, Remanded by Fla. Dep't of Revenue v. City of Gainesville, 918 So. 2d 250, 2005 Fla. LEXIS 2507 (Fla., Dec. 8, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from the Circuit Court for Leon County. Nikki Ann Clark, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The decision of the trial court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Leon County Circuit Court (Florida) granted summary judgment to appellee city, and against appellant, the Department of Revenue, in the city's declaratory judgment action. The Department appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court declared facially unconstitutional 1997 Fla. Laws ch. 197, § 2, creating Fla. Stat. ch. 166.047, which imposed ad valorem taxes on property owned and used by a municipality to provide telecommunications services, because the statute contravened Fla. Const. art. VII, § 3(a). For the same reason, the trial court also declared facially invalid a portion of 1997 Fla. Laws ch. 197(3), which amended Fla. Stat. ch. 196.012, to provide that a municipality's provision of two-way telecommunications services to the public did not constitute an exempt use for ad valorem tax purposes unless the services complied with certain conditions therein specified. On appeal, the court believed that the property in question was being used by the city for a municipal purpose and the legislature's attempt to condition the provision of these municipal services on the payment of an amount equal to any ad valorem tax liability was in direct conflict with Fla. Const. art. VII, § 3(a). The court also found the argument that the provisions of the act merely outlined a condition for the provision of telecommunication services was unpersuasive.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1891 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Therrien v. State


CASE NO. 1D01-3403


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


859 So. 2d 585; 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 18005; 28 Fla. L. Weekly D 2704



November 25, 2003, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication December 11, 2003.
Review granted by Therrien v. State, 888 So. 2d 625, 2004 Fla. LEXIS 2220 (Fla., 2004)
Reversed by, Remanded by Therrien v. State, 914 So. 2d 942, 2005 Fla. LEXIS 2055 (Fla., Oct. 27, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from a final order from the circuit court for Escambia County. John P. Kuder, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED. QUESTION CERTIFIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Escambia County (Florida) entered a post-judgment order designating defendant as a sexual predator, pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 775.21 (2000), as amended. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged the judgment entered, arguing that the Florida Sexual Predator Act, Fla. Stat. ch. 775.21 (2000), violated separation of powers and procedural due process requirements. The appeals court held that defendant's conviction was the only material fact necessary for the imposition of the Act. He did not challenge the hearing afforded on his plea nor the opportunity allowed to contest his conviction. Second, he was not entitled to a separate hearing to prove that he did not pose a danger or threat to society. Third, the only material fact for imposition of the employment restrictions was defendant's conviction of an offense involving a minor. Fourth, the presumption of prospective application did not apply where the legislature clearly stated an intent that the Act apply retroactively. Finally, the following question was certified as one of great importance: whether the retroactive application of the permanent employment restrictions of Fla. Stat. ch. 775.21(10)(b) (2000) to a defendant convicted and qualified as a sexual predator, without a separate hearing on whether such defendant constituted a danger or threat to public safety, violated procedural due process.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed and the court certified a question of great importance.
