1893 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Hernandez-Molina v. State


CASE NO. 4D03-215


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


860 So. 2d 483; 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 18368; 28 Fla. L. Weekly D 2656



November 19, 2003, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 19, 2003.
Review denied by Hernandez-Molina v. State, 2005 Fla. LEXIS 218 (Fla., Jan. 31, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal of order denying rule 3.800(a) motion from the Circuit Court for the Nineteenth Judicial Circuit, Martin County; Robert Makemson, Judge; L.T. Case No. 00-1451 CFA.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate pled no contest to trafficking in cocaine in excess of 200 grams, and received a seven-year mandatory minimum sentence. He brought a motion to correct an illegal sentence, arguing that amendments to Fla. Stat. ch. 893.135 (1999) violated the single subject provision of Fla. Const. art. III, § 6. The Circuit Court, Nineteenth Judicial Circuit, Martin County, Florida, denied the motion, and the inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: The inmate argued that the amendment at issue, 1999 Fla. Laws ch. 188, violated the single subject provision of Florida's Constitution because it included unrelated provisions. The supreme court initially held that retroactive application of a cure to a single subject violation was contrary to the Ex Post Facto Clauses of both the United States and Florida Constitutions, and receded from its published opinions relying on Hersey v. State, 831 So. 2d 679 (Fla. 5th DCA 2002). The title of ch. 188 -- "An act relating to sentencing" -- was not defective or misleading, as it fully informed of the provisions of the law. Noting that the single subject constitutional provision had to be liberally construed, the supreme court held that ch. 188 was constitutional. It was not an example of legislative logrolling. There was no suggestion that any of the provisions of the law would not have passed had they been introduced in separate bills. All of its provisions dealt with criminal law, were all logically related, and furthered the purpose of the law, which was to protect the public from serious felony offenders.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed the judgment of the trial court denying the inmate's motion to correct an illegal sentence.

Stav v. State


CASE NO. 4D00-4370


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


860 So. 2d 478; 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 17085; 28 Fla. L. Weekly D 2601



November 12, 2003, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Stav v. State, 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 20193 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., Dec. 31, 2003)
Review denied by Stav v. State, 2004 Fla. LEXIS 507 (Fla., Mar. 22, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County; Marvin U. Mounts, Jr., Judge; L.T. Case No. 98-6486 CFA02S.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART, and REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County (Florida), which convicted him of organized scheme to defraud and grand theft greater than $ 20,000 and less than $ 100,000 and which sentenced him to concurrent 42.5 month sentences on both convictions.


OVERVIEW: Defendant worked for a travel agency, and the agency became aware that defendant had booked some vacation packages without the authority to do so and terminated defendant. Defendant's records were then audited, resulting in the criminal charges against him. On appeal, the court found error only as to the double jeopardy issue, finding that the two crimes shared common elements and the State conceded the violation. The court held, however, that the organized scheme to defraud conviction and defendant's sentence were proper. The court determined that evidence of prior acts of defendant was properly admitted under the Williams rule to show that defendant engaged in a plan to defraud employers because at both this job and a prior job, defendant had used discount coupons that altered the cost of airline tickets and caused the travel agencies to be charged for any unaccounted airfare. The court also held that defendant's sentence was not in error because although the departure was based on the 1995 sentencing guidelines, which had been held unconstitutional in Heggs, the economic motive reason cited by the trial court was applicable under both the 1994 and 1995 sentencing guidelines.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the grand theft conviction and sentence and remanded for discharge, and it affirmed the organized scheme to defraud conviction and sentence.

State v. Veilleux


Case Nos. 2D02-3226, 2D02-3256


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


859 So. 2d 1224; 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 16953; 28 Fla. L. Weekly D 2568



November 7, 2003, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Veilleux, 880 So. 2d 1212, 2004 Fla. LEXIS 1116 (Fla., July 12, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Writ of Certiorari to the Circuit Court for Pinellas County; Nelly N. Khouzam, Judge. Opinion Substituted for Opinion dated July 30, 2003 reported at:.
State v. Veilleux, 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 11415 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2d Dist., July 30, 2003)



DISPOSITION: Writ of certiorari. denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State filed a motion for rehearing and certification of its petition, seeking a writ of certiorari and an order quashing the interlocutory pretrial order of the Circuit Court for Pinellas County (Florida), which granted respondent's motion in limine.


OVERVIEW: Respondent was stopped by police for driving a stolen vehicle and he identified himself by a false name and signed traffic citations by that name. He was charged with forgery in violation of Fla. Stat. ch. 831.01 (2002), and the trial court granted respondent's motion in limine to exclude the forged traffic citations pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 316.650(9) (2002) and Dixon. The trial court indicated that it was bound by the case law precedent, which appeared to be the only case directly on point. On rehearing of the State's petition for writ of certiorari, the court found that Fla. Stat. ch. 316.650(9) was unambiguous and did not provide any exceptions for the admissibility of traffic citations. Following principles of statutory interpretation, the court felt bound by the prior determination and by the statutory language. Accordingly, it found that the forged traffic citations were not admissible. There was nothing in ch. 316.650(9) which was unconstitutional or that violated clearly established law, and accordingly, the certiorari review would not have yielded a different result. The court certified a question to the supreme court on the admissibility of such citations.


OUTCOME: The court granted the motion for rehearing in part and denied it in part. The court withdrew its prior opinion and in substituting the new opinion, the court denied the petition for writ of certiorari. The court certified a question to the supreme court.

Smiley v. State


Case No. 2D01-5228


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


870 So. 2d 59; 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 16955; 28 Fla. L. Weekly D 2559



November 7, 2003, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication April 6, 2005. Reversed by, Remanded by State v. Henderson, 894 So. 2d 266, 2005 Fla. LEXIS 266 (Fla., Feb. 17, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Polk County; J. Tim Strickland, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Polk County (Florida), which convicted her of trafficking in methamphetamine and imposed a sentence of a minimum mandatory term of seven years' imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was sentenced for conviction of trafficking in methamphetamine pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 893.135(l)(f)(l)(b) (1999). During the pendency of the appeal, she filed a motion to correct sentence under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.800(b)(2), based on her assertion that her sentence was improper pursuant to Taylor v. State, as the sentencing statute had been declared unconstitutional and the newly enacted provision could not be applied retroactively. The court noted that since appellant's offense was committed during the "Taylor window period," her sentence should not have included the seven-year minimum mandatory term. The trial court denied her motion, noting that her sentence was final when it was entered. However, on appeal, the court found that the sentence was not final, as determined by the trial court, because her appeal which challenged the sentence was still pending. Accordingly, her motion was not a postconviction motion under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.800(a), but rather, it was a motion to preserve the sentencing issue for review in the direct appeal. Accordingly, judicial precedent applied and resentencing was mandated. The court certified a conflict with other districts.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction, but reversed the sentence and remanded for resentencing.

1899 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Yasir v. Singletary


Case No. 5D02-2344


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


861 So. 2d 460; 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 16518; 28 Fla. L. Weekly D 2490



October 31, 2003, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 16, 2004.
Rehearing denied by Yasir v. Singletary, 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 20383 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 5th Dist., Dec. 30, 2003)
Review denied by Yasir v. Crosby, 873 So. 2d 1226, 2004 Fla. LEXIS 739 (Fla., Apr. 26, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Marion County, Jack Singbush, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The St. Johns Court for Osceola County (Florida) denied appellant inmate's request to reopen a lawsuit for the purpose of obtaining a refund of copy fees. The inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: The inmate filed a lawsuit against defendant, the head of the Florida Department of Corrections. Pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 57.085(7) (1997), the inmate was required to provide the court with copies of his previous civil actions. He paid to obtain copies of those documents and then he attached them to his pleading. But, subsequently, that statute was declared unconstitutional, as it denied certain prisoners access to the courts. Thereafter, all inmates whose cases had been dismissed for failure to comply with the copy requirement would have two years from the date of the decision within which to file motions seeking reinstatement of their claims. The trial court then denied the instant motion to reopen, leading to this appeal. The appeals court held that the case which held § 57.085(7) unconstitutional specifically applied only to those inmates whose cases were dismissed for failure to comply with the copy requirement to file a motion seeking reinstatement. The inmate herein did not fall within that definition. In fact, he provided the necessary copies and made payment therefor. Accordingly, the trial court properly concluded that he was not entitled to reopen his case.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1900 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Envtl. Confederation of Southwest Fla., Inc. v. IMC Phosphates, Inc.


CASE NO. 1D03-1717


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


857 So. 2d 207; 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 16124; 28 Fla. L. Weekly D 2468



October 28, 2003, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication November 13, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal of an order of the Department of Environmental Protection.
Envtl. Confederation of Southwest Fla., Inc. v. IMC Phosphates, Inc., 857 So. 2d 207, 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 11571 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., 2003)



DISPOSITION: Rehearing denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellees, a company and an environmental agency, moved for rehearing of appellant corporations' appeal of the agency's order; the company claimed that the decision conflicted with a recent decision concerning the constitutionality of a statute.


OVERVIEW: The statute was employed to deny the corporations the right to initiate a challenge to a proposed permit. The appellate court held that the prior case dealt with the constitutionality of the statute in a declaratory judgment context. In contrast, the corporations' appeal involved a use of a statute at a time when it was alleged to be unconstitutional. The company's argument that the appeal was moot was presented for the first time in its motion for rehearing. The mootness argument could have been made much earlier. As a result, the company was not in a position to seek rehearing under Fla. R. App. P. 9.330 on the ground that the court overlooked or misunderstood its argument; the argument simply was not made. The agency referred only to matters that were properly before the court, but it did not reveal any error in the decision. Accordingly, neither party was entitled to a rehearing.


OUTCOME: The motions for rehearing were denied.

 

1901 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Fla. Pub. Emples. Council 79 v. Bush


CASE NO. 1D02-2087


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


860 So. 2d 992; 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 15704; 28 Fla. L. Weekly D 2636



October 22, 2003, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication December 30, 2003.
Rehearing denied by Fla. Pub. Emples. Council 79 v. Bush, 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 20187 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., Dec. 10, 2003)
Remanded by Fla. Pub. Emples. Council 79 v. State, 921 So. 2d 676, 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 658 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., Jan. 24, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from the Circuit Court for Leon County. Judge Kevin Davey.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant public employees union filed suit to challenge the "Service First" initiative, 2001 Fla. Laws ch. 043, and elements of the 2001 General Appropriations Act. The Circuit Court for Leon County, Florida, dismissed four counts of the complaint; granted summary judgment to appellee, the Florida Governor, as to three other counts; and denied the union's cross-motion for summary judgment. The union appealed.


OVERVIEW: The union was the certified bargaining agent for certain state employees, and the Governor was the employees' statutory public employer. After negotiations for a collective bargaining agreement foundered, the legislature passed ch. 043, which amended provisions of Fla. Stat. chs. 110, 216, and 447, and included proviso language in the General Appropriations Act regarding certain collective bargaining issues at impasse. The appellate court held that count I was properly dismissed, as (1) its allegations that the legislature acted improperly should have been resolved in the action it filed against that body, and (2) its allegations that the Governor acted improperly stated an alleged unfair labor practice subject to the jurisdiction of the Florida Public Employees Relations Commission. The trial judge's dismissal of count VI, on grounds the union sustained no definable or specific injury, was proper. However, as neither the State's last offer to the union nor the challenged proviso language of the General Appropriations Act was related to any specific appropriation, the proviso language clearly violated Fla. Const. art. III, § 12, and the trial court erred in dismissing count III.


OUTCOME: The grant of summary judgment to the Governor, dismissing the count alleging that the challenged proviso language of the General Appropriations Act violated the Florida Constitution, was reversed. Dismissal of the other counts was affirmed.

Henry v. State


Case No. 2D02-182


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


857 So. 2d 344; 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 15800; 28 Fla. L. Weekly D 2448



October 22, 2003, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication November 12, 2003.
Reversed by, Remanded by State v. Henderson, 2005 Fla. LEXIS 266 (Fla., Feb. 17, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Polk County; J. Tim Strickland, Judge. Opinion Substituted for Opinion dated July 18, 2003 reported at
Henry v. State, 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 10881 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2d Dist., July 18, 2003)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part; remanded for resentencing; conflicts certified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment by the Circuit Court for Polk County (Florida) that convicted and sentenced him for multiple offenses arising from his attack on several correctional officers; the State moved for certification of conflict.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted, inter alia, of attempted second-degree murder and aggravated battery of a law enforcement officer in violation of Fla. Stat. chs. 782.04(2), 777.04, 784.07(2) (1999). He was sentenced as a prison release reoffender (PRR) under Fla. Stat. ch. 775.082(9)(a)(2) (1999). The appellate court held that because the use of a weapon was not an essential element of the crimes of attempted second-degree murder or aggravated battery, the enhancements were proper. A scrivener's error in the written judgment could be corrected on remand. However, the trial court erred by sentencing defendant as a PRR because the amendment that created § 775.082(9)(a)(2) was an unconstitutional violation of the single subject rule. Defendant's sentences were affected by the amendments and fell within the window period. The appellate court certified conflict with contrary holdings.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction was affirmed; the judgment of sentence was reversed and remanded for resentencing.

Espindola v. State


CASE NO. 3D02-1839


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, THIRD DISTRICT


855 So. 2d 1281; 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 15797; 28 Fla. L. Weekly D 2406



October 22, 2003, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Later proceeding at Milks v. State, 881 So. 2d 1113, 2004 Fla. LEXIS 1332 (Fla., 2004)
Reversed by, Sub nomine at Milks v. State, 894 So. 2d 924, 2005 Fla. LEXIS 150 (Fla., Feb. 3, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An appeal from the Circuit Court for Miami-Dade County, Manuel A. Crespo, Judge. LOWER TRIBUNAL NO. 01-38819.
Espindola v. State, 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 270 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 3d Dist., Jan. 15, 2003)



DISPOSITION: Reversed, rehearing denied and conflict certified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Miami-Dade County, Florida, declared defendant, a convicted sex offender, to be a "sexual predator" in accordance with the Florida Sexual Predator Act (FSPA), Fla. Stat. ch. 775.21 (1999). The trial court rejected defendant's contention that FSPA was unconstitutional. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and his accomplice had sexual intercourse with an unconscious woman in a hotel room to which they had taken her. Defendant pled guilty to multiple perpetrator sexual battery; since this would have automatically resulted in defendant's being declared a "sexual predator" under FSPA, he moved for a declaration that FSPA was unconstitutional as violative of procedural due process. The appellate court noted that once an offender was designated a "sexual predator," the registration and public notification requirements of FSPA were automatically triggered. Being publicly labeled a "sexual predator" clearly resulted in a stigma; and under the "stigma-plus test," the restrictions on the types of employment a "sexual predator" could have, coupled with the stigma, resulted in an infringement on a constitutionally-protected liberty interest. The total failure of FSPA to provide for a judicial hearing on the risk of defendant's committing future offenses made it violative of procedural due process, and therefore unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed, denied rehearing, and certified conflict with a decision of an appellate court from a different district.

1906 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Dep't of Highway Safety & Motor Vehicles v. Bailey


Case No. 2D03-1735


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


870 So. 2d 47; 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 15645; 28 Fla. L. Weekly D 2384



October 17, 2003, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Writ of Certiorari to the Circuit Court for the Twelfth Judicial Circuit for Sarasota County; sitting in its appellate capacity.



DISPOSITION: Writ of certiorari granted, order quashed, and case remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner Highway Department (Department) sought a writ of certiorari from the court (Idaho) to quash a circuit court order determining that the administrative hearing officer had insufficient evidence to deny respondent applicant's request for a hardship driving permit and ordering the Department to reinstate the applicant's license. The Department asserted several errors on appeal.


OVERVIEW: The applicant's license was permanently revoked after he acquired four convictions for driving under the influence. The applicant later sought a hardship driving permit from the Department, but the Department denied the request. The circuit court ordered the Department to reinstate the applicant's license, finding that there was insufficient evidence to deny the application. The court granted the Department a writ of certiorari and quashed the order. Specifically, the court held that the circuit court exceeded its scope of certiorari review by ordering the Department to reinstate the applicant's license. The circuit court's review was limited to whether the hearing officer afforded the applicant due process, observed the essential requirements of the law, and whether the administrative findings were supported by competent, substantial evidence. On remand, the circuit court had to determine, in light of the criteria set out in Fla. Stat. ch. 322.271(4) (1997), whether the hearing officer's findings were supported by competent, substantial evidence and whether, in light of those findings, the hearing officer abused his discretion in denying the applicant's hardship permit.


OUTCOME: The court granted the Department a writ of certiorari and quashed the circuit court's order. The court remanded the case for further proceedings.

Tatum v. State


Case No. 2D02-177


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


857 So. 2d 331; 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 15447; 28 Fla. L. Weekly D 2380



October 15, 2003, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication November 4, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Pinellas County; Nancy Moate Ley, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part and remanded for a new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Circuit Court for Pinellas County (Florida) of violating the Florida Racketeer Influenced and Corrupt Organization Act (RICO), Fla. Stat. ch. 895.01-.06 (1997). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant operated a pawn shop. The RICO conviction was based on predicate acts of conspiring to deal in stolen property or dealing in stolen property; undercover officers sold merchandise on various occasions to either defendant or an employee as part of a sting operation. The trial court gave a special jury instruction that tracked the language of Fla. Stat. ch. 812.022(4) (1997), which allowed the jury to infer defendant's knowledge as to whether the property was stolen. Defendant argued that the instruction violated his due process rights by creating a mandatory rebuttable presumption of guilt, but the court found instead that no factual predicate was laid for the instruction. As defendant did not participate in all of the transactions, it was error to instruct the jury under ch. 812.022(4) without limitation or clarification as to defendant's personal involvement; entitlement to the instruction was linked to defendant's personal participation. On remand, if the trial court were to determine that a ch. 812.022(4) instruction was constitutional as a permissive inference rather than a mandatory presumption, clarifying language might be advisable.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was reversed and remanded for a new trial.

Sorrell v. State


CASE NO. 4D02-2050


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


855 So. 2d 1253; 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 15485; 28 Fla. L. Weekly D 2378



October 15, 2003, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Nineteenth Judicial Circuit, Martin County; Robert R. Makemson, Judge; L.T. Case No. 01-1493CFMA. Opinion Substituted for Opinion dated August 27, 2003 reported at :
Sorrell v. State, 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 12834 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., Aug. 27, 2003)



DISPOSITION: Rehearing granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State moved for rehearing of defendant's appeal of a judgment by the Circuit Court for the Nineteenth Judicial Circuit, Martin County (Florida) that convicted him of driving while his license was revoked in violation of Fla. Stat. ch. 322.341 (2001).


OVERVIEW: At a bench trial, the State proved by competent evidence that defendant's license had been revoked pursuant to Fla. Stat. chs. 322.201 (2001) and 322.251(2) (2001). However, 1998 Fla. Laws ch. 223, the statute creating the crime of driving with a revoked license under Fla. Stat. ch. 322.341, had been declared unconstitutional. The appellate court held that defendant could not be convicted of violating § 322.341. Even though the State did not request the trial judge to consider any lesser-included offenses, pursuant to Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.510(b), defendant could be retried for any lesser included offense of the offense charged in the information, such as driving without a valid driver's license contrary to Fla. Stat. ch. 322.03(1), that was supported by the evidence.


OUTCOME: The State's motion for rehearing and clarification was granted; the prior opinion was withdrawn and substituted with an order that defendant's conviction and sentence be reversed. The case was remanded for a new trial.

Mills v. State


Case No: 2D03-490


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


870 So. 2d 46; 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 15220; 28 Fla. L. Weekly D 2324



October 10, 2003, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal pursuant to Fla. R. App. P. 9.141(b)(2) from the Circuit Court for Lee County; Thomas S. Reese, Judge. Opinion Substituted for Opinion dated August 29, 2003 reported at:
Mills v. State, 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 13022 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2d Dist., Aug. 29, 2003)
Mills v. State, 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 15219 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2d Dist., Oct. 10, 2003)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the order of the Circuit Court for Lee County (Florida), summarily denying his motion to correct an illegal sentence pursuant to Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.800(a).


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that his habitual violent felony offender sentences were illegal, because the appellate court had held that 1999 Fla. OUTCOME: The order was reversed and remanded for correction of defendant's sentences. On remand, if defendant did not qualify as an habitual violent felony offender under the 1998 version of the statute at issue, the trial court was to strike the habitual violent felony offender designations and minimum mandatory terms from defendant's sentences.

GLA & Assocs. v. City of Boca Raton


CASE NO. 4D02-1051


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


855 So. 2d 278; 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 15104; 28 Fla. L. Weekly D 2318



October 8, 2003, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
Rehearing denied by Gla & Assoc. v. City of Boca Raton, 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 15867 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., Oct. 8, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County; Thomas H. Barkdull, III, Judge; L.T. Case No. 00-9282-AJ.
GLA & Assocs. v. City of Boca Raton, 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 10845 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., July 16, 2003)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a developer and a property owner, sued appellee city, alleging that Boca Raton, Fla., Code Ordinances § 28-1556 (1999), which required a city permit for activities conducted seaward of the established coastal construction control line (CCL), was unconstitutional. The Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County, Florida, granted the city summary judgment. Appellants sought review.


OVERVIEW: The Florida Department of Environmental Protection (DEP) granted the developer a permit to rehabilitate a beach dune. The city cited it for violating § 28-1556 by excavating the dune and building structures in a coastal area without a city permit. The city's later refusal to approve the rehabilitation project caused the DEP to revoke its permit. The trial court found that (1) the developer was collaterally estopped because its predecessor in title previously litigated the same issue, (2) the ordinance was not preempted by Fla. Stat. ch. 161, and (3) the ordinance was not unconstitutional for lacking adequate criteria to be considered upon a variance application. The appellate court agreed. As identical issues were raised and decided in the instant suit and a prior one, collateral estoppel applied. Since Boca Raton, Fla., Code Ordinances § 28-1556 was more strict than Fla. Stat. ch. 161.053, in that it prohibited excavation of a dune where the state would apparently have permitted it, the statute neither preempted the ordinance nor was in conflict with it. The city's ordinances, taken as a whole, set out adequate criteria for granting variances.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Mulligan v. City of Hollywood


CASE NO. 4D02-3626


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


871 So. 2d 249; 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 14814; 28 Fla. L. Weekly D 2265



October 1, 2003, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
Rehearing denied by, Question certified by Mulligan v. City of Hollywood, 871 So. 2d 249, 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 6622 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., 2004)
Rehearing denied by Mulligan v. City of Hollywood, 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 7266 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., May 12, 2004)
Motion granted by City of Hollywood v. Mulligan, 919 So. 2d 434, 2005 Fla. LEXIS 2592 (Fla., 2005)
Reversed by, Remanded by City of Hollywood v. Mulligan, 2006 Fla. LEXIS 1476 (Fla., July 6, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County; Thomas M. Lynch, IV, Judge; L.T. Case No. 00-001887 CACE(11).



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant vehicle owner sued appellee city in the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit Court, Broward County (Florida), challenging the validity of Hollywood, Fla., Code § 101.46, under which the owner's vehicle was impounded. The trial court granted the city's summary judgment motion, and the owner appealed.


OVERVIEW: After the owner's vehicle was impounded because he was arrested for offering to commit prostitution, he paid an administrative fee to recover his vehicle. The appellate court held the "impoundment" which Hollywood, Fla., Code § 101.46 purported to allow met the definition of forfeitures because owners were deprived of certain rights in seized vehicles as a penalty for violating the law. The facts that the seizure might be temporary and that the vehicle could be redeemed by the payment of an administrative fee which was less than the vehicle's fair market value did not change this fact. Under Fla. Stat. ch. 932.704(1) (2002), forfeitures were preempted by the Florida Contraband Forfeiture Act (FCFA), Fla. Stat. ch. 932.701 et seq. Forfeitures under the FCFA were limited to felonies, under the definition of contraband in Fla. Stat. ch. § 932.701(2)(a)5 (2002). The act for which the owner was arrested was a misdemeanor, so the forfeiture of his vehicle was unauthorized. Hollywood, Fla., Code § 101.46 also impermissibly conflicted with the provisions of Fla. Stat. ch. 932.704(2)-(4) for judicial proceedings and jury trials regarding forfeitures.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was reversed, and the matter was remanded.

Barrett v. State


Case No. 2D01-5257


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


862 So. 2d 44; 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 14538; 28 Fla. L. Weekly D 2237



September 26, 2003, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Barrett v. State, 873 So. 2d 1222, 2004 Fla. LEXIS 767 (Fla., 2004)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Barrett v. Florida, 543 U.S. 937, 125 S. Ct. 324, 160 L. Ed. 2d 243, 2004 U.S. LEXIS 6869 (2004)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Certificate of appealability denied Barrett v. Sec'y, 2013 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 146731 (M.D. Fla., Oct. 9, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Hillsborough County; Rex Martin Barbas, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury in the Circuit Court for Hillsborough County (Florida) of first-degree murder. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court allowed defendant to present evidence of his intoxication, but, pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 775.051 (2001), it did not allow him to argue or to present expert testimony that his intoxication prevented him from forming the requisite mental intent to commit first-degree murder. Also, the trial court instructed the jury that voluntary intoxication was not a defense to premeditated murder and could not be considered when determining whether defendant acted with premeditation. Defendant claimed that ch. 775.051, which eliminated voluntary intoxication as a defense to criminal charges, was unconstitutional because it violated his right of procedural due process under the Florida Constitution. On appeal, the court found that (1) the due process language contained in the United States and Florida Constitutions was comparable, and there was no basis to conclude that the Florida Constitution provided greater protections to defendant than did the United States Constitution in relation to the elimination of voluntary intoxication as a defense to a criminal offense; and (2) the due process analysis applied equally under the Florida and United States Constitutions.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Bynes v. State


CASE NO. 4D02-1119


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


854 So. 2d 289; 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 14372; 28 Fla. L. Weekly D 2214



September 24, 2003, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
Rehearing denied by Bynes v. State, 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 14985 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., Sept. 24, 2003)
Review denied by Bynes v. State, 892 So. 2d 1011, 2004 Fla. LEXIS 2459 (Fla., 2004)
Post-conviction relief denied at Bynes v. State, 2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 18949 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., Dec. 17, 2008)
Post-conviction relief denied at Bynes v. State, 73 So. 3d 777, 2011 Fla. App. LEXIS 17419 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., 2011)
Related proceeding at, Writ granted by State v. Bynes, 2013 Fla. App. LEXIS 13048 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., Aug. 21, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County; Richard Wennet, Judge; L.T. Case No. 01-912 CF A02. Opinion Substituted for Opinion dated July 30, 2003 reported at:
Bynes v. State, 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 11701 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., July 30, 2003)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant moved for rehearing of a judgment by the Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County (Florida); defendant claimed that his sentence under Fla. Stat. ch. 775.084(1)(d) (2001) was unconstitutional as applied because his prior convictions were not violent crimes.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that his sentence as a violent career criminal under § 775.084(1)(d) (2001) was erroneous because his prior felony convictions for burglary of an unoccupied conveyance were not violent felonies. The appellate court held that the inclusion of simple burglary in the sentencing enhancement available for violent felons under Fla. Stat. ch. 776.08 was rationally related to the legislature's goal of punishing career felony offenders. To conclude that burglary could not be a "violent" felony when the structure or conveyance being burglarized was unoccupied would substitute the court's opinion for the expression of the legislature. Because it was not unreasonable or irrational to equate simple burglary with a violent felony, its inclusion as a predicate offense under the violent career criminal statute did not render the statute unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The motion was denied; however, the opinion was withdrawn and a new one substituted therefor. The judgment was affirmed.

B.S. v. State


Case No. 2D01-1842


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


862 So. 2d 15; 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 13958; 28 Fla. L. Weekly D 2198



September 17, 2003, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Pinellas County; Marion L. Fleming, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Pinellas County (Florida) ordered appellant mother to pay fees related to the detainment of appellant, her son, during delinquency proceedings to cover the costs of the child's subsistence. The mother and son appealed.


OVERVIEW: The mother and son challenged the constitutionality of Fla. Stat. ch. 985.215(6), contending that it violated equal protection when it resulted in exonerated juveniles being treated differently than exonerated adults. They also contended that the statute violated substantive due process insofar as it required payment of subsistence costs for a child's detention at home. The appeals court agreed with both assertions. Consistent with that purpose, the court had no quarrel with requiring a parent to pay the State for her child's subsistence if the child was detained at State expense. However, such was not the instant case. In such circumstances, requiring payment of subsistence costs to the State bore no rational relationship to the legislative purpose of easing the State's financial burden associated with caring for detained children because the State had suffered no burden. Moreover, the statute was arbitrary and oppressive.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded.

 

1918 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Enriguez v. State


Case No. 2D02-2111


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


858 So. 2d 338; 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 13959; 28 Fla. L. Weekly D 2195



September 17, 2003, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication October 13, 2003.
Review denied by Enriguez v. State, 868 So. 2d 523, 2004 Fla. LEXIS 132 (Fla., Jan. 23, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Polk County; Ralph Artigliere, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was found guilty in the Circuit Court for Polk County (Florida) of felony dumping, under Fla. Stat. ch. 403.413 (2001) and misdemeanor trespass on property other than a structure or conveyance. He appealed from an order withholding adjudication and placing him on probation.


OVERVIEW: Defendant put cars and car parts in a neighboring orange grove, without the grove owners' consent. The appellate court held defendant, because he did not preserve the issue of the constitutionality of the felony dumping statute, Fla. Stat. ch. 403.413 (2001), in the trial court, could not argue it was unconstitutional as applied to him. The appellate court could only consider the statute's facial invalidity. Defendant had to show it was unconstitutionally vague in all applications. Isolated examples defendant presented in which the statute's application might be ambiguous did not meet this burden. The statute had to be specific enough to give persons of common intelligence adequate warning of the proscribed conduct. Defendant said the statute could transform the minor traffic infraction of parking a car illegally on private property into a felony. A person of common intelligence would not read this littering statute as applicable to parking violations, and the statute adequately warned people that placing trash, including junked cars, on a neighbor's property was illegal, so it was not vague in all applications and was not facially unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

1920 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Alachua County v. Scharps


CASE NO. 1D02-3240


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


855 So. 2d 195; 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 13916; 28 Fla. L. Weekly D 2157



September 12, 2003, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication September 30, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from the Circuit Court for Alachua County. Stan R. Morris, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant board of county commissioners (county) sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court for Alachua County (Florida) which invalidated a resolution passed by the county which directed that a referendum be placed on the general election ballot. The county raised a number of issues, including whether appellee taxpayer had taxpayer standing to challenge the county's authorization of the referendum.


OVERVIEW: The county adopted a resolution and directed that a non-binding question be placed on the general election ballot. The taxpayer sought a declaratory judgment and injunctive relief pursuant to Fla. Const. art. V, § 4 and Fla. Stat. chs. 26 and 86. Regarding his standing, the taxpayer alleged he was a resident, citizen, and taxpayer of the county. The trial court declared the resolution invalid and found the county improperly placed the non-binding referendum on the ballot. While the trial court did not address or explicitly rule on the standing issue, it implicitly found there was standing by addressing the merits of the complaint. The taxpayer suffered no special injury. The appellate court held he did not have "taxpayer standing" or constitutional standing. He did not assert that the county violated a specific taxing and spending power under the Florida or U.S. Constitution. Because he did not attempt to get an alternative petition placed on the ballot or offer his own ballot for submission, he could not show discrimination. It was not enough that others might be discriminated against in the future. Thus, he had no standing.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed. The appellate court directed that the taxpayer's complaint be dismissed.

Nedd v. State


Case No. 2D02-5457


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


855 So. 2d 664; 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 13590; 28 Fla. L. Weekly D 2152



September 10, 2003, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Nedd v. State, 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 18204 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2d Dist., Oct. 2, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal pursuant to Fla. R. App. P. 9.141(b)(2) from the Circuit Court for Hillsborough County, Daniel L. Perry, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was originally charged by information with trafficking in 28 grams to 30 kilograms of heroin. He entered a negotiated plea to the reduced charge of trafficking in 14 to 28 grams, in return for a 15-year minimum mandatory sentence. Defendant appealed the decision of the Circuit Court for Hillsborough County (Florida), which denied his motion for postconviction relief filed pursuant to Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.800.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's request for relief was based on the appellate court's decision in Taylor v. State, which declared 1999 Fla. Laws ch. 188 unconstitutional. Specifically, defendant argued that his sentence was illegal since the amendment was not valid on the date he committed his offense, December 21, 2000. Although the appellate court agreed with defendant that his sentence was illegal, the trial court's denial of the requested relief had to be affirmed because the attack was not properly brought pursuant to Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.800. Defendant's sentence was the product of a negotiated plea. Both the State and defendant bargained for the agreement. While defendant sought relief under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.800 to obtain correction only of his sentence, he was actually challenging the terms of a plea agreement, and thus the resulting convictions. Because a plea withdrawal was a potential consequence in the case, defendant had to seek relief under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's denial of defendant's motion without prejudice to his right to file an appropriate motion.

 

1922 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Reyes v. State


CASE NO. 4D02-1897


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


854 So. 2d 816; 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 13617; 28 Fla. L. Weekly D 2131



September 10, 2003, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication September 26, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County; Hubert Lindsey, Judge; L.T. Case No. 00-006882-CF A02.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment by the Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County, Florida, that declared him a sexual predator; defendant claimed that Florida's Sexual Predator Act violated due process and the separation of powers clause of the Florida Constitution.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pleaded guilty to first-degree attempted sexual battery on a person less than 12 years old and was designated a sexual predator under Fla. Stat. ch. 775.21 (2001). The appellate court held that although Florida's Third District had held that the Act violated procedural due process, the United States Supreme Court subsequently determined that a similar version of the sex offender registry did not violate procedural due process because it was not a sentence or punishment, but merely a status. The registration requirements under § 775.21(6) did not violate the right to privacy under Fla. Const. art. I, § 23. The Act's public purpose was a sufficiently compelling state interest justifying the intrusion. That a court had no discretion in making the sexual predator determination did not mean that the Act facially violated the separation of powers clause of Fla. Const. art. II, § 3.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1923 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


McLean v. State


Case No. 2D02-1322


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


854 So. 2d 796; 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 13243; 28 Fla. L. Weekly D 2075



September 5, 2003, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication September 30, 2003.
Review granted by McLean v. State, 913 So. 2d 597, 2005 Fla. LEXIS 2282 (Fla., 2005)
Affirmed by McLean v. State, 2006 Fla. LEXIS 1474 (Fla., July 6, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Polk County; Charles L. Brown, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court for Polk County (Florida), which convicted him of lewd molestation.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his judgment and sentence for lewd molestation but the court affirmed, holding that Fla. Stat. ch. 90.404(2)(b) (2001), which expanded the use of Williams rule evidence in child molestation cases, did not violate due process, at least in cases where the identity of the accused perpetrator was not an issue. The court also held that the trial court's reliance upon that rule of evidence did not result in an ex post facto application of a statute and that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in admitting certain Williams rule evidence pursuant to this statute. The witness was an individual who claimed to have been repeatedly abused as a child by defendant; thus, the Williams rule evidence admitted in the case was not introduced for the purpose of establishing identity. The court concluded by certifying a question to the supreme court as to whether § 90.404(2)(b) violated due process when applied in a case in which identity was not an issue.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed and the court certified a question to the supreme court.

1925 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Morrow v. State


CASE NO. 5D03-2322


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


856 So. 2d 1043; 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 13284; 28 Fla. L. Weekly D 2098



September 5, 2003, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication October 30, 2003.
Rehearing denied by Morrow v. State, 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 17264 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 5th Dist., Oct. 13, 2003)
Review denied by Morrow v. State, 889 So. 2d 71, 2004 Fla. LEXIS 2148 (Fla., Nov. 15, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: 3.850 Appeal from the Circuit Court for Sumter County, Hale R. Stancil, Judge.
Morrow v. State, 760 So. 2d 1098, 2000 Fla. App. LEXIS 8167 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 5th Dist., 2000)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment by the Circuit Court for Sumter County (Florida) that summarily denied his Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850 motion for post-conviction relief. Defendant claimed that his counsel was ineffective.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pleaded guilty to possession of a firearm by a violent career criminal in violation of Fla. Stat. ch. 790.235 and was sentenced to life imprisonment under Fla. Stat. ch. 775.087(2). In his Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850 motion, defendant claimed, inter alia, that his counsel was ineffective for not informing him that his plea could result in a mandatory life sentence and for failing to object to the constitutionality of the sentence under Fla. Const. art. I, § 17. The appellate court held that defendant was specifically advised that life imprisonment could result from his plea. In addition, the punishment was not grossly disproportionate, did not involve the unnecessary and wanton infliction of pain, and did not shock the court's conscience and sense of justice. Accordingly, counsel was not ineffective.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1926 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Hall v. State


CASE NO. 1D02-0181


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


853 So. 2d 546; 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 12857; 28 Fla. L. Weekly D 2024



August 29, 2003, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication September 16, 2003.
Review denied by Hall v. State, 865 So. 2d 480, 2003 Fla. LEXIS 2281 (Fla., Dec. 18, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from Circuit Court for Escambia County. Jan Shackelford, Judge.
Hall v. State, 643 So. 2d 1085, 1994 Fla. App. LEXIS 10241 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., 1994)



DISPOSITION: Conviction affirmed; sentence for first degree murder vacated with instructions to correct; question of great public importance certified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his convictions by the Circuit Court for Escambia County (Florida) for first degree murder and armed robbery. He contended the trial court erred in rejecting his request for a 12-person jury and that the written sentence had to be corrected to conform to the oral pronouncement.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was tried and found guilty of first degree felony murder and armed robbery. He was sentenced to life with no possibility of parole for 25 years for the murder and to 10 consecutive years for the robbery. After new evidence was discovered, defendant was retried. Prior to the new trial, defendant argued he was entitled to a 12-person jury because he was on trial for the capital offense of first degree murder. The State argued he had no right to a 12-person jury because double jeopardy barred a death sentence at the retrial. The trial court ruled that the case would be tried with a six person jury. The appellate court held that since defendant had received a life sentence in the original trial, he could not be subject to the death penalty again under principles of double jeopardy. Because the death penalty was not possible as a matter of law, a 12-person jury was not required. The state correctly conceded that the trial court's oral pronouncement of sentence, which was incorrect, prevailed over the written judgment and sentence form.


OUTCOME: Defendant was not entitled to a 12-person jury because the death penalty was not a possible penalty as a matter of law. The appellate court certified that ruling as a question of great public importance. The written sentence had to be corrected to reflect that the sentence on the murder count was to be life with no possibility of parole for 25 years.

1928 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Sorrell v. State


CASE NO. 4D02-2050


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 12834; 28 Fla. L. Weekly D 1998



August 27, 2003, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:

THIS OPINION WAS WITHDRAWN BY THE COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] Released for Publication October 31, 2003.
Opinion withdrawn by, Substituted opinion at, Rehearing granted by Sorrell v. State, 855 So. 2d 1253, 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 15485 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., Oct. 15, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Nineteenth Judicial Circuit, Martin County; Robert R. Makemson, Judge; L.T. Case No. 01-1493CFMA.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court for the Nineteenth Judicial Circuit, Martin County (Florida), which convicted him of driving while his license was permanently revoked, contrary to Fla. Stat. ch. 322.341 (2001).


OVERVIEW: At defendant's trial for driving while his driver's license was permanently revoked, the State admitted into evidence a copy of defendant's driving record and showed that notice of revocation had been established. The State did not submit evidence of the driving while under the influence (DUI) convictions that formed the basis for the license revocation. On defendant's appeal, the court rejected his attacks upon the evidence at trial, but reversed his conviction in light of recent precedent from the Supreme Court of Florida. It was not necessary that the State prove at trial defendant's DUI convictions, as it was the existence of the revocation that was an element of the crime charged, not the prior DUI convictions. However, because the statute that created ch. 322.341 had been declared unconstitutional for violation of the single subject rule, defendant could not be convicted of the crime of driving while his license was permanently revoked. At trial, the trial court did not instruct the jury on any lesser-included offenses to the ch. 322.341 charge. Therefore, defendant could not be retried on any lesser-included offenses of ch. 322.341.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction and remanded for discharge.

Stovall v. Cooper


Case No. 2D02-4606


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


860 So. 2d 5; 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 12809; 28 Fla. L. Weekly D 2033



August 27, 2003, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Stovall v. Cooper, 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 20695 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2d Dist., Oct. 10, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from nonfinal order of the Circuit Court for Polk County; Charles B. Curry, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate appealed a nonfinal order by the Circuit Court for Polk County (Florida), which granted respondent Department of Correction's (DOC) motion to transfer venue to the county in which it maintained its headquarters.


OVERVIEW: The inmate filed a complaint for declaratory relief against DOC employees alleging violation of his constitutional rights by failing to conduct a full investigation into his rating, which would have entitled him to two additional days of gain time. The appellate court held that, because the inmate did not allege that he was entitled to immediate release, his complaint was properly treated as a petition for a writ of mandamus. The court stated that an action in habeas corpus would only have applied had denial of time resulted in his detention beyond expiration of the sentence, which the court found was not the case with this inmate.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1930 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Condon v. Office Depot, Inc.


Case No. 2D02-1688


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


855 So. 2d 644; 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 12533; 28 Fla. L. Weekly D 1961



August 22, 2003, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Condon v. Home Depot, Inc., 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 18206 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2d Dist., Oct. 7, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Hillsborough County; Sam D. Pendino, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant consumer alleged that appellee corporation violated the Telephone Consumer Protection Act (TCPA), 47 U.S.C.S. § 227, by sending him 13 unsolicited facsimile ads. The corporation filed a motion to dismiss, arguing that statutory language required the state legislature to enact legislation before the claim was cognizable in state court. The Circuit Court for Hillsborough County (Florida) dismissed the suit. The consumer appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the issue was whether Florida recognized a private cause of action arising under the TCPA, in the absence of specific state legislation authorizing such action. The appellate court concluded that Florida was not required to adopt enabling legislation before a state court of competent jurisdiction could entertain this federal law claim because states had the right to structure their own court systems and state courts were not obligated to change their procedural rules or to create courts to accommodate TCPA claims. The ambiguous statutory language "if otherwise permitted" did not explicitly direct the enactment of enabling state legislation. Nor did the legislative history support such a requirement. There was no incompatibility between state-court jurisdiction and federal interests. To the contrary, although Congress created the private TCPA action, it was from the beginning a cause of action in the states' interests. Thus, the trial court erred by dismissing the consumer's complaint.


OUTCOME: The decision of the trial court was reversed and remanded for further proceedings.

Houston v. State


CASE NO. 5D02-3121


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


852 So. 2d 425; 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 12558; 28 Fla. L. Weekly D 1972



August 22, 2003, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication September 10, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Orange County, Frank Kaney, Senior Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED in part, REVERSED in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment by the Circuit Court for Orange County (Florida) that admitted similar acts evidence and ordered him to receive chemical castration, if necessary, upon release from prison pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 794.0235 (2000).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted under Fla. Stat. ch. 794.011(4)(b) (2000) of sexually assaulting a homeless woman. Defendant claimed that the encounter was consensual. He also claimed that chemical castration was a cruel or unusual punishment violative of Fla. Const. art. I, § 17 and U.S. Const. amend. VIII. The appellate court held that evidence of prior sexual batteries by defendant on other homeless women was relevant under Fla. Stat. ch. 90.404(2) (2002) to rebut the consent defense. However, the trial court failed to follow the procedures of Fla. Stat. ch. 794.0235(2)(a) (2000) in its imposition of chemical castration. The trial court did not at any time appoint a medical expert to opine on whether defendant was an appropriate candidate for treatment, and failed to specify the duration of treatment in the sentence. Defendant's constitutional claims were not addressed.


OUTCOME: The judgment and sentence dealing with chemical castration was reversed; it was affirmed in all other respects.

 

1932 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


GTE Fla., Inc. v. Todora


Case No. 2D01-1035


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


854 So. 2d 731; 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 12531; 28 Fla. L. Weekly D 1957



August 22, 2003, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication September 9, 2003.
Review denied by Todora v. GTE Fla., Inc., 861 So. 2d 433, 2003 Fla. LEXIS 2094 (Fla., Nov. 25, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Sarasota County; Robert W. McDonald, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer challenged, in the Circuit Court for Sarasota County (Florida), appellee county property appraiser's valuation of its tangible personal property for ad valorem tax purposes. The trial court upheld the property appraiser's valuations, and the taxpayer appealed.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer, a previously regulated telecommunications utility, argued that when it became unregulated and subject to competition, it was improper to use the income approach to value its tangible personal property. The appellate court held that under Fla. Const. art. VII, §§ 1(a), 2, 9(a), only the State could tax intangible personal property. From the single value arrived at by the income approach to valuation of the taxpayer's tangible personal property, it was virtually impossible to segregate intangible assets and identify their values in a nonarbitrary fashion. The income method of valuation was found unconstitutional inasmuch as it taxed a cable television company's intangible property, and the same rule applied to the taxpayer. The taxpayer did not have to prove the extent to which the appraiser's valuation improperly included intangible property. The appraiser could not justify its valuation by comparing it to amounts for which the taxpayer sold access lines around the country, as these varied widely. There was no basis for applying a 30 percent intangible factor to the taxpayer's sales.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was reversed, and the matter was remanded to either establish an assessment of the taxpayer's tangible personal property based on the record or remand the matter to the appraiser.

 

1933 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Lee v. State


CASE NO. 2D00-1430


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


854 So. 2d 709; 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 12216; 28 Fla. L. Weekly D 1912



August 15, 2003, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication September 8, 2003.
Review denied by Lee v. State, 908 So. 2d 1057, 2005 Fla. LEXIS 1539 (Fla., July 8, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Manatee County; Thomas M. Gallen, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed; question certified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Manatee County (Florida) committed appellant, a convicted sex offender, to the custody of the Department of Children and Family Services, pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 394.917(2) (1999). Appellant sought review.


OVERVIEW: Appellant suffered from a mental abnormality or personality disorder which made him likely to engage in acts of sexual violence if not confined for long-term control, care, and treatment. On appeal from a commitment order, the appeals court first held that although there were conflicts in the evidence as to the reliability of the scientific tests and the conclusions drawn, the witnesses discussed their clinical evaluations, the results of tests, and the basis for their conclusions and recommendations. Because there was substantial evidence apart from the test results supporting the State's claim that appellant met the requirements for commitment, any error in the admission of the test results was harmless. Second, appellant failed to prove any constitutional infirmity arising from Fla. Stat. ch. 394.9155(5) (1999). Third, based on the nature of commitment proceedings and the evidence was addressed at trial, factual details relating to appellant's prior offenses were properly admitted. Finally, absent objection, a jury instruction regarding appellant's inability to control himself was not grounds for reversal, but prompted review by the Florida Supreme Court.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed, and the following was certified to the Florida Supreme Court as a question of great public importance: May an individual be committed under the Jimmy Ryce Act in the absence of a jury instruction that the State must prove that the individual has serious difficulty in controlling his or her dangerous behavior?

Strong v. State


CASE NO. 3D01-3589


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, THIRD DISTRICT


853 So. 2d 1095; 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 20794; 28 Fla. L. Weekly D 1877



August 13, 2003, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Amended February 11, 2004.
Rehearing denied by Strong v. State, 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 15060 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 3d Dist., Sept. 5, 2003)
Review denied by Strong v. State, 862 So. 2d 728, 2003 Fla. LEXIS 2173 (Fla., 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from the Circuit Court for Monroe County, Luis Garcia, Judge. LOWER TRIBUNAL NO. 01-29.
Strong v. State, 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 12331 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 3d Dist., 2003)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Monroe County (Florida) entered on a jury verdict convicting him of sexual battery and kidnapping.


OVERVIEW: The victim claimed that she was forced at knifepoint to leave her path and was sexually assaulted. At one point, the victim admitted to offering the use of a condom for fear of sexual disease. Defendant admitted to the sexual encounters, but claimed that it was consensual. On appeal, he claimed that the trial court erred by giving a jury instruction regarding Fla. Stat. Ann. § 794.022(5) (2001) on the relevance of prophylactic condom use in sexual battery prosecution. The court disagreed, holding that the instruction properly educated the jury on the law and noting that the jury might otherwise have relied on its possibly incorrect intuitive reaction to the condom use. The court acknowledged that another subsection of § 794.022 mandated a jury instruction on its topic, but held that the legislature's omission of such a mandate in § 794.022(5) did not mean that an instruction on prophylactic use was barred. Rather, the court noted that the omission meant that the trial court had discretion as to whether to give such an instruction. The court also found no fundamental error in the State's closing argument when read as a whole.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

 

1935 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Bacon Family Partners, L.P. v. Apollo Condo. Ass'n


Case No. 2D02-4991


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


852 So. 2d 882; 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 11582; 28 Fla. L. Weekly D 1795



August 1, 2003, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication August 22, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Collier County; Hugh D. Hayes, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant condominium unit owner sought review from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Collier County (Florida), which struck the owner's motion for trial and granted a final judgment in favor of appellee condominium association, based on a decision of the arbitrator. The association had filed an action seeking damages and injunctive relief due to the owner's use of a deck area as a restaurant.


OVERVIEW: The association filed an action against the owner for using the deck area as a restaurant, and it responded with affirmative defenses and a counterclaim. The parties attended nonbinding arbitration, whereupon the arbitrator awarded injunctive relief to the association but denied its claim for damages, and denied the owner's counterclaim for damages. The owner's motion for trial on the limited issues of the association's claim for injunctive relief and its counterclaim for damages was denied, and final judgment was entered in accordance with the arbitration award. On appeal, the court noted that extensive litigation had transpired between the parties regarding the disputed use of the deck. The court held that the notice for trial by the owner was timely filed pursuant to Fla. R. Civ. P. 1.820(h) following the decision of the arbitrator and accordingly, the trial court had no discretion to deny holding a trial de novo on the stated issues. The issues were found to have been tried by consent, and accordingly the voluntary dismissal of the counterclaim did not preclude the trial de novo after decision of the arbitrator.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded the matter for trial on specific limited issues.

Donnelly v. Marion County


Case No. 5D02-1851


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


851 So. 2d 256; 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 11726; 28 Fla. L. Weekly D 1812



August 1, 2003, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication August 20, 2003.
Review denied by Marion County v. Donnelly, 860 So. 2d 978, 2003 Fla. LEXIS 1967 (Fla., Nov. 3, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Marion County, Jack Singbush, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowners filed an action against appellee county in the Circuit Court for Marion County (Florida), to declare that a county ordinance was unconstitutional and special assessments made thereunder invalid. Both sides moved for partial summary judgment. The trial court found in favor of the county on the motions and ruled the ordinance to be valid, facially constitutional, and constitutional as applied. The landowners appealed.


OVERVIEW: The county passed an ordinance that created a municipal service taxing unit (MSTU). The MSTU then enacted special assessments to fund enhanced law enforcement and community resource facilities in an unincorporated area of the county. The trial court found that the assessments did not fund general government services but supplemented such services. The trial court ruled that the special assessments provided a special benefit to the assessed properties by enhancing the value of the property and creating a community identity. Further, the court ruled that the assessments were fairly and reasonably apportioned among the benefitted properties. On appeal, the court found that any benefit was not the type of direct, special benefit to the real property that was required to validate a special assessment.


OUTCOME: The partial summary judgment and the final judgment were reversed, and the ordinance was invalidated.

 

1938 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Envtl. Confederation of Southwest Fla., Inc. v. IMC Phosphates, Inc.


CASE NO. 1D03-1717


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


857 So. 2d 207; 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 11571; 28 Fla. L. Weekly D 1786



July 31, 2003, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication November 13, 2003.
Rehearing denied by Envtl. Confederation of Southwest Fla., Inc. v. IMC Phosphates, Inc., 857 So. 2d 207, 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 16124 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., 2003)
Rehearing denied by Envtl. Confederation of Southwest Fla., Inc. v. IMC Phosphates, Inc., 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 17914 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., Oct. 28, 2003)
Subsequent appeal at Envtl. Confederation of Southwest Fla., Inc. v. Dep't of Envtl. Protection, 886 So. 2d 1013, 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 16079 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., Oct. 28, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal of an order of the Department of Environmental Protection.



DISPOSITION: Motion denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant environmental public interest groups petitioned for a formal administrative hearing by the Florida Department of Environmental Protection, to challenge the issuance of a permit to appellee mining corporation. The Department dismissed their petition. When the Department issued its final order, the public interest groups filed an appeal. The mining corporation moved to dismiss the appeal.


OVERVIEW: The Department found that the public interest groups lacked standing to challenge the issuance of the permit, pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 403.412 (2002), because they had less than 25 members living in the subject county. The mining corporation contended that the appeal should be dismissed because the public interest groups did not show that they were harmed by the order dismissing their petition before the Department, as they were entitled to intervene in the consolidated proceeding. On appeal, the court found that the public interest groups were adversely affected by the order denying their right to a formal administrative hearing on the proposed environmental permit for the simple reason that the order denied them a right to assert a challenge to the permit. If the public interest groups were wrongfully denied the right to initiate their own challenge to the permit, merely allowing them to intervene in the proceeding, which other litigants controlled, could not cure the harm. Because the order was subject to judicial review under Fla. Stat. ch. 120.68(1) (2002), the court had jurisdiction to address the merits of the appeal.


OUTCOME: The motion was denied.

 

1939 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


State v. Veilleux


Case Nos. 2D02-3226, 2D02-3256 CONSOLIDATED


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 11415; 28 Fla. L. Weekly D 1804



July 30, 2003, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:

 [*1] NOT FINAL UNTIL TIME EXPIRES TO FILE REHEARING MOTION AND, IF FILED, DETERMINED

THIS OPINION WAS WITHDRAWN BY THE COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Opinion withdrawn by, Substituted opinion at, Rehearing granted by, Writ of certiorari denied State v. Veilleux, 859 So. 2d 1224, 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 16953 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2d Dist., Nov. 7, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Petition for Writ of Certiorari to the Circuit Court for Pinellas County; Nelly N. Khouzam, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Certiorari denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State petitioned for a writ of certiorari to the Circuit Court for Pinellas County (Florida) requesting that the trial court's interlocutory pretrial order granting defendant's motion in limine to exclude a forged traffic citation, based on Fla. Stat. ch. 316.650(9) (2002), be quashed. Defendant was charged with forgery pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 831.01 (2002).


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that Fla. Stat. 316.650(9) (2002) barred the admission of a traffic citation he signed with a false name. The appellate court found that ch. 316.650(9) was clear and unambiguous. There was no indication that the legislature intended a different result that the exclusion of traffic citations. Further, the trial court was obligated to follow an appellate court holding that traffic citations were inadmissible in trials for forgery of the citations. The proper inquiry on certiorari was whether the trial court afforded procedural due process and applied the correct law. The trial court applied the correct law. The majority rejected the dissent's theory for granting certiorari based on the statute's violation of the constitutional principle of law that only the Florida Supreme Court could promulgate procedural rules under Fla. Const. art. V, § 2(a). Even if Fla. Stat. ch. 316.650(9) (2002) was purely procedural, the constitutional limitation on the legislature's enactment of procedural law was limited to instances where the statute conflicted with a rule of the Florida Supreme Court. There was no rule governing the admissibility of traffic citations as evidence.


OUTCOME: The petition for a writ of certiorari was denied.

 

1940 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Staley v. State


Case No. 2D02-857, 2D02-1325 CONSOLIDATED


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


851 So. 2d 805; 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 11430; 28 Fla. L. Weekly D 1800



July 30, 2003, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication August 20, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from and Petition for Writ of Habeas Corpus to the Circuit Court for Lee County; Edward J. Volz, Jr., Acting Circuit Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reverse..


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant prisoner challenged a Circuit Court for Lee County (Florida) decision revoking his probation. He also petitioned for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court reversed the order revoking the prisoner's probation where the State had presented no evidence and failed to satisfy its burden of proof. The fact that the prisoner waived his right to an adversarial hearing in drug court made no difference. Even if he validly made an advance waiver of his right to contest evidence that might be submitted against him in the future, that was all that he waived. He did not relieve the State of its burden to file an affidavit setting out the alleged violation. He did not relieve the State of its burden to prove the violation by competent evidence. As no evidence was presented at the hearing, the court's belief that he failed to give a required urine sample could only have been the result of hearsay from some unspecified extrajudicial source. The court never covered the clause that concerned the waiver of an adversarial hearing, so he could not have knowingly and intelligently waived his right to contest allegations against him without knowing what those allegations were. Under Fla. Stat. ch. 948.06 and Fla. Stat. ch. 948.01(13), the revocation was improper.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the order revoking probation. The habeas petition was moot.

 

1941 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Givens v. State


Case No. 2D02-3084


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


851 So. 2d 813; 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 11431; 28 Fla. L. Weekly D 1809



July 30, 2003, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication August 20, 2003.
Review denied by Givens v. State, 917 So. 2d 193, 2005 Fla. LEXIS 2485 (Fla., Nov. 18, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Pinellas County; John A. Schaefer, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court, Pinellas County (Florida) entered a judgment finding defendant guilty of failure to register as a sex offender. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted as a sexual offender. Thereafter, he was convicted of failing to register as a sexual offender. On appeal, he argued that the sexual offender registration and notification requirements in Fla. Stat. ch. 943.0435, 944.607 (2001) violated his procedural due process because he was not afforded a hearing to determine whether he was a danger to the public before being subject to the statutory requirements. He also contended that Fla. Stat. ch. 943.0435 (2001), the sexual offender registration statute, violated ex post facto principles because it was enacted after he began his sentence. Regarding procedural due process, the appellate court found that the sexual offender statute did not entitle a defendant to a hearing to establish whether he or she was dangerous, as that fact was not material under the statute; the relevant fact was whether a defendant had been convicted of a specific crime and a defendant had to be offered procedural due process before a conviction was entered. Regarding the Ex Post Facto Clause, the appellate court found its retroactive application did not violate that clause because the statute was procedural and nonpunitive in nature.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

Padilla v. State


CASE NO. 2D02-5319


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


870 So. 2d 6; 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 11436; 28 Fla. L. Weekly D 1789



July 30, 2003, Opinion Filed
