PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal pursuant to Fla. R. App. P. 9.141(b)(2) from the Circuit Court for Hillsborough County; Chet A. Tharpe, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the order of the Circuit Court for Hillsborough County (Florida) denying his motion filed pursuant to Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.800(a).


OVERVIEW: Defendant pleaded guilty to 4 counts of an information and was sentenced accordingly. He alleged that the mandatory minimum sentences were illegal based on Taylor v. State, which held that 1999 Fla. Laws ch. 188, which provided for the imposition of mandatory minimum prison sentences for certain drug offenses, was unconstitutional, as it violated the single subject rule of the Florida Constitution. The appellate court found the dates of the commission of the offenses in question fell within the Taylor window. Defendant therefore presented facially sufficient claims in regard to the offenses of trafficking in cocaine in an amount of more than 200, but less than 400 grams, Fla. Stat. ch. 893.135(1)(b)(1)(b). However, he was not entitled to relief on his claim that the 15-year mandatory minimum term of imprisonment imposed pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 893.135(1)(b)(1)(c) was an illegal sentence, as that section was not affected by the amendments to ch. 893.135 contained in 1999 Fla. Laws ch. 188.


OUTCOME: The order of the trial court was reversed and remanded for the trial court to resentence on counts 1 and 4 under the 1997 statute. The denial of defendant's claim as to the 15-year mandatory minimum sentence was affirmed.

Bynes v. State


CASE NO. 4D02-1119


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 11701



July 30, 2003, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1]
Opinion withdrawn by, Substituted opinion at, Rehearing denied by Bynes v. State, 854 So. 2d 289, 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 14372 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., Sept. 24, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County; Richard Wennet, Judge; L.T. Case No. 01-912 CF A02.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County (Florida), which convicted him as a violent career criminal and sentenced him to concurrent terms of 40 years for fleeing and eluding and aggravated assault on a law enforcement officer, and to 15 years for resisting arrest with violence and grand theft.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of fleeing and eluding, aggravated assault on a law enforcement officer, resisting arrest with violence, and grand theft. He was sentenced as a violent career criminal and he appealed, challenging the constitutionality of Fla. Stat. ch. 775.084(1)(d) (2001). Defendant's previous felony convictions included burglary of an unoccupied conveyance, which he contended were not violent crimes, thereby rendering the statute unconstitutional. The court concluded that burglary of an unoccupied conveyance was included as a qualifying offense and that the effect thereof was not unconstitutional. The court found that the inclusion of burglary as a forcible felony under Fla. Stat. ch. 776.08 was rationally related to the valid legislative purpose of punishing repeat offenders more severely. Accordingly, the court concluded that Fla. Stat. ch. 775.084(1)(d) was not over-inclusive.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of conviction and sentences of the trial court.

A.A. v. Dep't of Children & Families


CASE NOS. 4D02-4484, and 4D02-4583


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


852 So. 2d 318; 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 11710; 28 Fla. L. Weekly D 1767



July 30, 2003, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication September 3, 2003.
Rehearing denied by A.A. v. DCF, 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 14493 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., Sept. 3, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Consolidated appeals from the Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County; Richard B. Burk, Senior Judge; L.T. Case Nos. 99-300136-JL, 00-300343-JL, and 01-300595-JL.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant biological parents appealed from the termination of their parental rights by the Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County (Florida), after the trial court denied a request for the names of a child's foster parents, who wanted to adopt the child.


OVERVIEW: The parents argued that they were entitled to the names of the children's foster parents and that Fla. Stat. ch. 409.175(16) (2002) was unconstitutional. The appellate court held that the trial court properly focused the termination of parental rights trial on the parents' deficiencies. An evaluation of a foster parent's qualities was immaterial under Fla. Stat. ch. 39.810 (2002). The legislature intended to shield foster parents from a termination case. In fact, Fla. Stat. ch. 409.175(16) (2002) excluded information on foster parents from public record disclosure. Further, the confidentiality of foster parents' information was a matter of sound public policy. The parents' interests were protected through their ability to cross-examine all of the witnesses who testified as to the relationship between the children and the foster parents. Finally, the parents' argument that the children, through their guardian ad litem, lacked standing to join in the case as it was brought by the Florida Department of Children and Families was rejected. The guardian ad litem could have brought the termination case under Fla. Stat. ch. 39.802(1) (2002), and was entitled to participate in the action.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.

Rodriguez v. State


CASE NO. 3D01-2332


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, THIRD DISTRICT


2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 11074; 28 Fla. L. Weekly D 1680



July 23, 2003, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:

 [*1] NOT FINAL UNTIL TIME EXPIRES TO FILE REHEARING MOTION AND, IF FILED, DISPOSED OF.

THIS OPINION WAS WITHDRAWN BY THE COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing granted by, Clarified by, Opinion withdrawn by, Substituted opinion at Rodriguez v. State, 906 So. 2d 1082, 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 457 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 3d Dist., Jan. 21, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from the Circuit Court for Miami-Dade County, Jose M. Rodriguez, Judge. LOWER TRIBUNAL NO. 01-8689.



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part; affirmed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury of resisting an officer without violence, fleeing or attempting to elude a law enforcement officer, unlawful display of authorized indicia of law enforcement activity, in violation of Fla. Stat. ch. 843.085, and reckless driving. The Circuit Court for Miami-Dade County (Florida) imposed sentence. Defendant appealed, and his appeal included a challenge to the constitutionality of Fla. Stat. ch. 843.085.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, who was traveling on his motorcycle at over 100 miles per hour, was wearing a black shirt with the word "POLICE" written on the front and back. When the real police pointed for him to move off to the shoulder of the road, defendant mouthed the word "police" and kept going. After finding that Fla. Stat. ch. 843.085 was content-based, and subject to strict judicial scrutiny, the appellate court held that it was unconstitutionally overbroad. It banned the wearing of any indicia of law enforcement authority regardless of the intent of the non-official. There needed to be an intent or scienter requirement. Even though the defendant's own conduct was proscribed by the statute, he nevertheless had standing to interpose and maintain an overbreadth challenge, as the statute could have a chilling effect on the exercise of First Amendment freedoms. Claimed error in the prosecutor's closing argument was found to have been in response to argument made by the defense, and therefore the claimed error was invited. Error in failing to suppress one of defendant's responses to an officer's question was harmless, given all of the other overwhelming evidence of defendant's guilt.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and sentence for unlawful display of authorized indicia of law enforcement authority were reversed and vacated. The convictions and sentences on all remaining counts were affirmed.

Thompson v. Douds


Case No. 2D02-3972


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


852 So. 2d 299; 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 10880; 28 Fla. L. Weekly D 1667



July 18, 2003, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Thompson v. Douds, 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 18191 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2d Dist., Aug. 26, 2003)
Review denied by Douds v. Thompson, 871 So. 2d 872, 2004 Fla. LEXIS 522 (Fla., 2004)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Douds v. Thompson, 543 U.S. 820, 125 S. Ct. 59, 160 L. Ed. 2d 29, 2004 U.S. LEXIS 5666 (U.S., Oct. 4, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Hillsborough County; Vivian C. Maye, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, an alleged victim's guardian and another, sued defendant police officers, alleging the use of excessive force. Claims were made against the individual officers, pursuant to 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, and a state-law claim was made for battery. The officers asserted statutory immunity, under Fla. Stat. ch. 768.28(9) (1997). The Circuit Court for Hillsborough County (Florida) granted summary judgment to the officers. Plaintiffs appealed.


OVERVIEW: The victim committed no offense, but acted strangely. He was left in a vegetative state as a result of his encounter with the police. The police offered no plausible explanation for the severity of the victim's injuries. The trial court, in granting summary judgment, found, as a matter of law, that the actions of the officers were reasonable. The appellate court disagreed. The fact that the victim committed no offense at all militated against the use of force, much less the force used in the instant case to effect the victim's detention. There was no evidence that the victim posed any immediate threat to others. The officers should have known, based upon the state of the law at the time of the incident, that their actions violated the victim's constitutional rights. The officers contended that their testimony was unrefuted, as the victim was in a vegetative state and could not raise an issue of material fact. The appellate court found that standing alone, the fact that the substance of the officers' internal affairs interviews conflicted with their deposition testimony raised a genuine issue of material fact on the issue of the force used and the officers' credibility.


OUTCOME: The case was reversed and remanded for further proceedings on both claims. It was ordered that the individual officers were not entitled to either qualified immunity or statutory immunity as a matter of law.

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Polk County; J. Tim Strickland, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part; remanded for resentencing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment by the Circuit Court for Polk County (Florida) that convicted and sentenced him for multiple offenses based on his attack on correctional officers; defendant claimed, inter alia, that his convictions were erroneously reclassified based on the use of a weapon.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that his attempted second-degree murder and aggravated battery convictions were erroneously based on his use of a weapon. Although the attempted second-degree murder conviction was properly treated as a first-degree felony under Fla. The prison releasee reoffender sentence was erroneously entered under the amendment to Fla. Stat. ch. 775.082(9)(a)(2), which had been held to be an unconstitutional violation of the single subject rule.


OUTCOME: The convictions were affirmed; the prison releasee reoffender sentences was reversed and remand for resentencing.

Prof'l Consulting Servs. v. Hartford Life & Accident Ins. Co.


Case No. 2D02-429


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant billing company sued appellee insurer in the County Court for Manatee County (Florida), to collect personal injury protection (PIP) benefits owed to the insured. The trial court granted the insurer's motion to dismiss. The billing company appealed.


OVERVIEW: The billing company accepted an assignment of PIP benefits from the insured. The assignment was given for the purpose of billing the insurer for treatment rendered to the insured by health care providers. The insurer moved to dismiss, contending that Fla. GLA & Assocs. v. City of Boca Raton


CASE NO. 4D02-1051


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 10845; 28 Fla. L. Weekly D 1636



July 16, 2003, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:

 [*1] NOT FINAL UNTIL DISPOSITION OF ANY TIMELY FILED MOTION FOR REHEARING. NOT FINAL UNTIL TIME EXPIRES TO FILE REHEARING MOTION AND, IF FILED, DISPOSED OF.

THIS OPINION WAS WITHDRAWN BY THE COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Opinion withdrawn by, Substituted opinion at, Rehearing denied by GLA & Assocs. v. City of Boca Raton, 855 So. 2d 278, 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 15104 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., Oct. 8, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County; Thomas H. Barkdull, III, Judge; L.T. Case No. 00-9282-AJ.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant condominium developer appealed from the entry of summary judgment by the Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County (Florida), for appellee City and holding constitutional a city ordinance requiring a city permit for activities conducted seaward of the established coastal construction control line (CCL).


OVERVIEW: The developer argued that Boca Raton, Fla., Code of Ordinances § 28-1556 (1999), which required a permit to perform excavation, was preempted by the Florida Beach and Shore Preservation Act, Fla. Stat. ch. 161. The appellate court held that the developer was collaterally estopped from litigating the preemption and inconsistency arguments due to litigation brought by the developer's predecessor, which determined that ch. 161 did not preempt the City from regulating seaward of the CCL. Even if collateral estoppel did not apply, the Act did not impliedly preempt the ordinance. The Florida Department of Environmental Protection (DEP) had always interpreted the Act as allowing local setback ordinances, and DEP's interpretation was given considerable deference. Boca Raton, Fla., Code of Ordinances § 28-1556(4) was more strict than the Act. Therefore, the statute neither preempted the ordinance nor was in conflict with it. As § 28-1556(4) was part of the same chapter as Boca Raton, Fla., Code of Ordinances § 28-130, its criteria applied to variances sought under Boca Raton, Fla., Code of Ordinances § 28-1556(4).


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Meister


CASE NO. 4D02-3528


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


849 So. 2d 1127; 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 10846; 28 Fla. L. Weekly D 1635



July 16, 2003, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County; Lisa G. Trachman, Judge; L.T. Case No. 02-823 TC10A.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged by indictment in the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County (Florida) with driving while license suspended. Defendant moved to dismiss the information. The circuit court granted the motion to dismiss, declaring Fla. Stat. ch. 322.34(2) (2001) unconstitutionally vague as applied to the facts of the case. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant alleged that she was arrested while riding a moped and charged with driving with a suspended license. She argued that Fla. Stat. ch. 322.03(1) (2001) did not provide a clear meaning of the conduct which was prohibited by statute, thereby rendering it unconstitutionally vague. She also argued that a motor vehicle, as defined in Fla. Stat. ch. 316.003(21), specifically excluded bicycles and mopeds from the definition. Thus, she concluded that it would be reasonable to assume that a moped was not a motor vehicle. The circuit court found for defendant and ruled that Fla. Stat. ch. 322.34(2) was unconstitutional as applied in the case. On appeal, the court found that driving a moped required a license because a moped was not excluded from the definition of a motor vehicle in Fla. Stat. ch. 322.01(26) (2001). Further, there was no vagueness or ambiguity in ch. 322.34 with respect to mopeds which would render the statute unconstitutionally vague.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, and the case was remanded with directions to reinstate the charges against defendant.

F.L. v. Dep't of Children & Families


CASE NO. 4D02-4396


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


849 So. 2d 1114; 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 10150; 28 Fla. L. Weekly D 1533



July 3, 2003, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication August 7, 2003.
Rehearing denied by F.L. v. DCF, 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 12458 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., Aug. 7, 2003)
Reversed by, Remanded by Fla. Dep't of Children & Families v. F.L., 2004 Fla. LEXIS 984 (Fla., July 8, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County; Michael L. Gates, Judge; L.T. Case No. 97-12294 CJDP.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee child care agency filed a petition in the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County (Florida), for termination of appellant mother's parental rights. The trial court concluded that the child care agency proved its case for termination in accordance with both Fla. Stat. ch. 39.806(1)(c), (i), and terminated the mother's parental rights. The mother appealed.


OVERVIEW: The mother's parental rights to her first six children were terminated due to her failure to comply with court-ordered case plan tasks. The agency alleged that, pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 39.806(1)(c), the mother failed to comply with prior case plans leading to the termination of her rights to the other children. As a second ground for termination, the agency alleged that the mother's rights to her sixth child were involuntarily terminated and constituted a ground for termination under Fla. Stat. ch. 39.806(1)(i) as to the seventh and subject child. A counselor for the agency admitted that the agency relied solely on the mother's history and not on any new allegations of neglect relating to the subject child. In fact, she conceded that the mother had made several efforts to improve herself and her ability to parent the subject child, which she had not done with the other children. The guardian ad litem also opined as to the mother's improved efforts at child rearing as to the subject child. On appeal, the court found that the agency failed to prove the ch. 39.806(1)(c) requirements for termination. Further, the court found ch. 39.806(1)(i) to be facially unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

 

1954 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Langley v. State


Case No. 2D02-481


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


848 So. 2d 428; 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 9915; 28 Fla. L. Weekly D 1546



July 2, 2003, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 24, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Sarasota County; Lee E. Haworth, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court, Sarasota County (Florida), denied defendant's motion to suppress evidence and entered a final judgment of conviction after he entered a negotiated plea of no contest to a drug trafficking charge in exchange for a sentence of three years in prison. It then imposed a three-year minimum mandatory sentence despite the fact that the written plea agreement did not contain reference to a minimum mandatory term. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with drug trafficking. After the trial court denied his dispositive motion to suppress evidence, defendant entered a negotiated plea of no contest to the charge in exchange for a sentence of three years in prison. The trial court then imposed a three-year minimum mandatory sentence, even though the written plea agreement did not contain reference to a minimum mandatory term. On appeal, defendant argued that his sentence had to be reversed based on the appellate court's Taylor opinion that held the Florida law that required mandatory minimum prison sentences for certain drug offenses was unconstitutional because it violated the single-subject rule of the Florida Constitution. After considering that argument, the appellate court found that defendant did not preserve that issue for review either at sentencing or by filing an appropriate motion. It then affirmed the trial court's judgment, but without prejudice to defendant's right to file a facially-sufficient motion for postconviction relief pursuant to Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850, if he determined that doing so was is in his best interest, because defendant might have a cognizable Taylor claim.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment, but without prejudice to defendant's right to file a facially-sufficient motion for postconviction relief.

 

1955 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


State v. Treworgy


CASE NO. 3D03-626


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, THIRD DISTRICT


849 So. 2d 406; 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 9919; 28 Fla. L. Weekly D 1517



July 2, 2003, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 18, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: A Writ of Certiorari to the Circuit Court for Monroe County, Richard Payne, Judge. LOWER TRIBUNAL NO. 02-1005.



DISPOSITION: Certiorari granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State filed a petition for writ of certiorari to challenge an affirmance by the trial court (Florida) of a county court order which dismissed the State's action against respondent criminal defendants for violation of a state administrative rule that barred the harvesting and possessing of "short" spiny lobsters.


OVERVIEW: The criminal defendants caught several "short" spiny lobsters. When harvested, each lobster had a carapace measurement of over three inches. When the criminal defendants arrived back at the dock, the lobsters' heads were separated from their tails. One criminal defendant then disposed of the heads. When he returned from doing so, Fish and Wildlife officers determined that 186 of the lobsters had tails less than five-and-one-half inches in length. The criminal defendants were then charged with violating Fla. Admin. Code Ann. r. 68B-24.003(1), prohibiting a person from possessing any spiny lobster with a carapace measurement of three inches or less, or if the tail had been separated from the body, a tail measurement less than five-and-one-half inches not including protruding muscle tissue. The county court dismissed the action on the ground that the provision was unconstitutional. The trial court affirmed. After the State filed a petition for writ of certiorari, the appellate court found that the provision was not unconstitutional because the two measurements were not inconsistent; if either measurement violated the provision, the lobster could not be harvested or possessed.


OUTCOME: The appellate court granted the petition for writ of certiorari, ordered that the trial court's affirmance was quashed and that the cause be remanded to the trial court with directions to reverse the county court order on appeal and to order that the case proceed to trial.

 

1956 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Watts v. State


CASE NO. 4D01-3582


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


855 So. 2d 100; 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 9374; 28 Fla. L. Weekly D 1481



June 25, 2003, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County; Hugh S. Glickstein, Senior Judge; L.T. Case No. 99-14258CF10A.
Watts v. State, 848 So. 2d 336, 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 5839 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., 2003)



DISPOSITION: Motion for rehearing or certification denied


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment by the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County (Florida), by way of a motion for rehearing or certification; defendant claimed that a controlling case, pending on review before the Florida Supreme Court, had been overlooked.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of failing to report a change of address as a sexual offender within 48 hours of a residence change, contrary to Fla. Stat. chs. 943.0435(4), 944.607(9) (2001). The appellate court held that the records produced at trial demonstrated that defendant had previously registered as a sexual offender. Therefore, defendant was aware of the registration requirement. The "controlling" case dealt with a jury instruction that the State was not required to prove scienter or guilty knowledge to obtain a conviction for a failure to register. There was no indication that the trial court decided the case based on an erroneous determination that no "broadly applicable guilty knowledge requirement" was applicable. As such, the "controlling" case was distinguishable and did not apply.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1957 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


State v. Exposito


CASE NO. 3D02-2467


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, THIRD DISTRICT


854 So. 2d 674; 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 9413; 28 Fla. L. Weekly D 1475



June 25, 2003, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by Exposito v. State, 869 So. 2d 539, 2004 Fla. LEXIS 232 (Fla., 2004)
Quashed by, in part Exposito v. State, 891 So. 2d 525, 2004 Fla. LEXIS 2407 (Fla., Dec. 23, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An appeal from the Circuit Court of Miami-Dade County, Peter R. Lopez, Judge. LOWER TRIBUNAL CASE NO. 01-7461.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the State's right to appeal a judgment by the Circuit Court of Miami-Dade County (Florida); defendant claimed that the appellate court had no jurisdiction since Fla. Stat. ch. 924.07 (2000) did not authorize an appeal from the reduction of a charge in the indictment.


OVERVIEW: A jury returned a verdict of guilty on a trafficking charge. Defendant claimed that the three-year mandatory minimum sentence was illegal because it was enacted by 1999 Fla. Laws ch. 188, which had been declared unconstitutional by the Second and Fifth Districts. He claimed that the appellate court lacked jurisdiction based on a Fourth District ruling. The Court of Appeal of Florida, Third District, declined to follow the lead of the other appellate districts. It held that an order reducing a charge in the information or indictment was an order dismissing the charge. As Fla. Stat. ch. 924.07 (2000) authorized the State to appeal orders dismissing an indictment or information or any count therein, the appellate court had jurisdiction over the State's appeal under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.670. Conflict was certified.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and remanded.

Miller v. State


Case No. 2D02-2921


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled to trafficking in oxycodone, sale of clonazepam, and possession of clonazepam. He was sentenced to a total of seven years' imprisonment. Also, a $ 100,000 fine was imposed pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 893.135(1)(c)(1)(b) (1997-2001). Defendant appealed the order of the Circuit Court for Pinellas County (Florida), which denied his motion filed pursuant to Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850.

In ground three, defendant alleged that the $ 100,000 fine for trafficking in oxycodone was illegally imposed. The appellate court concluded that the imposition of the fine was mandatory pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 893.135(1)(c)(1)(b) (1997), which was in existence prior to the passage of 1999 Fla. Laws ch. 188.


OUTCOME: The order of the trial court was affirmed.

 

1959 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Budget Rent-A-Car Sys. v. Bennett


CASE NO. 3D01-3174


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, THIRD DISTRICT


847 So. 2d 579; 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 8972; 28 Fla. L. Weekly D 1432



June 18, 2003, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 9, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court for Dade County, Norman Gerstein, Judge. LOWER TRIBUNAL NO. 00-26923.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After an automobile was involved in an accident and four passengers were killed, and one was seriously injured, appellees, a personal representative and others, brought wrongful death actions and an action for personal injury against appellant rental car company as the vicariously liable vehicle owner. The rental car company appealed the order of the Circuit Court for Dade County (Florida), which granted summary final judgment to appellees.


OVERVIEW: The rental car company informed appellees that pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 324.021(9)(b)(2) (1999), which limited the liability of short term lessors for motor vehicles, its maximum liability to appellees was $ 800,000, and offered to tender that amount. However, appellees sought a declaration that Fla. Stat. ch. 324.021(9)(b)(2) was unconstitutional. On appeal, the rental car company argued that the trial court erred in finding that 1999 Fla. Laws ch. 225 violated the single-subject rule of Fla. Const. art. III, § 6, and that Fla. Stat. ch. 324.021(9)(b)(2) itself violated no provision of the Florida Constitution. The appellate court agreed with the rental car company for the reasons set forth by the First District Court of Appeal in another case. In that case, the First District reversed a trial court's determination that 1999 Fla. Laws ch. 225 was unconstitutional, concluding that 1999 Fla. Laws ch. 225 did not violate the single-subject rule. In addition, that court also held that Fla. Stat. ch. 324.021 did not violate a plaintiff's right of access to courts, a plaintiff's right to trial by jury, or the Equal Protection and Due Process Clauses of the Florida Constitution.


OUTCOME: The order of the trial court was reversed and the cause was remanded to the trial court for further proceedings.

Nichols v. State Farm Mut.


CASE NO. 5D01-3851


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


851 So. 2d 742; 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 8794; 28 Fla. L. Weekly D 1404



June 13, 2003, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication August 28, 2003.
Review granted by State Farm Mut. Auto. Ins. Co. v. Nichols, 913 So. 2d 598, 2005 Fla. LEXIS 2281 (Fla., 2005)
Approved by, Certified question answered by State Farm Mut. Auto. Ins. Co. v. Nichols, 932 So. 2d 1067, 2006 Fla. LEXIS 982 (Fla., June 1, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: 9.160 Appeal from the County Court for Orange County, C. Jeffrey Arnold, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED; QUESTION CERTIFIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant insured sought review from an order of the County Court for Orange County (Florida), which assessed attorney's fees and costs against her and in favor of appellee insurer, pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 768.69 (1999). The trial court entered the award after the insured failed to prevail in her claim for damages under the personal injury protection provision (PIP) of her insurance policy.


OVERVIEW: The insured's action alleged that she did not receive payment of medical treatment and expenses arising from injuries she sustained in an automobile accident, for which she had PIP insurance. The insurer had claimed that the insured had unreasonably refused to submit to an independent medical exam. The insured rejected the insurer's proposal of settlement, and after trial the jury rendered a verdict of no liability for the insurer. The trial court awarded costs and fees to the insurer pursuant to ch. 769.79(1). The insured contended that ch. 768.79 did not apply to PIP claims, or alternatively, that the settlement proposal was not valid. The trial court rejected the insured's arguments but certified the question as to whether the insurer could recover attorney's fees under ch. 768.79 and Fla. R. Civ. P. 1.442 in such an action. The court held that the insurer could recover in that situation, although it certified the question for review to the higher court. However, the court also held that the settlement proposal in the instant case was not valid because the release was either overly broad or ambiguous, and accordingly the trial court's award of damages was erroneous.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order awarding costs and fees, and certified the same question to the higher court for review.

Barnum v. State


CASE NO. 1D01-4759


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


849 So. 2d 371; 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 8233; 28 Fla. L. Weekly D 1314



June 2, 2003, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Amended. Released for Publication July 31, 2003.
Quashed by State v. Barnum, 921 So. 2d 513, 2005 Fla. LEXIS 1780 (Fla., Sept. 22, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from the Circuit Court for Leon County. Janet E. Ferris, Judge.
Barnum v. State, 662 So. 2d 968, 1995 Fla. App. LEXIS 10466 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., 1995)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, convicted in the Circuit Court for Leon County (Florida) of attempted first-degree murder of a law-enforcement officer in violation of Fla. Stat. ch. 782.04(1)(a)(1), 777.04(1), and 784.07(3) (1991), challenged the denial of his motion filed pursuant to Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850, wherein he claimed that a supreme court decision, Thompson v. State, should be retroactively applied to reverse his judgment and sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant asserted fundamental error on appeal, because the State failed to prove as an essential element that he knew the victim was a law-enforcement officer. After considering case precedent in Florida, the appellate court found Moreland v. State controlling. If the trial court certified conflict with Grinage v. State in defendant's direct appeal, the supreme court could have considered his case, decided it in the manner it did Thompson, which held that knowledge of the victim's status as a law-enforcement officer was a necessary element of the offense, and remanded for a new trial. The appellate court therefore reversed, and certified conflict with Sweeney v. State, wherein the Fourth District refused to apply Thompson retroactively. The appellate court was unable to reconcile Thompson with either supreme court decisions that "clarified" statutory law or decisions that "changed" the law. The court certified the following question as one of great public importance: "whether the analysis of State v. Klayman applies when an issue that the supreme court has clarified requires resolution of a disputed factual matter?"


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and remanded for either a new trial or entry of a conviction for the lesser-included offense of attempted murder and resentencing.

 

1965 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Saidi v. State


Case No. 5D02-2029


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


845 So. 2d 1022; 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 7988; 28 Fla. L. Weekly D 1309



May 30, 2003, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication June 18, 2003.
Review denied by Saidi v. State, 854 So. 2d 660, 2003 Fla. LEXIS 1465 (Fla., 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Seminole County, Alan A. Dickey, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sent various letters and papers to the attorney representing his former wife in a contentious post-judgment family law proceeding, and to the circuit court. Defendant appealed the decision of the Circuit Court for Seminole County (Florida), which convicted him of sending written threats of death or bodily injury in violation of Fla. Stat. ch. 836.10 (2001).


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant argued that Fla. Stat. ch. 836.10 was unconstitutional, as it was vague, overbroad, and infringed on his First Amendment rights. He also argued that the trial court erred in its instructions to the jury and by improperly prohibiting him from filing any pro se pleadings or papers in the future, as a condition of his probation. The appellate court concluded that Fla. Stat. ch. 836.10 was not vague and was not constitutionally infirm because it was overbroad. Because threats to injure or kill were not constitutionally protected, defendant's First Amendment rights were not compromised by laws prohibiting such threats. In addition, the appellate court concluded that the trial court properly instructed the jury as to the elements of the charged crime. Finally, the prohibition against pro se filings as a special condition of probation did not constitute error, fundamental or otherwise. Admittedly, the condition of probation banning pro se filings burdened defendant's constitutional right to access to the courts under Fla. Const. art. I, § 21. However, the record supported the imposition of this condition of probation considering defendant's crime and past conduct.


OUTCOME: The decision of the trial court was affirmed.

 

1966 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Battles v. State


CASE NO. 2D03-27


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


846 So. 2d 1191; 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 7899; 28 Fla. L. Weekly D 1296



May 28, 2003, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication June 19, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal pursuant to Fla. R. App. P. 9.141(b)(2) from the Circuit Court for Pinellas County; Richard A. Luce, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the decision of the Circuit Court for Pinellas County (Florida), which denied his motion to correct illegal sentence filed pursuant to Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.800(a).


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that his habitual violent felony offender minimum mandatory sentence was illegal because of Taylor v. State, which held 1999 Fla. Laws ch. 188 unconstitutional in violation of the single subject rule. In Green v. State, the appellate court had previously held that the legislature's retroactive reenactment of 1999 Fla. Laws ch. 188 was invalid. Therefore, defendant would be entitled to relief under Taylor if his sentence was affected by the amendments in 1999 Fla. Laws ch. 188. However, the minimum mandatory sentencing provisions for habitual violent felony offenders were already present in Fla. Stat. ch. 775.084 when the legislature adopted 1999 Fla. Laws ch. 188, and they were not affected by the amendments in 1999 Fla. Laws ch. 188. Thus, defendant was not entitled to relief on this basis.


OUTCOME: The decision of the trial court was affirmed without prejudice to any right defendant might have to file a facially sufficient motion.

 

1967 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Price v. City of Boynton Beach


CASE NO. 4D02-2656


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


847 So. 2d 1051; 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 7957; 28 Fla. L. Weekly D 1286



May 28, 2003, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
Rehearing denied by Price v. Boynton Beach, 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 10730 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., July 3, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal of a non-final order from the Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County; Stephen A. Rapp, Judge; L.T. Case No. CA 02-5291 AN.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employee appealed the non-final order of the Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County (Florida), which granted appellee city's motion for temporary injunction for protection against repeat violence which alleged that the employee had made verbal threats against city employees.


OVERVIEW: The trial court quoted in the injunction from the deposition of a psychiatrist, which had been taken in the employee's workers' compensation case, in which the psychiatrist testified that the employee had made threats, talked about his guns, and was a danger. The employee objected on the ground of hearsay, but the trial court ruled that it would be admissible simply because it was a deposition of an expert. The appellate court concluded that the trial court's ruling was improper because the deposition was taken in a proceeding involving different issues. It did not meet the requirements of the hearsay exception for former testimony found in Fla. Stat. ch. 90.803(22). In addition, the trial court also erred in admitting a letter written by the employee's workers' compensation counsel, on the ground that the counsel was his agent. There was no showing that the harmful statement made by counsel was within the scope of her agency.


OUTCOME: The temporary injunction was reversed.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment by the Circuit Court for Brevard County (Florida) that summarily denied his Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.800(a) motion to correct his sentence; defendant claimed, inter alia, that his scoresheet contained errors.


OVERVIEW: After defendant was convicted of armed burglary of a dwelling, sexual battery, robbery, and aggravated battery, he was classified as a habitual offender. Liggett Group Inc. v. Engle


CASE NOS: 3D00-3400, 3D00-3206, 3D00-3207, 3D00-3208, 3D00-3210, 3D00-3212, 3D00-3215


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, THIRD DISTRICT


853 So. 2d 434; 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 7500; CCH Prod. Liab. Rep. P16,629; 28 Fla. L. Weekly D 1219



May 21, 2003, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication September 22, 2003.  [**1]
Rehearing, en banc, denied by Liggett Group, Inc. v. Engle, 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 14774 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 3d Dist., Sept. 22, 2003)
Review granted by Engle v. Liggett Group, Inc., 873 So. 2d 1222, 2004 Fla. LEXIS 807 (Fla., 2004)
Approved by, in part, Reversed by, Remanded by, in part Engle v. Liggett Group, Inc., 2006 Fla. LEXIS 1480 (Fla., July 6, 2006)
Approved by, in part, Quashed by, in part, Remanded by Engle v. Liggett Group, 2006 Fla. LEXIS 2952 (Fla., Dec. 21, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court for Miami-Dade County, Robert P. Kaye, Judge. LOWER TRIBUNAL NO. 94-8273.
R. J. Reynolds Tobacco Co. v. Engle, 750 So. 2d 781, 2000 Fla. App. LEXIS 1716 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 3d Dist., 2000)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with instructions to decertify the class.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, various entities comprising cigarette companies and industry organizations, appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Miami-Dade County (Florida), which awarded compensatory damages to three individual plaintiffs in their class action lawsuit on behalf of smokers and their survivors, and also awarded $ 145 billion in punitive damages to the entire class, wherein damages had been sought for injuries caused by smoking.


OVERVIEW: The individuals' class action was based on assorted injuries caused by smoking and a variety of tort and breach of warranty claims were alleged. The class was certified to include Florida smokers and their survivors who suffered an injury or death due to cigarette addiction. The jury rendered a verdict for the class on liability and punitive damage entitlement, and determined damage amounts for the individual class representatives and for the class. Defendants filed post-verdict motions seeking, inter alia, remittitur and decertification. The trial court entered an omnibus order which required payment of the judgments by defendants and a reservation of jurisdiction for further individual hearings. Defendants appealed and the court held that decertification of the class should have been granted due to the multitudinous individual issues, including choice-of-law, liability, reliance, affirmative defenses, damages, and medical causation. The court also found that the punitive damages required reversal because there was no prior determination of liability and compensatory damages, it was based on jury nullification, it was excessive, and it was precluded by res judicata.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded the matter with instructions that the class be decertified.

Barber v. State


CASE NO. 2D02-4986


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


849 So. 2d 361; 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 7008; 28 Fla. L. Weekly D 1173



May 14, 2003, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication April 6, 2005. Reversed by, Remanded by State v. Henderson, 894 So. 2d 266, 2005 Fla. LEXIS 266 (Fla., Feb. 17, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal pursuant to Fla. R. App. P. 9.141(b)(2) from the Circuit Court for Pinellas County; Philip J. Federico, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Pinellas County, Florida, denied defendant's motion for post-conviction relief, filed pursuant to Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.800(a). Defendant appealed, pursuant to Fla. R. App. P. 9.141(b)(2).


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged the judgment denying her post-conviction relief. In her motion, she alleged that the three-year mandatory minimum term of imprisonment imposed by the trial court, pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 893.135(1)(c)(1)(a) (2000), was illegal based on the case of Taylor v. State. In the Taylor case, the Florida Court of Appeals held that the imposition of mandatory minimum prison sentences for certain drug offenses was unconstitutional, as it violated the single subject rule of the Florida Constitution. However, in Green v. State, re-enactment of the sentencing provisions of 1999 Fla. Laws. ch. 188 could not have been applied retroactively. The instant court held that defendant, through her allegations that she committed the offense of trafficking in hydromorphone within the window under Taylor, presented a facially sufficient claim. On remand, if she was correct in her assertions, the trial court was to resentence her under the 1997 version of Fla. Stat. ch. 893.135(1)(c)(1)(a). The appeals court also certified conflict with the Fourth and Fifth District cases with which it disagreed with in Green v. State.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, and the case was remanded.

 

1972 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Baron v. Rhett


CASE NO. 4D02-3475


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


847 So. 2d 1032; 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 7055; 28 Fla. L. Weekly D 1205



May 14, 2003, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
Rehearing denied by Baron v. Rhett, 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 10731 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., July 7, 2003)
Review denied by Baron v. Rhett, 2005 Fla. LEXIS 319 (Fla., Feb. 10, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County; Robert Lance Andrews, Judge; L.T. Case No. 02-3031 CACE 09.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant tax sale purchasers appealed from the entry of summary judgment by the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County (Florida), for appellee property owner in the owner's suit seeking cancellation of a tax sale, to quiet title to property, and from the denial of the purchaser's motion for summary judgment in their counterclaim to quiet title.


OVERVIEW: The owner took title to the property from the grantor, who failed to pay the property taxes, by a quitclaim deed. The deed was recorded, although it was not signed by the grantor. Before the deed was corrected, the purchasers bought the property at a tax sale. The clerk waited approximately five months before noticing and setting the tax deed sale; during the time lapse, the name on the tax assessment roll changed. The appellate court held that Florida's scheme for enforcement of property taxes was designed to afford due process to interested persons. The appellate court, in conflict with Delta Property Management v. Profile Investments, Inc., 830 So. 2d 867 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2002), held that the owner had a "reasonably ascertainable" interest of record and was entitled to notice of a tax sale, as the property had been assessed to him. When the clerk failed to schedule a tax sale and mail notice thereof within a reasonable time after the filing of an application for a tax deed, and a new tax roll assessment intervened during such period of delay, the clerk had to obtain an updated statement from the tax collector for notification purposes.


OUTCOME: The conflict was certified. The judgment was affirmed.

1975 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Brazill v. State


CASE NO. 4D01-3244


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


845 So. 2d 282; 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 7069; 28 Fla. L. Weekly D 1187



May 14, 2003, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Brazill v. State, 876 So. 2d 561, 2004 Fla. LEXIS 924 (Fla., 2004)
Post-conviction proceeding at, Remanded by Brazill v. State, 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 15188 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., Sept. 13, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County; Richard I. Wennet, Judge; L.T. Case No. 00-6385CFA02.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, who was 13 at the time of the crime, but was tried as an adult, appealed his conviction by the Circuit Court, Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County (Florida), for second-degree murder and aggravated assault with a firearm. He was sentenced to concurrent sentences: a mandatory minimum sentence of 28 years in prison on the murder charge and 5 years in prison, with a 3 year mandatory minimum, on the assault charge.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and another student were suspended as the result of a water balloon fight. Taking a gun from his bedroom, defendant rode his bike back to school and asked a teacher to let 2 girls leave the class to talk to him. The teacher refused, and defendant shot him in the head. The appellate court held defendant was afforded the same procedural rights as anyone else charged with first-degree murder by indictment. Children 13 and under could be prosecuted in adult court only by indictment. The involuntary waiver provisions of Fla. Stat. ch. 985.226(2) (1999) did not apply. Fla. Stat. ch. 985.225, which allowed defendant to be tried as an adult, was constitutional. The prosecutor's closing argument did not reach the critical mass of fundamental error. The most serious prosecutorial lapse was making comments designed to evoke sympathy for the victim. There was abundant evidence to support a conviction of first-degree murder, let alone second-degree murder. The 28-year mandatory minimum sentence was lawful. The jury's verdict was sufficient to support the mandatory minimum sentence.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

1977 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Karo v. State


CASE NO. 2D02-3324


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


849 So. 2d 351; 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 6214; 28 Fla. L. Weekly D 1104



May 2, 2003, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication April 6, 2005. Reversed by, Remanded by State v. Henderson, 894 So. 2d 266, 2005 Fla. LEXIS 266 (Fla., Feb. 17, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal pursuant to Fla. R. App. P. 9.141(b)(2) from the Circuit Court for Hillsborough County; William Fuente, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Hillsborough County (Florida) entered a judgment that denied defendant's Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.800(a) motion to challenge the legality of his seven-year and 15-year mandatory minimum sentences imposed after he entered guilty pleas in separate drug trafficking cases. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled guilty to trafficking in cocaine. The trial court then imposed a seven-year mandatory minimum term of imprisonment pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 893.135(1)(b)(1)(b) (1999-2000). He also pled guilty in another trial court case to trafficking in even more cocaine. The trial court imposed a 15-year mandatory minimum term of imprisonment pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 893.135(1)(b)(1)(c) on that offense. After judgments of conviction were entered, defendant filed a Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.800(a) motion alleging the sentences were illegal based on a ruling that imposition of mandatory minimum prison sentences for certain drug offenses was unconstitutional because the law permitting them violated the Florida Constitution. The trial court denied the motion and found the legislature had cured the defect, reenacted the law, and that reenactment was retroactive to a certain date. After defendant appealed, the appellate court found that retroactive application as to his seven-year mandatory minimum sentence might violate the Ex Post Facto Clauses of the United States and Florida Constitutions, although the same was not true with regard to his 15-year mandatory minimum sentence.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed to the extent that if denied defendant's motion for correction, modification, or reduction of 15-year mandatory minimum sentence. However, its judgment denying that motion as to his seven-year mandatory minimum sentence was reversed and the cause was remanded for further consideration of his seven-year mandatory minimum sentence.

Stay vacated by Milks v. State, 881 So. 2d 1113, 2004 Fla. LEXIS 1332 (Fla., 2004)
Approved by Milks v. State, 894 So. 2d 924, 2005 Fla. LEXIS 150 (Fla., Feb. 3, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Pasco County; Maynard F. Swanson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order by the Circuit Court for Pasco County (Florida) that designated him a sexual predator under the Florida Sexual Predators Act, Fla. Stat. ch. 775 (2000); defendant claimed that the Act violated constitutional principles of separation of powers and procedural due process.


OVERVIEW: Four months after defendant entered a no contest plea to a charge of lewd and lascivious molestation, he was designated a sexual predator pursuant to ch. 775.21. OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.

Miller v. State


CASE NO. 2D02-2921


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 6161; 28 Fla. L. Weekly D 1097



April 30, 2003, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:

 [*1] THIS OPINION WAS WITHDRAWN BY THE COURT.

NOT FINAL UNTIL TIME EXPIRES TO FILE REHEARING MOTION AND, IF FILED, DETERMINED.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing granted by, Opinion withdrawn by, Substituted opinion at Miller v. State, 848 So. 2d 401, 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 9420 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2d Dist., June 25, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal pursuant to Fla. R. App. P. 9.141(b)(2) from the Circuit Court for Pinellas County; Philip J. Federico, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Pinellas County, Florida, denied defendant's motion for post-conviction relief, filed pursuant Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged the judgment entered. The appeals court upheld the trial court's decision. As to the third ground, the appeals court agreed that defendant failed to present a facially sufficient claim. In his motion, he alleged that he received a total of seven years' imprisonment with a three-year mandatory minimum for the charge of trafficking in a prescription drug. In ground two, he alleged that counsel was ineffective for failing to move to dismiss the charge of possession of another drug after he informed his trial counsel that he had a prescription. The facts supporting his claim were contained in the memorandum of law attached to the motion. However, the memorandum was not properly sworn to, and thus unworthy of consideration. Further, defendant failed to affirmatively allege that he committed the offense on a date within the Taylor window. Finally, the court affirmed that portion of the trial court's order denying ground three, because the mandatory fine was not part of his plea bargain. Defendant did not seek to withdraw his plea on this basis, and the fine was mandatory, pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 893.135(1)(c)(1)(b) (1997-2001).


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

S.C. v. Guardian Ad Litem


CASE NO. 4D02-3414


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


845 So. 2d 953; 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 6176; 28 Fla. L. Weekly D 1057



April 30, 2003, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
Rehearing denied by S.C. v. Guardian Ad Litem, 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 9134 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., June 6, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Petition for writ of certiorari to the Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County; Karen L. Martin, Judge; L.T. Case No. CJ 02 DP 300133 JL.



DISPOSITION: Certiorari granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action seeking an order adjudicating petitioner minor as dependent, the minor objected to release of records created by her therapist, a psychologist, to the Florida Department of Children and Families and to respondent guardian ad litem. The Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County (Florida), ruled that the Department could have limited access, but did not restrict the guardian's access. The minor appealed.


OVERVIEW: The Department filed an action against a 14-year-old minor's parents, seeking an order allowing it to place their daughter in a shelter, and the trial court appointed a guardian ad litem to represent the minor. The Department and the guardian sought access to records which a psychologist created when the minor was in therapy, but the minor opposed release. The trial court reviewed the records in camera and gave the Department access to statements the minor's parents made to the psychologist, but the court's order did not restrict access by the guardian. The trial court also ruled that the psychologist could testify on a limited basis. In the minor's appeal from the trial court's rulings, the appellate court held that (1) it would review the trial court's orders as if a petition for a writ of certiorari was filed challenging the denial of a protective order; (2) the minor had the right to assert the psychotherapist/patient privilege; and (3) because the minor made a prima facie showing that she would be harmed by release of the records, the appellate court would quash the trial court's order allowing her guardian unrestricted access.


OUTCOME: The appellate court treated the minor's appeal as a petition for certiorari, granted the petition, and quashed the trial court's order allowing the guardian ad litem unrestricted access to the records created by the minor's psychologist because the trial court issued its order without hearing the minor's objections.

Diaz v. State


CASE NO. 5D03-840


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


846 So. 2d 1158; 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 5830; 28 Fla. L. Weekly D 1053



April 25, 2003, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
Rehearing denied by Diaz v. State, 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 10464 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 5th Dist., June 9, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: 3.850 Appeal from the Circuit Court for Orange County, Richard F. Conrad, Judge.
Diaz v. State, 818 So. 2d 521, 2002 Fla. App. LEXIS 8104 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 5th Dist., 2002)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment by the Circuit Court for Orange County (Florida) that summarily denied his Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850 motion for postconviction relief; defendant claimed that because a 1999 revision of Fla. Stat. ch. 893.135 was determined to be unconstitutional, his sentence was illegal.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pleaded guilty to trafficking in heroin in violation of Fla. Stat. ch. 893.135(1)(c)1.c (1999), and was sentenced to the statutorily mandated 25-year minimum prison term. The appellate court held that defendant was not entitled to relief under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850. Although the 1999 revision to Fla. Stat. ch. 893.135 had been declared unconstitutional, 2002 Fla. Laws ch. 210 corrected the error and was retroactive. In any event, defendant was not adversely affected by the 1999 amendment because under the 1998 version of Fla. Stat. ch. 893.135, his mandatory minimum sentence would have been the same.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Herndon v. State


CASE NO. 2D02-3204


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


842 So. 2d 1026; 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 5662; 28 Fla. L. Weekly D 1030



April 23, 2003, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
Released for Publication April 6, 2005. Reversed by, Remanded by State v. Henderson, 894 So. 2d 266, 2005 Fla. LEXIS 266 (Fla., Feb. 17, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal pursuant to Fla. R. App. P. 9.141(b)(2) from the Circuit Court for Polk County; Ralph Artigliere, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Polk County, Florida, dismissed defendant's Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.800(a) motion for post-conviction relief. Defendant appealed, pursuant to Fla. R. App. P. 9.141(b)(2).


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged the judgment entered against her. In her motion, she alleged that she pleaded to trafficking in methamphetamine and that the seven-year mandatory minimum term of imprisonment imposed by the trial court was illegal based on the case of Taylor v. State. In that case, the instant court held that the imposition of mandatory minimum prison sentences for certain drug offenses was unconstitutional, as it violated the single subject rule of the Florida Constitution. However, in Green v. State, re-enactment of the sentencing provisions of 1999 Fla. Laws. ch. 188 could not have been applied retroactively. The instant court held that defendant, through her allegations that she committed the offense of trafficking in methamphetamine within the window under Taylor, presented a facially sufficient claim. On remand, if she was correct in her assertions, the trial court was to resentence her under the 1997 version of 1999 Florida Laws ch. 188. The appeals court also certified conflict with the Fourth and Fifth District cases with which it disagreed with in Green v. State.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, and the case was remanded.

 

1989 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


G.P. v. State


CASE NO. 4D02-3410


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


842 So. 2d 1059; 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 5743; 28 Fla. L. Weekly D 1008



April 23, 2003, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 9, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County; Peter D. Blanc, Judge; L.T. Case Nos. CD02-70 FY; CD02-1880 FZ; and CD02-3071 FY.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, women who consented to allow private adoption of their children, sought review from an order of the Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County (Florida), which held in a declaratory judgment action that Fla. Stat. chs. 63.087, 63.088(5) (2002) were not unconstitutional as they related to private adoptions under the Florida Adoption Act.


OVERVIEW: Each of the four appellants sought to allow a private adoption of their child but the identity of the father was not known and accordingly, constructive notice was required under Fla. Stat. chs. 63.087, 63.088(5). Appellants contended that their rights to privacy pursuant to U.S. Const. amend. 14 and Fla. Const. art. I, § 23 were violated. However, the trial court found that the law was constitutional due to the State's compelling interest, and that no less intrusive means was shown to achieve the same interest. However, the trial court held the law unconstitutional with respect to women whose pregnancies were the result of a sexual battery. On appeal, the court found that chs. 63.087, 63.088(5) were unconstitutional invasions of the mothers' rights to privacy because they substantially interfered with both a woman's independence in choosing adoption as an alternative to giving birth and with the right not to disclose the intimate personal information that was required when the father was unknown. The State failed in its burden of proof as to a showing of a sufficiently compelling interest for such an invasion.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the trial court and remanded the matter for further proceedings.

 

1990 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


State v. Richards


CASE NO. 3D02-572


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, THIRD DISTRICT


843 So. 2d 962; 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 6043; 28 Fla. L. Weekly D 1043



April 23, 2003, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Richards v. State, 851 So. 2d 729, 2003 Fla. LEXIS 1329 (Fla., July 14, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] A Writ of Certiorari to the Circuit Court for Dade County, Roberto M. Pineiro, Judge. LOWER TRIBUNAL NO. 00-35987.
State v. Richards, 2002 Fla. App. LEXIS 11423 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 3d Dist., Aug. 7, 2002)



DISPOSITION: Petition granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant moved for rehearing in the State's petition for a writ of certiorari to the Circuit Court for Dade County (Florida), seeking to quash an order limiting the State's ability to impeach a State witness, after the trial court denied defendant's motion to suppress, but granted defendant's motion under Morton.


OVERVIEW: The witness recanted the part of her statement where she said that defendant called her and admitted shooting the victim. The State's highest court held that since there was a legitimate purpose for calling the witness, the State, as the party calling the witness, could impeach her with a prior inconsistent statement. The State could not, however, offer the witness's original statement through a detective that defendant admitted the shooting as a statement by the witness of identification of a person made after perceiving the person under Fla. Stat. ch. 90.801(2)(c) (2001). The substance of defendant's statement went beyond being a statement of identification for purposes of ch. 90.801(2)(c). The exercise of certiorari jurisdiction was appropriate, as the trial court order was at odds with Morton and represented a departure from the essential requirements of law. Further, the excluded matter was important evidence that, if not presented at trial, might significantly impair the State's prosecution of defendant. Finally, since the State had no appellate remedy if there was an acquittal of defendant, the State did not have an adequate remedy by way of appeal.


OUTCOME: The petition for a writ of certiorari was granted. Defendant's motion for rehearing was denied.

1992 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Four Jay's Constr., Inc. v. Marina at the Bluffs Condo. Ass'n


CASE NO. 4D01-4348


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


846 So. 2d 555; 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 5626; 28 Fla. L. Weekly D 951



April 16, 2003, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication June 11, 2003.
Rehearing denied by Four Jays v. Marina, 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 9728 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., June 11, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County; Thomas H. Barkdull, III, Judge; L.T. Case No. CL-01-00034-AJ.



DISPOSITION: Question certified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant contractor appealed from the dismissal of its amended complaint against a homeowners' association, as agent for, and as class representative of, the condominium unit owners by the Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County (Florida).


OVERVIEW: The contractor contended that the association was a proper class representative under Fla. R. Civ. P. 1.221. The appellate court held that the suit against the homeowners' association, as the representative of the class of unit owners, was proper as the controversy was of common interest to all units. The appellate court distinguished cases holding that the unit owners could not be individually joined as defendants under Fla. Stat. ch. 718.119, as the action was not against the owners, but against the association as the representative of the class of units sharing the undivided ownership of the common elements. The contractor did not seek individual money judgments against the owners. To the extent that the complaint might be interpreted by the trial court as seeking a money judgment against the individual unit owners, leave to amend was to be granted. The appellate court certified the question as to the ability of a plaintiff to sue a class of condominium unit owners as a class represented by the homeowners' association in controversies concerning matters of common interest under Fla. R. Civ. P. 1.221 and Fla. Stat. ch. 718.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed. A question was certified.

 

1993 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Keinz v. State


Case No. 2D01-2969


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 5428; 28 Fla. L. Weekly D 977



April 16, 2003, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:

 [*1] NOT FINAL UNTIL TIME EXPIRES TO FILE REHEARING MOTION AND, IF FILED, DETERMINED

THIS OPINION WAS WITHDRAWN BY THE COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Opinion withdrawn by, Motion granted by, in part, Motion denied by, in part Keinz v. State, 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 10357 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2d Dist., July 11, 2003)
Substituted opinion at, Remanded by Keinz v. State, 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 10356 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2d Dist., July 11, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Lee County; Thomas S. Reese, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled no contest to trafficking in more than 400 grams of cocaine, trafficking in four grams or more of heroin, and trafficking in 28 grams or more of cocaine. Defendant challenged the denial by the Circuit Court for Lee County (Florida) of his Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.800(b) motion in which he claimed that the three-year minimum mandatory terms imposed for trafficking in heroin and trafficking in 28 grams or more of cocaine were illegal.


OVERVIEW: In support of his argument, defendant cited to Taylor, which found that 1999 Fla. Laws. ch. 188, providing for the imposition of minimum mandatory sentences was unconstitutional. In response, the State argued that the trial court did not err when it imposed the minimum mandatory sentences because before the Taylor opinion became final, the legislature reenacted the minimum mandatory terms for drug trafficking and provided for retroactive application of the statute. However, the appellate court had recently rejected the State's argument in Green.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirm the convictions; affirmed the sentence for trafficking in 400 grams or more of cocaine; reversed the sentences for trafficking in four grams or more of heroin and trafficking in 28 grams or more of cocaine; and remanded for resentencing on those two convictions in accordance with the valid laws in effect on the date of the offenses, December 14, 1999.

1995 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Clayton v. State


Case No. 5D01-3213


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


842 So. 2d 971; 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 4905; 28 Fla. L. Weekly D 921



April 11, 2003, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 30, 2003.
Reversed by Hersey v. State, 908 So. 2d 1052, 2005 Fla. LEXIS 727 (Fla., Apr. 21, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Brevard County, J. Preston Silvernail, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED, QUESTION CERTIFIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Brevard County (Florida), which entered a conviction against him for robbery with a firearm and designated him as a prison releasee reoffender.


OVERVIEW: The trial record indicated that defendant had committed the robbery while using a type of revolver designed to fire a type of bullet that was not commercially available. However, the bullets could be made by someone skilled in hand loading ammunition. An expert at trial indicated that the weapon would fire if loaded with the proper ammunition, although the expert was unable to determine the precise make, model, or serial number of the weapon. Defendant was convicted and appealed. The court initially held that the evidence was sufficient to prove that he possessed a firearm because the weapon that defendant had fit within the definition of "firearm" contained in Fla. Stat. ch. 790.001(6) (2000). The court also held that 2002 Fla. Laws ch. 210 applied retroactively and cured the unconstitutionality of the prison releasee reoffender status law of 1999 Fla. Laws ch. 1888. However, the court acknowledged that its opinion conflicted with another on the same issue and certified the question as to retroactive application.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court. However, the court also certified a question as to the ability to apply a statute allowing for classification as a prison releasee reoffender retroactively.

 

1996 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Oliver v. State


CASE NO. 5D01-3510


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


842 So. 2d 259; 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 4918; 28 Fla. L. Weekly D 920



April 11, 2003, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 30, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Orange County, Stan Strickland, Judge.
Oliver v. State, 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 2423 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 5th Dist., Feb. 28, 2003)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED in part; REVERSED in part; Question CERTIFIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Orange County, Florida, convicted defendant of robbery, battery, and petit theft, and sentenced him thereon. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged his convictions, first arguing that he should be re-sentenced on the robbery charge because the habitual violent offender statute was unconstitutional. However, the appeals court certified the question of whether the curative statute passed in 2002 should have been applied retroactively to the offenses defendant committed in 2000. Defendant next argued that double jeopardy barred his dual convictions for petit theft and robbery. The appeals court agreed. It was clear from the information and proofs offered at trial that the robbery and petit theft charges were based on the taking of the cash drawer containing cash from the clerk during the same incident. Herein, there was no separation of anything: not time, object, place, or circumstances.


OUTCOME: The robbery sentence was affirmed, but the petit theft conviction and sentence were reversed, and a question was certified as to whether the curative statute should have been applied retroactively to the offenses defendant committed. In all other respects, the judgment was affirmed.

1998 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Fla. Dep't of Ins. v. Amador


CASE NO. 3D02-2905


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, THIRD DISTRICT


841 So. 2d 612; 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 4417; 28 Fla. L. Weekly D 864



April 2, 2003, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 21, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from a non-final order from the Circuit Court for Miami-Dade County, Barbara S. Levenson. LOWER TRIBUNAL NO. 02-18371.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee, a former state employee, sued appellant, the Florida Department of Insurance, claiming that the Department's withdrawal of legal representation constituted a breach of contract. The Department moved to dismiss the case due to improper venue pursuant to the "home venue privilege." The Department appealed the non-final order of the Circuit Court for Miami-Dade County (Florida), which denied its motion to dismiss due to improper venue.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the Department argued that the trial judge erred in refusing to dismiss the case because under Florida's home venue privilege, the proper venue would be Leon County where the Department's principle headquarters was located. The employee argued that valid exceptions to the home venue privilege applied. The appellate court concluded that the joint tortfeasor exception did not apply because the Department was not sued as a joint tortfeasor. The case was a simple breach of contract claim by the employee against the Department. In addition, the employee could not characterize his breach of contract claim against the Department as an unconstitutional taking of a property interest so as to invoke the sword wielder doctrine. There was no constitutional right in Florida to have one's attorney's fees paid; thus, no constitutionally guaranteed right or property interest was infringed upon. Furthermore, the employee was not entitled by statute to have his fees paid under Fla. Stat. ch. 111.07, as individual application of ch. 111.07 was to be decided by the respective governmental unit (i.e. the Department), not the judiciary.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the order of the trial court, which denied the motion to dismiss. The case was remanded with directions that the trial court transfer the case to Leon County, Florida.

 

1999 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Powell v. State


CASE NO. 2D02-3133


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


841 So. 2d 580; 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 4045; 28 Fla. L. Weekly D 827



March 26, 2003, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication April 24, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal pursuant to Fla. R. App. P. 9.141(b)(2) from the Circuit Court for Pasco County; Wayne L. Cobb, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the decision of the Circuit Court for Pasco County (Florida), which denied his motion to correct illegal sentence filed pursuant to Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.800(a).


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant argued that his sentence as a prison releasee reoffender was illegal based on Taylor, which held that 1999 Fla. Laws ch. 188 was unconstitutional because it was enacted in violation of the single subject rule. However, since defendant had not alleged that he was affected by the amendments to the prison releasee reoffender statute, the appellate court concluded that his claim was facially insufficient. Defendant also argued that his sentence violated double jeopardy because the enhancement of his sentence contained two punishments for one criminal episode. However, defendant did not explain the enhancement or the two punishments to which he referred nor did he allege that his entitlement to relief could be determined from the face of the record. Therefore, the appellate court concluded that this claim was also facially insufficient.


OUTCOME: The decision of the trial court was affirmed.
